201 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rivera


Docket No. 98609.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2006 Ill. LEXIS 628



May 18, 2006, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion replaced by, Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Rivera, 221 Ill. 2d 481, 852 N.E.2d 771, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1094, 304 Ill. Dec. 315 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Rivera, 348 Ill. App. 3d 168, 810 N.E.2d 129, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 456, 284 Ill. Dec. 476 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of two counts of first degree murder following a jury trial. The appellate court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The supreme court granted his petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The trial court made a sua sponte Batson challenge to defense counsel's peremptory strike of an African-American juror. The supreme court saw no clear indication of a prima facie case of racial discrimination. The only factor that appeared to weigh in favor of a prima facie case was the fact that defendant was Hispanic and both the victim and the potential juror were African-American. No other considerations supported the trial court's apparent belief that a prima facie case existed. The record did not reveal a prima facie case of racial discrimination, if indeed that, as opposed to race-gender discrimination, was the basis for the sua sponte action. A trial court could raise a Batson issue sua sponte, but it could do so only when a prima facie case of discrimination was abundantly clear. Moreover, the trial court had to make an adequate record consisting of all relevant facts, factual findings, and articulated bases for both its finding of a prima facie case and for its ultimate determination at the third stage of the Batson procedure. The record was insufficient to demonstrate either a prima facie case of racial discrimination or the bases for the trial court's rulings.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the circuit court for a hearing on the existence of a prima facie case of discrimination. At that hearing, any omitted evidence pertinent to that question could be included in the record. The circuit court was to articulate proper findings of fact and conclusions of law with respect to the threshold question of a prima facie case of discrimination and specify what kind of discrimination it believed was at issue.

 

202 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rivera


Docket No. 98609.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


221 Ill. 2d 481; 852 N.E.2d 771; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1094; 304 Ill. Dec. 315



May 18, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified Upon Denial of Rehearing June 29, 2006.
Appeal after remand at People v. Rivera, 227 Ill. 2d 1, 879 N.E.2d 876, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1705, 316 Ill. Dec. 488 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Rivera, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 628 (Ill., May 18, 2006)
People v. Rivera, 348 Ill. App. 3d 168, 810 N.E.2d 129, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 456, 284 Ill. Dec. 476 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of two counts of first degree murder and was subsequently sentenced to 85 years' incarceration. The appellate panel (Illinois) affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The supreme court granted his petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The issue was the trial court's sua sponte Batson challenge to defense counsel's peremptory strike of a female African-American juror. The supreme court found that the record in its current state did not reveal a prima facie case of racial discrimination, if indeed that-as opposed to race-gender discrimination-was the basis for the trial court's sua sponte action. The supreme court held that a trial court could raise a Batson issue sua sponte, but it could do so only when a prima facie case of discrimination was abundantly clear. Moreover, the trial court had to make an adequate record consisting of all relevant facts, factual findings, and articulated bases for both its finding of a prima facie case and for its ultimate determination of discrimination at the third stage of the Batson procedure. The record in the instant case was insufficient to demonstrate either a prima facie case of racial discrimination or the bases for the trial court's rulings. There could be evidence that was not made a part of the record because the trial court believed that the preliminary matter of a prima facie case would become moot after it ruled on the third-stage issue.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the circuit court for a limited hearing to allow the trial judge an opportunity to articulate the bases for his Batson rulings, particularly in regard to the threshold question of a prima facie case of discrimination. After proceedings on remand were completed, and any supplemental arguments were considered, the court would announce its judgment on any and all pending issues requiring resolution at that time.

 

203 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Nitz


Docket No. 99712.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


219 Ill. 2d 400; 848 N.E.2d 982; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 611; 302 Ill. Dec. 418



April 20, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Rehearing denied by People v. Nitz, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 638 (Ill., May 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District.
People v. Nitz, 353 Ill. App. 3d 978, 820 N.E.2d 536, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1357, 289 Ill. Dec. 760 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, defendant was convicted of first-degree murder. The trial court sentenced him to life imprisonment pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. 1987, ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a) (codified as amended at 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(b) (2004)). The Illinois appellate court modified his sentence to 60 years. The State appealed. Defendant requested cross-relief.


OVERVIEW: The trial court enhanced the sentence based on its finding that the crime was accompanied by exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty. The court first held that because the finding had not been made by a jury, the sentence violated Apprendi. Applying a plain-error analysis because defendant had not timely objected to the error, the court held that defendant had not proven that the evidence was closely balanced as to whether his crime was exceptionally brutal or heinous and indicative of wanton cruelty. Defendant's cutting off the victim's head after his death indicated brutality in regard to his family, and testimony that defendant struck the victim repeatedly with a baseball bat displayed wanton cruelty. Thus, defendant's procedural default of the Apprendi violation could not be excused. Next, the trial court properly held inadmissible a juror's affidavit in which the juror stated that jurors inappropriately considered defendant's previous trial and his failure to testify. The allegations concerned only the jury's private deliberations and were not of the sort subject to extraneous proof; thus, the affidavit was inadmissible to impeach the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's imposition of a sentence of life imprisonment. It reversed the appellate court's modification of defendant's sentence. It affirmed the decisions of the trial court and the appellate court as they pertained to defendant's request for cross-relief.

 

204 of 2788 DOCUMENTS



Elem. Sch. Dist. 159 v. Schiller


Docket No. 100947


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


221 Ill. 2d 130; 849 N.E.2d 349; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 614; 302 Ill. Dec. 557



April 20, 2006, Opinion Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) found that appellant property owner's petition to detach his parcel of vacant farmland property from appellee school districts in a township and annex it to adjoining school districts associated with a village did not comply with 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-2c (1998). It also found that statute constituted impermissible special legislation. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-2c (1998), the property owner petitioned the state education superintendent to detach his parcel of vacant farmland property from the existing school districts associated with a township and annex it to adjoining school districts associated with the village. The trial court, however, found that the petition did not comply with 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-2c (1998) and additionally found that 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-2c (1998) constituted special legislation in violation of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13. On appeal, the state supreme court found that the property owner's petition to detach vacant farmland property from the township school districts and annex it to the adjoining village school districts did not violate the statute, as the language of the statute dictated that the village to which the property was annexed only had to be in either the elementary or high school district and did not require that village be within both districts. The state supreme court also found that there was no special legislation violation because the law did not exclude any entity from a benefit received by the property owner.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the state education superintendent's order was confirmed.


 

205 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Thompson


Docket No. 97373.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


222 Ill. 2d 1; 853 N.E.2d 378; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 609; 304 Ill. Dec. 589



April 10, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Rehearing denied by People v. Thompson, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1106 (Ill., July 5, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Thompson v. Ill., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 2707 (U.S., Feb. 26, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of, among other crimes, three counts of first degree murder (720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1(a) (2002)) for killing three persons. The Circuit Court of Stark County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to death on each of the first degree murder convictions. Pursuant to Ill. Const. art. VI, § 4(b) (1970), defendant's appeal was brought directly to the supreme court because he was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the sentence was inappropriate because he acted under an extreme mental disturbance at the time of the murders and had no significant prior criminal history. The supreme court disagreed. A psychiatrist testified that defendant did not suffer from any delusional disorder pursuant to the 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1(c)(2) mitigating factor. Rather, defendant suffered from two behavioral disorders, paranoid personality disorder and antisocial personality disorder. His conduct was the culmination of an escalating pattern of violence against citizens in the community, and not the result of a spontaneous reaction. The trial court specifically found that defendant remained a threat to society, and that if given the opportunity, he would continue to be violent. Even if he had established the mitigating circumstance of an extreme mental disturbance, it would not be sufficient to overcome the aggravating circumstances. The Apprendi and Ring rules were not applicable to the second phase of a death penalty proceeding in Illinois because the trier of fact had already found beyond a reasonable doubt the necessary aggravating factor for imposition of the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

206 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Garvin


Doc ket No. 99031.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


219 Ill. 2d 104; 847 N.E.2d 82; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 328; 301 Ill. Dec. 423



March 23, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Garvin v. Illinois, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 7076 (U.S., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
People v. Garvin, 349 Ill. App. 3d 845, 812 N.E.2d 773, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 833, 285 Ill. Dec. 953 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial by Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) of his motion to quash arrest and suppress evidence on charges of burglary and theft. He also challenged the constitutionality of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2002). The latter argument challenged the statute both on its face and as applied in the case under the search and seizure provisions of the federal constitution and the Illinois Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued a lack of probable cause for his arrest because the police had no particularized suspicion that he was involved in the theft of a license plate based on his proximity to a stolen van to which the plate had been attached. He also alleged that the taking of blood for deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) analysis and registration under § 5-4-3 was unconstitutional. The appellate court found a lack of probable cause for defendant's arrest and harmless error in the admission of certain statements. Finding that the evidence presented a sufficient basis for the finding of probable cause, the supreme court affirmed the denial of both the motion to quash and the motion to suppress. The supreme court also held that § 5-4-3 was constitutional as applied to defendant. Thus, it was also facially constitutional. The purpose of the statute was to create a DNA database that could aid in future investigations to absolve innocents and identify the guilty. It was constitutional under both the special needs and the balancing only tests. Further, as a convicted felon, defendant's privacy rights were greatly reduced, and the drawing of blood was considered a minimal intrusion on those rights.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the appellate court's ultimate judgment. It also found the DNA registry statute to be constitutional both facially and as applied to defendant.

 

207 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


O'Brien v. White


Docket No. 102077


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


219 Ill. 2d 86; 846 N.E.2d 116; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 319; 301 Ill. Dec. 154



March 6, 2006, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) granted appellee judges motion for summary judgment on their claim that statutory law dictating that their judicial positions would be come vacant after the upcoming elections due to their late filings of declarations of candidacy to succeed themselves, was unconstitutional. Appellant secretary of state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The judges were elected to their judicial positions. Several years later, each of them was faced with running for retention in the general election. Each of them filed with the secretary of state a declaration of candidacy to succeed himself or herself. In each case, the secretary of state refused to accept the declaration because it was filed late, according to a statute regarding judicial retention, 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7A-1 (2004). The judges then moved for summary judgment and claimed that the statutory provision was unconstitutional due to the time deadline set forth in Ill. Const. art. VI, § 12(d) regarding judicial retention. The trial court granted the motion. On appeal, the state supreme court first addressed whether the statute was mandatory or directory, and found that it was mandatory because it set forth a consequence for a judge's failure to meet the deadline. It then found that the statute was facially unconstitutional because it was directly in conflict with the Ill. Const. art. VI, § 12(d) given that the statute tried to change the time deadline for filing judicial retention declarations in that constitutional provision.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

208 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Perlstein v. Wolk


Docket No. 98909


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


218 Ill. 2d 448; 844 N.E.2d 923; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 315; 300 Ill. Dec. 480



February 17, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court of the Second District.
Perlstein v. Wolk, 349 Ill. App. 3d 161, 810 N.E.2d 598, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 580, 284 Ill. Dec. 808 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and found that application of the void ab initio doctrine would be fundamentally unfair in a case where plaintiff claimants filed a legal malpractice action just three weeks after the state supreme court declared a public act unconstitutional. The public act had shortened the time for filing a legal malpractice action. Defendants, an attorney and a law firm, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimants filed a legal malpractice action against the attorney and law firm. The claimants relied on the limitations period for malpractice actions set forth in a civil procedure statute, as amended by 1995 Ill. Laws 89-7. The attorney and law firm moved to dismiss and claimed that the state supreme court's decision in Best, holding 1995 Ill. Laws 89-7 void in its entirety, rendered their complaint untimely. The trial court, relying on the void ab initio doctrine, agreed and dismissed the complaint with prejudice. The appellate court reversed and held that dismissal would be unfair, as the claimants had filed their complaint within three weeks of the Best decision being filed. On further review, the state supreme court found that by virtue of its Best decision, no time remained for them to file their complaint because it was instantaneously barred when the prior version of the law became operative again; thus, the state supreme court found that the void ab initio doctrine should not be applied and that the three weeks in which the claimants filed their complaint after Best was a reasonable time period for filing their legal malpractice action.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was affirmed, and the case was ordered to be remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

209 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Cassens Transp. Co. v. Indus. Comm'n (Ade)


Docket No. 100183.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


218 Ill. 2d 519; 844 N.E.2d 414; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 317; 300 Ill. Dec. 416



February 17, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
Cassens Transp. Co. v. Ill. Indus. Comm'n (Ade), 354 Ill. App. 3d 807, 821 N.E.2d 1274, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 17, 290 Ill. Dec. 700 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employer challenged a decision from an appellate court in Illinois, which dismissed the employer's appeal in a workers' compensation dispute with appellee former employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee suffered a disability, and he was awarded benefits under 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 305/8(d)(1) (2002). About 10 years later, the employer sought to terminate the award based on the fact that the employee earned too much money. The Illinois Workers' Compensation Commission denied relief, and the decision was confirmed by a circuit court. The employer's subsequent appeal was dismissed, and it again sought review. In affirming the dismissal of the appeal, the state supreme court determined that the Commission lacked jurisdiction to hear the case. The Commission had jurisdiction for this purpose, but only for 30 months following the issuance of the award, pursuant to 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 305/19(h) (2002). The state supreme court determined that the review sought by the employer was not appropriate for partial disability claims, even though they were authorized for claims of totally and permanently disabled persons under 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 305/8(f) (2002). The state supreme court also rejected the argument that due process and rights under Ill. Const. art. I, § 12 were violated. There was no right to a specific form of review, and the employer had already received a hearing.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the appeal was affirmed.

 

210 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Harshman v. DePhillips


Docket No. 99805.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


218 Ill. 2d 482; 844 N.E.2d 941; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 316; 300 Ill. Dec. 498



February 17, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Harshman v. DePhillips, 354 Ill. App. 3d 429, 820 N.E.2d 1164, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1482, 290 Ill. Dec. 97 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court answered a certified question, about whether Illinois law permits a party to bring a contribution claim in a separate proceeding after a court of another jurisdiction has denied the party leave to file the claim in the original proceeding, in the negative and ordered that the case be remanded to the trial court for further proceedings. Plaintiffs, a truck driver, truck owner, and truck lessee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The truck driver's vehicle was involved in an auto accident with another vehicle carrying two people, in Indiana. The two people filed a personal injury lawsuit in an Indiana state court against the truck driver, truck owner, and truck lessee. The truck driver, truck owner, and truck lessee removed the case to the federal trial court. A physician who treated one of the two people stated in a deposition that defendant doctor's surgery performed on that person was unnecessary and exacerbated his injuries. The truck driver, truck owner, and truck lessee moved to file a third-party complaint for contribution against the doctor. A federal magistrate judge denied the motion. Thereafter, the truck driver, truck owner, and truck lessee filed a claim for contribution against the doctor in the Illinois state trial court. The trial court denied the doctor's motion to dismiss; the appellate court reversed. On further review, the state supreme court found that the contribution claim, pursuant to language in 740 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 100/5, could not be brought in the Illinois state court because it was not a third-party complaint filed in a pending action, as that statute required.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was affirmed.

 

211 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Timmons ex rel. R.L.S. v. L.S. (In re R.L.S.)


Docket No. 100081.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


218 Ill. 2d 428; 844 N.E.2d 22; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 312; 300 Ill. Dec. 350



February 2, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
Claggett v. Ronald L.S. (In re R.L.S.), 354 Ill. App. 3d 462, 820 N.E.2d 1201, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1529, 290 Ill. Dec. 134 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court reversed the trial court's findings that petitioner maternal grandparents lacked standing and that their petition for guardianship had to be dismissed, and held the sole standing requirement for guardianship petitioners was stated in 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-5(b) (2004). It ordered a remand of the case to the trial court to resolve the standing question under that statute. Respondent biological father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The minor child was the daughter of the mother and the biological father. The mother died. At the time, the mother and the biological father were separated. The mother and daughter had been living with the mother's maternal grandmother. Following the mother's death, the minor child's maternal grandparents petitioned the trial court to be appointed the minor child's guardians. The trial court appointed them as temporary guardians. The biological father moved to dismiss the maternal grandparents' guardianship petition, and the trial court eventually granted that motion. The maternal grandparents appealed. The appellate court reversed after concluding that the sole standing requirement for guardianship petitioners was stated in 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-5(b) (2004) and remanded to the trial court to resolve the standing question. Upon further review, the state supreme court found that the appellate court cited the correct statutory standard and that the maternal grandparents lacked standing to go forward with the guardianship petition unless they could show that they rebutted the presumption that the biological father was willing and able to make day-to-day child care decisions.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment and ordered that the case be remanded to resolve the case under the statutory standard cited by the appellate court.

 

212 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jordan


Docket No. 99895.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


218 Ill. 2d 255; 843 N.E.2d 870; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 4; 300 Ill. Dec. 270



January 20, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 2, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Jordan, 354 Ill. App. 3d 294, 820 N.E.2d 1083, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1470, 290 Ill. Dec. 16 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court found that the statute under which defendant was convicted, endangering the life and health of child, contained an unconstitutional presumption that was nevertheless severable, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-21.6(b) (2002). It also found that the State's evidence was otherwise insufficient to prove defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: A college campus security supervisor proceeded to a parking lot to search for a crying infant located in a vehicle. The infant appeared to be less than four-months-old. The outside air temperature was around 20 degrees. The police and fire departments were summoned and opened the car door. The supervisor believed that about 30 minutes passed between the time he arrived and the door was opened. The infant was removed to an ambulance; her father, the defendant, then showed up. The infant was dressed in warm clothing and defendant had been running an errand. Following a bench trial, defendant was found guilty of endangering the life and health of a child in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-21.6 (2002). On appeal, the appellate court found that the statute contained an unconstitutional mandatory presumption which was severable, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-21.6(b) (2002), and that the State's evidence was insufficient to proved defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. On further review, the state supreme court agreed that the one provision was unconstitutional, but found that sufficient evidence supported the conviction, and, thus, further proceedings were necessary.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's finding that the statute at issue contained an unconstitutional presumption, which was severable from the rest of the statute, was affirmed; however, its finding that the State's evidence was otherwise insufficient to prove defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

People ex rel. Dep't of Pub. Health v. Wiley


Docket No. 98763.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


218 Ill. 2d 207; 843 N.E.2d 259; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 7; 300 Ill. Dec. 1



January 20, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People ex rel. Dep't of Pub. Health v. Wiley, 348 Ill. App. 3d 809, 810 N.E.2d 614, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 593, 284 Ill. Dec. 824 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, the Illinois Department of Public Health. The Department had filed a two-count complaint against the doctor, alleging that the doctor breached four scholarship contracts under the Illinois Family Practice Residency Act, 110 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 935/1 et seq. (2002).


OVERVIEW: The Department asserted that the doctor failed to serve, within 30 days after her residency, as a full-time primary care physician in a designated shortage area approved by the Department and was, therefore, obligated to repay the original debt in treble, for a balance of $ 157,395 owed. The trial court had found that there was no question of material fact that the doctor failed to fulfill her service obligation because neither the type of medicine she practiced nor the locations where she practiced satisfied the terms of the scholarship contracts and the Act. The court found no merit with regard to the doctor's assertion on appeal that an installment agreement that had been entered into merged all claims based on the scholarship contracts and, therefore, the Department was precluded from proceeding. To the contrary, the court found that the installment agreement was a payment plan, rather than a settlement, and that the doctor failed to maintain the installment payments in any regard. The court held that the doctor breached the contracts when she did not obtain approval of her post-residency fellowship and failed to serve as a doctor within a designated shortage area.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

214 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Palmer


Docket No. 98333.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


218 Ill. 2d 148; 843 N.E.2d 292; 2006 Ill. LEXIS 8; 300 Ill. Dec. 34



January 20, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
People v. Palmer, 346 Ill. App. 3d 942, 806 N.E.2d 734, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 304, 282 Ill. Dec. 437 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part; sentence modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of eight Class X offenses. The trial court adjudged defendant an habitual criminal, and imposed seven natural-life sentences pursuant to the Habitual Criminal Act, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/33B-1 et seq., to be served consecutively. The Illinois Court of Appeals vacated three of the eight convictions, and imposed a single sentence of natural life. The State appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant invaded the victim's home, and over the course of two hours, forced the victims to engage in sex acts and committed robbery. The appellate court held that because there was only one conviction, the trial court improperly sentenced defendant to consecutive natural-life sentences. The state supreme court held that under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 5/33B-1, the individual crimes did not merge. Thus, the trial court properly imposed natural-life sentences on each count. However, the state supreme court held that the appellate court properly determined that natural-life sentences could not be imposed consecutively. The state supreme court found that it was physically impossible to serve consecutive sentences of natural life. Nor would the total amount of two or more natural-life sentences ever be more than defendant's one life. The state supreme court found that the purpose of the consecutive sentencing statute, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 5-8-4, of removing from society criminals not capable of reform was not served by consecutive natural life sentences. The state supreme court exercised its authority under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(b)(4) and imposed concurrent natural life sentences.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court concerning the holding that the trial court erred in imposing natural-life sentences on each of defendant's remaining five convictions was reversed. The trial court's judgment on the convictions and natural-life sentences for each conviction was affirmed. However, the trial court's judgment that defendant served those sentences consecutively was reversed, and concurrent sentences were imposed.

 

215 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Christopher K. (In re Christopher K.)


Docket No. 98597


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


217 Ill. 2d 348; 841 N.E.2d 945; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 2063; 299 Ill. Dec. 213



December 15, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
People v. Christopher K. (In re Christopher K.), 348 Ill. App. 3d 130, 810 N.E.2d 145, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 462, 284 Ill. Dec. 492 (Ill. App. Ct., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court allowed a petition by the State for review of a decision of the Appellate Court of Illinois that affirmed respondent juvenile's adjudication as delinquent after finding that he had committed acts that would have constituted murder if committed by an adult but reversed an adult sentence that had been imposed under the extended juvenile jurisdiction (EJJ) statute, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/5-810 (1998).


OVERVIEW: The juvenile had been 14 when he killed the victim. The trial court had denied the State's motion to try him as an adult, and the appellate court had affirmed the ruling. Nonetheless, to assure the juvenile's compliance with its disposition, it imposed an EJJ adult sentence, which would come into play only in the event of an unsuccessful juvenile disposition. Since the juvenile had complied and been released, the issue of the propriety of an EJJ sentence was moot, but the court addressed it as a matter of public interest. The EJJ issue and the transfer for trial as an adult issues involved distinct consideration of different statutory factors by a trial judge. Therefore, the decision not to grant discretionary transfer to an adult court had no law of the case effect on the trial court's ability to impose an EJJ sentence. The court also considered whether the juvenile's statements to police during custodial interrogation were properly admitted. Adopting the objective test used in federal constitutional case law, it held that the juvenile's question, "Do I need a lawyer?," to which an officer made a noncommittal response, was not an unequivocal invocation of the right to counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the affirmance of the delinquency adjudication but reversed the portion of the appellate judgment that had reversed the EJJ sentence.

 

216 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dinelli


Docket No. 98621


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


217 Ill. 2d 387; 841 N.E.2d 968; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 2065; 299 Ill. Dec. 236



December 15, 2005, Opinion Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The DuPage County Circuit Court (Illinois) permitted defendant to withdraw her guilty plea to a charge of unlawful possession of a stolen motor vehicle, denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charge against her, and then dismissed that charge anyway, on the ground that the permissive inference contained in 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/4-103 (2000) was unconstitutional. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with unlawful possession of a stolen motor vehicle in violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/4-103(a)(1) (2000). She subsequently pled guilty. Thereafter, she sought to withdraw her guilty plea and challenged the constitutionality of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/4-103(a)(1) (2000), which provided that the trier of fact could infer that a person exercising exclusive unexplained possession over a stolen vehicle knew that the vehicle was stolen, regardless of when it was stolen. Defendant also argued that the charge should be dismissed based on double jeopardy because she had pled guilty to criminal trespass to the same vehicle in a proceeding in another county, and the unlawful possession of a stolen motor vehicle charge in the forum county was the same continuing transaction. The trial court allowed her to withdraw her guilty plea, denied her motion to dismiss based on double jeopardy, and found the permissive inference to be unconstitutional. On appeal, the state supreme court found the two charges were separate acts and that the trial court prematurely found the permissive inference to be unconstitutional because it might not even be applied to her case.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment insofar as it allowed defendant to withdraw her guilty pled. However, it reversed that part of the trial court's judgment that dismissed the indictment filed against defendant, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

People v. Hall


Docket No. 98225


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


217 Ill. 2d 324; 841 N.E.2d 913; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 2073; 299 Ill. Dec. 181



December 15, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District.
People v. Hall, 211 Ill. 2d 594, 823 N.E.2d 971, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1073 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed, cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment to dismiss defendant's postconviction petition at the second stage of proceedings in a case where he filed that petition and claimed in it that his guilty plea to the charge against him of aggravated kidnapping was involuntary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant saw a car that had been left running at a gas station. No one appeared to be inside it. Defendant drove away in the car and soon wrecked the vehicle. Defendant then saw that a young child was in the car's rear seat. Defendant was charged with, inter alia, aggravated kidnapping. Defendant's counsel allegedly asserted that the lack of awareness of the child in the car would not be a defense to an aggravated kidnapping charge. Counsel also allegedly informed defendant that he would receive a 25-year sentence if he was convicted on it. Defendant was then admonished by the trial court, pled guilty in return for dismissal of other charges, and was sentenced to six years in prison. The trial court granted the State's motion to dismiss that claimed a substantial showing was not made of a constitutional violation. On further review, the state supreme court found defendant had stated a constitutional claim and the State had not shown that the trial court's admonitions overcame defense counsel's alleged erroneous advice given to defendant.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment that affirmed the trial court's dismissal of defendant's postconviction petition at the second stage of the proceedings, reversed the trial court's dismissal of the petition, and remanded the cause to the trial court for further proceedings on the petition.

People v. Olender


Docket No. 98932


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


222 Ill. 2d 123; 854 N.E.2d 593; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 2070; 305 Ill. Dec. 1



December 15, 2005, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) granted defendants' motions to dismiss the indictments filed against then pursuant to the Illinois Income Tax Act, 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1301 (1994) (Act), based on their contention that the Illinois General Assembly violated the single subject clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d), in enacting the public law containing the Act. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Illinois General Assembly enacted 1994 Ill. Laws 88-669 entitled "An Act in relation to government regulation." That law amended, among other statutes, the Illinois Income Tax Act, 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1301 (1994) (Act). Thereafter, the State charged defendants under the amended version of the Act with willfully violating the Act by filing fraudulent tax returns for two different tax years by listing their adjusted gross income as nothing in each of those years when they allegedly knew that the true amount was in excess of that figure. Defendants moved to dismiss the indictments on the ground that the Act, as amended, violated the single subject clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d). The trial court granted defendants' motions to dismiss. On appeal, the state supreme court first found that defendants had standing to challenge the Act despite the nine-year delay between enactment and their challenge to it because they were charged with violating it. The state supreme court then found that 1994 Ill. Laws 88-669 violated the single subject clause of the Illinois Constitution because that law dealt with many different and disparate subjects.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Phillips


Docket No. 99568


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


217 Ill. 2d 270; 840 N.E.2d 1194; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1625; 298 Ill. Dec. 759



December 1, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District.
People v. Phillips, 352 Ill. App. 3d 867, 817 N.E.2d 566, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1254, 288 Ill. Dec. 208 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of various drug related charges and driving while her license was suspended. The appellate court affirmed. The supreme court denied defendant's petition for leave to appeal but issued a supervisory order directing the appellate court to reconsider. Upon reconsideration, the appellate court (Illinois) reached a contrary result. The State's petition for leave to appeal was granted.


OVERVIEW: In her initial appeal, defendant alleged that the admission into evidence of a lab report violated her Sixth Amendment right to be confronted with the witnesses against her. In the appellate court's response to the supreme court's supervisory order, the appellate court concluded that the record failed to show that defendant was advised of the consequences and implications of the evidentiary stipulation counsel made with regard to the lab report. The supreme court, in its review, held that it was not necessary for the trial court or counsel to have admonished defendant about the implications and consequences of the stipulation because (1) defense counsel's decision to stipulate appeared to have been a matter of trial tactics and strategy and defendant did not object to counsel's decision, and (2) the State's entire case was not presented by stipulation, defendant did present or preserve a defense, and the stipulation did not include a statement that the evidence was sufficient to convict.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed, and the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

220 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Big Sky Excavating, Inc. v. Ill. Bell Tel. Co.


Docket No. 99380


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


217 Ill. 2d 221; 840 N.E.2d 1174; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1628; 298 Ill. Dec. 739; 36 A.L.R.6th 783



December 1, 2005, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee businesses filed a class action suit challenging the constitutionality of 220 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-502.5 of the Illinois Public Utilities Act, 220 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1-101 et seq. (2002), which abated the Illinois Commerce Commission's proceedings against appellant telephone company. The Madison County Circuit Court declared § 13-502.5 invalid under the Illinois Constitution. The company sought review.


OVERVIEW: While the Commission's investigation of the company's rate hike was pending, the legislature enacted § 13-502.5, which abated the Commission's case against the company; classified certain of the company's services as competitive, enabling it to increase rates; and obliged it to refund money to some customers and to fund a state program. The trial court held that § 13-502.5 violated the special legislation clause of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 and the due process and equal protection clauses of Ill Const. art. I, § 2. The supreme court disagreed. Any advantages the company may have received under the law were not denied to others who were similarly situated. As the company was uniquely situated, the special legislation clause did not bar enactment of a law tailored to address conditions presented by that unique situation. Further, the classification established by 220 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-502.5 was rationally related to a legitimate state interest. Since § 13-502.5 did not violate the special legislation clause, it did not violate the businesses' right to equal protection. Finally, the businesses lacked a vested property right necessary to support their due process claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

221 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Campa


Docket No. 99501


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


217 Ill. 2d 243; 840 N.E.2d 1157; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1631; 298 Ill. Dec. 722



December 1, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District. H
People v. Campa, 353 Ill. App. 3d 178, 818 N.E.2d 787, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1198, 288 Ill. Dec. 852 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: At issue was whether defendant received a speedy trial as required by 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/103-5 (2000). The appellate court (Illinois) held that he did not. The state supreme court granted the State's petition for leave to appeal pursuant to 177 Ill. 2d R. 315(a).


OVERVIEW: At the time defendant demanded a speedy trial, he was participating in the county sheriff's day reporting center program. On appeal, the State argued that the appellate court committed error in finding that defendant was in "custody" within the meaning of the speedy trial statute. The state supreme court concluded that the program was a form of restraint that fell within the broad meaning of the term "custody." Thus, as a participant in the program, defendant was in the "custody" of the Cook County Department of Corrections and the Department of Community Supervision and Intervention. Significant restraints were placed on defendant's liberty. He reported to a jail facility on a daily basis and was expected to be at the facility from 8 a.m. until 1:30 p.m. In addition, the state supreme court concluded that the definitions of bail and recognizance found in 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/102-6, 5/102-19, and 5/110-2 (2000), and the statutory framework providing for the release of a defendant on bail or recognizance, left no doubt that the trial court was responsible for setting and modifying bail and releasing a defendant on his or her own recognizance, not the county sheriff.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.

 

222 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mertz


Docket No. 96288


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


218 Ill. 2d 1; 842 N.E.2d 618; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1612; 299 Ill. Dec. 581



November 17, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Rehearing denied by People v. Mertz, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 15 (Ill., Jan. 23, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Mertz v. Illinois, 549 U.S. 828, 127 S. Ct. 47, 166 L. Ed. 2d 48, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5941 (2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability granted, in part, Certificate of appealability denied, in part United States ex rel. Mertz v. Hardy, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 131034 (N.D. Ill., Sept. 13, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Coles County (Illinois), defendant was convicted of first degree murder (720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1(a) (2000)) and other crimes. The jury found him eligible for the death penalty, and that no mitigating factors precluded such a sentence. The circuit court sentenced him to death on the first degree murder conviction. Because he was sentenced to death, his appeal was brought directly to the court.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, all issues were related to the propriety of the death sentence. Defendant first disputed the use of statements he made pertaining to uncharged offenses, that he had committed a murder and burned down an apartment building. The state supreme court found these statements were voluntary and were not made to police officers in a custodial setting, but were made to defendant's friends, with no prompting whatsoever. It was for the jury to decide whether they were the product of a "poor sense of humor" or genuine admissions of responsibility. Defendant also disputed the State's introduction of his Internet viewing of sexually explicit sites, nude photos of his girlfriends, his e-mail address, his tattoos, the books he possessed, his possession of guns, and his "political" statements. However, most, if not all, of the evidence was admissible under Dawson. To the extent that some evidence could have been improperly admitted, its admission was harmless in view of overwhelming aggravating evidence. The admission of a crime scene expert's testimony was harmless, as it was cumulative of testimony given by other witnesses, and any inferences drawn by the expert were commonsense ones.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The clerk of the court was directed to enter an order setting Monday, January 9, 2006, as the date on which the sentence of death was to be carried out. Defendant was to be executed in the manner provided by law. The clerk was to send a certified copy of the mandate to the Director of Corrections, the warden of Tamms Correctional Center, and the warden of the institution where defendant was confined.

Bowman v. Am. River Transp. Co.


Docket No. 99094


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


217 Ill. 2d 75; 838 N.E.2d 949; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1604; 298 Ill. Dec. 56; 2005 AMC 2584



October 20, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bowman v. Am. River Transp. Co., 126 S. Ct. 1619, 164 L. Ed. 2d 333, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 2517 (U.S., Mar. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District.
Bowman v. Am. River Transp. Co., 212 Ill. 2d 528, 824 N.E.2d 282, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1841, 291 Ill. Dec. 706 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employers challenged a decision from an Illinois appellate court, which affirmed a trial court's refusal to grant a motion for a jury trial in a Jones Act, 46 U.S.C.S. app. § 688 et seq., case filed by plaintiff injured employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured while working as a seaman on a harbor boat. A request for a jury trial was stricken by the circuit court. An appeal was filed after a bench trial, and the decision to deny a jury trial was affirmed. In reversing, the court determined that the "election" referred to in the Jones Act was not the seaman's election of a right to a jury trial, but his election to proceed at law, rather than in admiralty. There was a right to trial by jury in common law claims, but not those filed in admiralty. The court noted that it was not bound by federal court decisions since the exact issues were not decided by the United States Supreme Court. The Act did not give an exclusive right to the injured employee to elect a trial by jury in an action filed in state court. Next, the court held that the availability of a jury trial in cases brought under the Act was a question properly controlled by the laws of the forum. The right was guaranteed by Ill. Const. art. I, § 13 because jury trials had been held for injured seamen for many years. The Act was not a new cause of action at law because it merely removed the bar to common law suits created by the decision in The Osceola.


OUTCOME: The judgments of both the appellate and the circuit court were reversed, and the case was remanded for a trial by jury.

Apex Tax Invs., Inc. v. Lowe (In re County Collector)


Docket No. 97165


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


217 Ill. 2d 1; 838 N.E.2d 907; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1605; 298 Ill. Dec. 14



October 20, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by, Remanded by Estate of Lowe v. Apex Tax Invs., Inc., 126 S. Ct. 2287, 164 L. Ed. 2d 811, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 3959 (U.S., 2006)
Substituted opinion at, On remand at County Collector for Judgment & Sale Against Landsand Lots Returned Delinquent for Nonpayment of Gen. Taxes v. Lowe, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 450 (Ill., Apr. 19, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Petition of Apex Tax Invs., Inc. v. Lowe (In re County Collector), 207 Ill. 2d 602, 807 N.E.2d 975, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 64, 283 Ill. Dec. 134 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a public guardian on behalf of an estate of a mentally incompetent person, challenged the judgment of the Court County Circuit Court (Illinois), which denied the public guardian's request to set aside a tax deed issued to appellee, an investment corporation. The public guardian filed an amended petition to set aside the deed, pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1401 (1994) and 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 200/22-45 (1994).


OVERVIEW: The public guardian filed its amended petition after the investment corporation purchased the home of the mentally incompetent person at a tax sale. The investment corporation received a tax deed in 1993. At the close of the hearing, the trial court found that the redemption period had expired, that no redemption had been made, and that the investment corporation complied with applicable notice provisions by exercising due diligence in attempting to locate the incompetent. The public guardian asserted that the tax deed should have been set aside because there was clear and convincing evidence that it was procured by fraud or deception because two of the notices were returned in their envelopes with the notation that the addressee was mentally incompetent. The court disagreed and noted that the fact that the investment corporation submitted those two envelopes into evidence was a strong indication that there was no deceptive or fraudulent act on the part of the investment corporation. The court also noted that no provisions existed under statutory law to set aside a tax deed upon equitable principles.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Sharpe


Docket No. 91874


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


216 Ill. 2d 481; 839 N.E.2d 492; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 977; 298 Ill. Dec. 169



October 6, 2005, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which partially granted defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment against him by holding that the 15-year and 20-year enhancements to first degree murder under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(i) and (a)(1)(d)(ii) (2000) were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court also held that the 25-to-life enhancement applicable to first degree murder when the defendant personally discharged a firearm which resulted in death, pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(iii) (2000), was not unconstitutional. The trial court determined that the 15 and 20-year enhancements violated the proportionate penalties clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. On appeal, the State argued that the trial court erred in determining that the 15- and 20-year sentence enhancements were unconstitutionally disproportionate. Defendant argued that the trial court was correct in so concluding and asserted that the 25-to-life sentence enhancement suffered from the same defect in that such enhancement was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that it was impermissible for a defendant to challenge a penalty under the proportionate penalties clause by comparing it to the penalty for an offense with different elements. As such, the trial court erred in holding that the 15- and 20-year firearm enhancements to first degree murder were unconstitutional under the proportionate penalties clause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

226 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Guevara


Docket Nos. 97070, 97299 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


216 Ill. 2d 533; 837 N.E.2d 901; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 981; 297 Ill. Dec. 450



October 6, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District.
People v. Waltrip, 207 Ill. 2d 626, 807 N.E.2d 981, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 163, 283 Ill. Dec. 140 (2004)



DISPOSITION: No. 97070-Reversed and remanded. No. 97299-Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In defendant one's case, the State filed an interlocutory appeal from an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which declared that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-11(a)(3) (2000) was unconstitutional. In a separate case, defendant two appealed from an appellate court ruling that § 12-11(a)(3), (c) did not violate the proportionate penalties clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970). The appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: Both defendants had been charged with home invasion with a firearm under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-11(a)(3) (2000). Both defendants argued that the sentence for home invasion while in possession of a firearm was unconstitutionally disproportionate to the sentence for aggravated battery with a firearm. That argument failed because after the Sharpe decision, defendants could not challenge a penalty under the proportionate penalties clause by comparing it with the penalty for an offense with different elements. Defendant one also argued that § 12-11(a)(3) constituted an impermissible double enhancement. The trial court agreed with defendant two that the presence of a firearm was used twice in the home invasion statute, first as an element of the offense and then again to enhance the offense with a 15-year sentencing add-on. The supreme court disagreed. Home invasion with a firearm was a distinct offense. However, the firearm factor was used only as an element of the offense under § 12-11(a)(3); it was not mentioned in the sentencing provision of § 12-11(c), which simply defined the sentence for the distinct crime in § 12-11(a)(3).


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and defendant one's case was remanded for further proceedings. The appellate court's judgment was affirmed.

Ill. State Chamber of Commerce v. Filan


Docket No. 100197


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


216 Ill. 2d 653; 837 N.E.2d 922; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1610; 297 Ill. Dec. 471



October 6, 2005, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Circuit court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state officials appealed a Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) summary judgment declaring the Illinois FY2004 Budget Implementation Act, 2003 Ill. Laws 32 (2003), violative of Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 and Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 as applied to plaintiff employer. The employer had challenged the operation of new statutory provisions, in particular, 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/416 (2004) and 30 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 105/8j (2004).


OVERVIEW: To meet a fiscal crisis, the legislature had enacted what were denominated as non-consumer user fees, imposed on groups of taxpayers that used certain state administrative services. 30 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 105/8j (2004) authorized transfers of portions of those fees into the general revenue fund, ostensibly to cover indirect costs of providing the services. The employer challenged a particular fee imposed on it under 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/416 (2004) as a purchaser of workers' compensation insurance. It claimed that it had been unfairly burdened in violation of the uniformity clause and that the fee violated due process. The court held that the employer had failed to meet the heavy burden imposed on those who claimed a statute was unconstitutional. It had not overcome the officials' showing that the distinction between employers and employees was rationally based on which parties were best positioned to pay for administration of the workers' compensation system. The fee itself had already been lowered, and there was simply too little evidence to find a confiscatory fee that violated due process. The employer's takings claim would be considered on remand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of summary judgment as to another constitutional claim raised by the employer, but reversed the grant of summary in favor of the employer as to the other two constitutional claims. It remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Vill. of Chatham v. County of Sangamon


Docket No. 99136


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


216 Ill. 2d 402; 837 N.E.2d 29; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 967; 297 Ill. Dec. 249



September 22, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District.
Vill. of Chatham v. County of Sangamon, 351 Ill. App. 3d 889, 814 N.E.2d 216, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 952, 286 Ill. Dec. 566 (Ill. App. Ct., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which affirmed the circuit court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee village in its suit seeking declaratory judgment that the village, and not the county, had zoning and building code jurisdiction on areas subject to annexation agreements with the village and an injunction preventing the county from interfering with such agreements.


OVERVIEW: Property owners in the county reached agreements with the village for the future annexation of their properties. When the county asserted that it had building code jurisdiction over the properties, the village successfully sought declaratory judgment that it, not the county, had zoning and building code jurisdiction over the properties. On review, the court affirmed, first finding that because the county was not affected by § 15.1 of the Municipal Code, 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-15.1-2.1 (2002), it did not have standing to challenge its constitutionality. The court then found that under all versions of the often amended § 15.1, 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-15.1-1, property subject to an annexation agreement within the county would be subject to the municipality's ordinances, control, and jurisdiction. The court then found that the legislature had determined that a municipality could exercise certain jurisdiction over property that was subject to an annexation agreement as of the time the agreement was entered into, rather than the time of annexation, and that such a determination was best left to the discretion of the legislature in the exercise of its police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Avery v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


Docket No. 91494


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


216 Ill. 2d 100; 835 N.E.2d 801; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 959; 296 Ill. Dec. 448



August 18, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Avery v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 2005 Ill. LEXIS 970 (Ill., Sept. 26, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Avery v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 547 U.S. 1003, 126 S. Ct. 1470, 164 L. Ed. 2d 248, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 2047 (2006)
Related proceeding at Hale v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 44270 (S.D. Ill., Mar. 28, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District.
Avery v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 321 Ill. App. 3d 269, 746 N.E.2d 1242, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 249, 254 Ill. Dec. 194 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: The portion of the circuit court's judgment which denied the policyholders' request for equitable relief was affirmed. All other portions of the circuit court's judgment were reversed. Those portions of the appellate court judgment which affirmed the denial of equitable relief and which reversed the circuit court's award of disgorgement damages were affirmed. All other portions of the appellate court's judgment were reversed.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff policyholders brought a class action against defendant insurance company, for breach of contract and statutory consumer fraud, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief. The jury found in their favor on the breach of contract and fraud claims. The circuit court granted declaratory relief but not injunctive relief. The Appellate Court (Illinois) affirmed, but reversed a part of the damages. The company's petition to appeal was allowed.


OVERVIEW: The policyholders disputed the propriety of the company's practice of specifying the use of non-"original equipment manufacturer" crash parts to repair its policyholders' cars when such cheaper parts were available. The appeals court found the jury verdict on the breach of contract claim could not be affirmed. The jury was incorrectly instructed that the operative language in the insurer's various policy forms could be given a uniform interpretation. Further, the verdict could not be affirmed for any subclass of policyholders who were insured under any of the relevant individual policy forms. There was no basis in the law for specification damages. As to the Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act, the supreme court found that the circuit court erred in certifying a nationwide class that included class members whose claims proceedings took place outside Illinois. The only putative class that could exist was a class consisting of policyholders whose vehicles were assessed and repaired in Illinois. Because the representative policyholder had not proven his claim for consumer fraud, there could be no Illinois class for the policyholders' consumer fraud count.


OUTCOME: That portion of the circuit court's judgment which denied the policyholders' request for equitable relief was affirmed. All other portions of the circuit court's judgment were reversed. Those portions of the appellate court judgment which affirmed the denial of equitable relief and which reversed the circuit court's award of disgorgement damages were affirmed. All other portions of the appellate court's judgment were reversed.


 

230 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Shellstrom


Docket No. 97831


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


216 Ill. 2d 45; 833 N.E.2d 863; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 957; 295 Ill. Dec. 657



July 21, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
People v. Shellstrom, 345 Ill. App. 3d 175, 802 N.E.2d 381, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1568, 280 Ill. Dec. 456 (Ill. App. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed; circuit court judgment vacated; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Illinois sought review of a decision of an appellate court (Illinois), which reversed a circuit court's summary dismissal of appellee inmate's pro se pleading in which the inmate sought a reduction in his sentence or a writ of mandamus directing compliance with the guilty plea he had entered on home invasion and aggravated criminal sexual assault charges.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court recharacterized the mandamus motion as a motion under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-1 et seq. (2002), and summarily dismissed the motion as patently without merit. The appellate court held that the pleading should have been dealt with as labeled and that there was no provision for summary dismissal under the mandamus statute. The supreme court affirmed but held that 1) the circuit court had the option, under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-1(d) (2002), of recharacterizing the pro se motion, regardless of how it was labeled; 2) in all future cases, where a circuit court wished to recharacterize a first postconviction pro se motion as one falling under the Act, the circuit court was required to notify the pro se litigant of the court's intention, to warn the litigant of the effect of the recharacterization on subsequent postconviction petitions, and to provide the litigant with an opportunity to withdraw or amend the pleading so that it contained all of the claims appropriate to a postconviction petition; and 3) as the inmate had not been given the opportunity to withdraw or amend, remand was required so that he could do so.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed but on a different basis than the appellate court's holding.

County of Cook ex rel. Rifkin v. Bear Stearns & Co.


Docket No. 97022


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


215 Ill. 2d 466; 831 N.E.2d 563; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 943; 294 Ill. Dec. 613



June 3, 2005, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that dismissed plaintiff taxpayers' complaint that asserted that they had standing to assert a cause of action on behalf of the forum county pursuant to either 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/20-101 et seq. (1998) or the common law. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant underwriter was the lead underwriter for the forum county's issuance of bonds to refinance, at lower interest rates, some municipal bonds. Thereafter, the taxpayers filed a putative class action seeking to recover, on behalf of the forum county, overcharges made by the underwriter. Also included in the taxpayers' lawsuit were defendants, two financial advisors who allegedly gave advice. The complaint did not allege any county involvement in any of the alleged wrongdoing. The underwriter, the two financial advisors, and the county, as a nominal plaintiff, filed motions to dismiss. They challenged the taxpayers' standing. The trial court granted the motions to dismiss. On direct appeal, the state supreme court found that the State's Attorney had the exclusive power to represent the forum county in litigation where it was the real party in interest, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/20-104(b) (1998) was unconstitutional to the extent it purported to confer standing on the taxpayers, and no common law claim could be brought because no claim was made that a public official was responsible for any alleged injury and only the State's Attorney had the power to assert such a claim.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

232 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Phillips


Docket No. 98070


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


215 Ill. 2d 554; 831 N.E.2d 574; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 945; 294 Ill. Dec. 624



June 3, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District.
People v. Phillips, 346 Ill. App. 3d 487, 805 N.E.2d 667, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 166, 282 Ill. Dec. 48 (Ill. App. Ct., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court of Illinois affirming defendant's convictions of possessing, with intent to disseminate, a picture of a child engaged in sexual intercourse in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-20.1(a)(1)(i), (2) (2000) and of two counts of possessing, with intent to disseminate, a picture of a child engaged in oral sex in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-20.1(a)(1)(ii), (2) (2000).


OVERVIEW: A person who was repairing defendant's computer discovered that a file on the hard drive contained child pornography. The repair person called the police officer and told him what he had seen. The officer viewed the video and agreed that it was child pornography. Defendant was arrested. A search of defendant's home revealed numerous other images of child pornography. The indictment against defendant was sufficiently precise to adequately inform defendant of the nature of the charges. The indictment charged him with possessing a photograph or other similar visual reproduction or depiction by computer. From this language, defendant should have understood that he was charged with possessing pornographic pictures of children. The disjunctive language in each count merely gave the State flexibility as to the physical form of the pictures. Defendant's motion to suppress was properly denied. The Fourth Amendment was not violated when the officer viewed the file as the officer's confirmation of what the repair person, a private citizen, saw on the file did not exceed the scope of the repair person's private search to which no Fourth Amendment protection attached.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

PHL, Inc. v. Pullman Bank & Trust Co.


Docket Nos. 96250, 96294 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


216 Ill. 2d 250; 836 N.E.2d 351; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 947; 296 Ill. Dec. 828



June 3, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Rehearing denied by PHL, Inc. v. Pullman Bank & Trust Co., 2005 Ill. LEXIS 971 (Ill., Sept. 26, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by PHL, Inc. v. Pullman Bank & Trust Co., 2006 U.S. LEXIS 2043 (U.S., Mar. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District.
PHL, Inc. v. Pullman Bank & Trust Co., 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1436 (Ill., Oct. 7, 2003)
President Lincoln Hotel Venture v. Bank One, 271 Ill. App. 3d 1048, 649 N.E.2d 432, 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1300, 208 Ill. Dec. 376 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Illinois State Treasurer and a bank, appealed from a decision of an appellate court (Illinois), which affirmed a circuit court's judgment in favor of plaintiff buyers in a breach of contract action involving the buyers' attempts to purchase two hotel venture loans from the State.


OVERVIEW: The buyers tried to purchase venture loans that had been made from a state mortgage fund. The Treasurer failed to close on the agreements after the Illinois Attorney General withheld approval of them, based in part on his opinion that the Governor's consent was required before the transactions could go forward. On appeal, defendants contended, as they had in both lower courts, that the buyers were asserting a breach of contract action against the State that could only be brought in the Illinois Court of Claims. The court agreed, holding that the officer suit exception to the doctrine of sovereign immunity did not apply. The fact that the Treasurer chose to adhere to the Attorney General's opinion did not violate Ill. Const. art. V, § 18 (1970). The court expressed no opinion as to whether either approval of the buy-sell agreements by either the Governor or the Attorney General was needed. It simply held that the Treasurer had not acted outside the broad grant of authority given to her in § 18 and, even if she had, her actions were not ultra vires. Thus, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 505/8(b) (2000) controlled, and the buyers' action could only be brought in the court of claims.


OUTCOME: The judgments of both lower courts reversed, and the case was remanded to the circuit court with directions to dismiss the buyers' complaint.

Scachitti v. UBS Fin. Servs.


Docket Nos. 97023, 97866 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


215 Ill. 2d 484; 831 N.E.2d 544; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 949; 294 Ill. Dec. 594



June 3, 2005, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Circuit court judgments affirmed in part and reversed in part; causes remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, taxpayers in two separate actions, sought review after their complaints were dismissed by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). The complaints included common law claims alleging fraud, breach of fiduciary duty, breach of contract, accountant malpractice, and fraudulent and negligent misrepresentation as well as claims under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/20-104(b) (2002) and the Whistleblower Reward and Protection Act.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed their actions against defendant financial entities to recover, on behalf of the State, overcharges made in connection with certain state bond transactions. The issues on appeal dealt with the taxpayers' standing to bring their claims and the constitutionality of the qui tam provisions of the Whistleblower Act, 740 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 175/1 et seq. (2002). Refusing to deviate from its holding in Lyons, the supreme court held that the taxpayers lacked standing to bring the common law claims because the State was the real party in interest on those claims and, therefore, only the Illinois Attorney General had standing to bring them. Also in accordance with Lyons, the taxpayers' claims under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/20-104(b) (2002) failed because that statute unconstitutionally usurped the Attorney General's powers. However, as the Attorney General retained authority to control any litigation under the qui tam provisions of the Whistleblower Act, the trial court erred in finding those provisions to be unconstitutional and in dismissing the taxpayers' qui tam claims.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the dismissal of the common law claims and claims filed under the Code of Civil Procedure; the supreme court reversed the dismissal of the qui tam claims and remanded the cases for further proceedings.

Turcol v. Pension Bd. of Trustees


Docket No. 98571


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


214 Ill. 2d 521; 828 N.E.2d 277; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 622; 293 Ill. Dec. 307



April 7, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Adhered to Turcol v. Pension Bd., 359 Ill. App. 3d 795, 834 N.E.2d 490, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 796, 295 Ill. Dec. 909 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District.
Turcol v. Pension Bd. of Trs. of the Matteson Police Pension Fund, 346 Ill. App. 3d 1182, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 3251 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Appeal Dismissed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court confirmed appellee police pension board's decision that denied appellant policeman's application for a line-of-duty disability retirement pension under 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-114.1 because the board correctly decided that 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-115 precluded awarding a pension since one of the three physicians selected by the board declined "to certify" that he was disabled. The policeman appealed.


OVERVIEW: The highest court allowed the appeal to resolve a conflict in between published decisions of the appeals court regarding the construction of § 5/3-115. However, the highest court decided that it had improvidently allowed the appeal. That was because the board also denied the policeman's application on the basis that the policeman failed "to prove" he was disabled and the appeals court did not address that alternative issue; if it had addressed that alternative issue and agreed with the board, then it would not have had to address the issue of (1) whether the policeman's application could be denied just because one of the three physicians failed "to certify" the policeman was disabled, and (2) the resulting question of whether the board's requirement, that all three physicians had to certify that the policeman was disabled, was constitutional (a question that the appeals court had resolved in favor of the board).


OUTCOME: The highest court dismissed the appeal and remanded the case to the appeals court for further proceedings, which were to include issuing a supplemental opinion or order considering whether the board's decision could be confirmed on the ground that the policeman failed to prove his disability.
