People v. Wilson


Docket No. 98111


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


214 Ill. 2d 394; 827 N.E.2d 416; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 323; 292 Ill. Dec. 887



March 24, 2005, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment of the trial court reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with two counts of domestic battery, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-3.2(a)(1), (a)(2) (2002). Defendant moved to dismiss the charges. Following an evidentiary hearing, the circuit court granted the motion to dismiss. The Circuit Court of Douglas County (Illinois) denied the State's motion to reconsider. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction for domestic battery was based on an incident involving a former girlfriend. Defendant and the victim dated for 10 months and lived together for four of those months. The incident occurred four months after the couple ended their relationship. On appeal, defendant argued that the definition of family or household members in 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-3.2(a)(1), (a)(2) (2002) was unconstitutionally vague because it did not place a time limit on the former relationship. The appellate court agreed with the State that the trial court clearly erred in holding the statute unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant. Defendant fell within the definition of a family or household member on two separate bases: he and the victim had had a dating relationship and had shared a common dwelling. In addition, the appellate court found the prohibitions were sufficiently definite, when measured by common understanding and practice, to give a person of ordinary intelligence fair warning as to what conduct was prohibited. It was not unreasonable for the legislature to include within the domestic battery statute relationships that had been over for only a few months.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order holding the statute unconstitutional was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Lisa M. (In re D.W.)


Docket Nos. 97292, 98896 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


214 Ill. 2d 289; 827 N.E.2d 466; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 319; 292 Ill. Dec. 937



March 24, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Lisa Z. (In re Amanda D.), 349 Ill. App. 3d 941, 811 N.E.2d 1237, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 763, 285 Ill. Dec. 358 (Ill. App. Ct., 2004)
People v. L.M. (In re D.W.), 344 Ill. App. 3d 30, 799 N.E.2d 410, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1238, 278 Ill. Dec. 692 (Ill. App. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: In cause no. 98896, judgment of the appellate court affirmed; in cause no. 97292, judgments of the appellate court and of the trial court reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court found in the case of respondent first mother that the statute used to conclusively presume her to be an unfit parent, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(q) (2000), violated her due process and equal protection clause rights. In a separate case, the Illinois appellate court upheld that statute's constitutionality. Petitioner State appealed in the first mother's case, and respondent second mother appealed in the other.


OVERVIEW: In two appeals, the state supreme court considered the constitutionality of 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(q) (2000), which provided a conclusive presumption of parental unfitness if the parent had been convicted of certain offenses. In the first case, the first mother was convicted of the attempted murder of her infant son. She later gave birth to another child. The State sought to have her found unfit based on the conviction and that statute. The trial court found her to be unfit; her parental rights were later terminated. On appeal, the appellate court found the statute violated her due process and equal protection rights. In the second case, the prior conviction was aggravated battery; the parental rights were also terminated under the statute. The appellate court found the statute to be constitutional. On further review, the state supreme court noted that the same or similar offenses listed under 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(i) (2000) created only a rebuttable presumption of unfitness and violated the mothers' equal protection rights because the State could not show a compelling state interest existed in having different presumptions in similar statutory provisions.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment finding that the statute was unconstitutional was affirmed. Its judgment in the second case finding that the statute was constitutional was reversed as was the underlying trial court decision terminating the second mother's parental rights. Both decisions found the mothers' equal protection rights were violated. Also, the second case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


214 Ill. 2d 253; 824 N.E.2d 614; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 314; 291 Ill. Dec. 758



February 17, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at Forus Mortg. Corp. v. Dwyer (In re County Treasurer), 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 867 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Aug. 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]

DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court of Illinois dismissed the appeal filed by appellant property owners from the trial court's denial of property owners' 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1203 (2000) postjudgment motion after the appellate court found that the trial court's order for issuance of a tax deed was incontestable and that a property owner could not file a postjudgment motion for reconsideration. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owners had a single-family residence which was sold to a company for taxes due. The company later transferred the property to appellant mortgage corporation. The mortgage corporation petitioned the trial court for a tax deed. The property owners did not redeem. The mortgage corporation applied for an order directing the county clerk to issue a tax deed. The appellate court dismissed the appeal as untimely because it found, from the language of 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 200/22-45 (2000), that the order for issuance of a tax deed could only be challenged by a direct appeal or by a 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 (2000) motion for relief from judgment. On further appeal, the state supreme court found that the property owners could file a § 2-1203 motion because the legislature, in drafting § 2-1401, was only concerned about limiting collateral, but not direct, attacks on an order for issuance of a tax deed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was reversed and the cause was remanded to the appellate court for further proceedings on the merits.

243 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Ryan v. Agpro, Inc.


Docket No. 97986


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


214 Ill. 2d 222; 824 N.E.2d 270; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 311; 291 Ill. Dec. 694



February 3, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
People ex rel. Ryan v. Agpro, Inc., 345 Ill. App. 3d 1011, 803 N.E.2d 1007, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 64, 281 Ill. Dec. 386 (Ill. App. Ct., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State sued defendants, a corporation and its president, over the alleged contamination of soil and groundwater. The circuit court awarded remediation costs and imposed a civil penalty, but refused to enter a mandatory injunction requiring defendants to clean up the contamination. The State and defendants appealed. The Illinois appellate court affirmed the denial of injunctive relief. The State sought further review on this issue.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were in the business of applying fertilizers and pesticides to farm fields. The circuit court found that defendants caused soil, groundwater, and wells to be contaminated by pesticides. The circuit court refused to order defendants to clean up the site, finding that it had no authority under former 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/42(e) (2002) of the Illinois Environmental Protection Act, 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1 et seq. (2002), to issue a mandatory injunction. The appellate court affirmed; six months later, the legislature amended 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/42(e) to provide for mandatory injunctions. The supreme court held that, based on the plain and ordinary meaning of the word "restrain," former § 5/42(e) did not allow mandatory injunctions. Further, under the constitutional doctrine of separation of powers, the legislature could not retroactively alter a statute to overrule a decision of a reviewing court. The amendment to § 5/42(e) was not a retrospective "clarification" of existing law, but was instead a change in the law. A subsequent amendment to a statute could not replace the plain meaning as the best evidence of the legislature's original intent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Ramirez


Docket No. 97620


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


214 Ill. 2d 176; 824 N.E.2d 232; 2005 Ill. LEXIS 8; 291 Ill. Dec. 656



January 21, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District.
People v. Ramirez, 344 Ill. App. 3d 296, 800 N.E.2d 844, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1400, 279 Ill. Dec. 556 (Ill. App. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment by the appellate court (Illinois) that reversed and remanded defendant's in absentia conviction.


OVERVIEW: When defendant failed to appear for trial, he was tried in absentia and convicted of unlawful possession of cocaine with the intent to deliver. He was sentenced to 21 years in prison. Thereafter, the trial court denied defendant's motion for a new trial, and the appellate court reversed and remanded for a new trial. On further review, the state supreme court held that although defendant was present in open court when the trial court set his case, he was not present when the actual trial dates were set. Thereafter, the notice of the trial date was sent by regular mail rather than by certified mail, as required by 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-4.1(a) (1992). By requiring the State to show strict compliance with § 115-4.1(a), defendant's important constitutional rights were afforded all of the necessary statutory safeguards.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

245 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cornelius


Docket No. 97062


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


213 Ill. 2d 178; 821 N.E.2d 288; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 2034; 290 Ill. Dec. 237



December 2, 2004, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with unlawful failure to register as a sex offender in violation of § 3(b) of the Sex Offender Registration Act (730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/3(b) (2002)). He moved to dismiss, arguing the Act, and the Sex Offender and Child Murderer Community Notification Law, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 152/101 et seq. (2002), was unconstitutional. The Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) granted dismissal. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 2000 the Notification Law was amended by adding § 115(b), 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 152/115(b) (2002), requiring the state police to post Statewide Sex Offender Database on the Internet. Defendant claimed the dissemination of his photograph and physical attributes on an Internet page violated his privacy rights. The supreme court found that as the sex offender registry information was already open to the public and was a matter of public record, defendant's registry information was not "private" and did not fall within the Illinois Constitution's privacy clause protections. On defendant's substantive due process challenge, the court found there was a rational relationship between the disclosure of sex offender registration information via the Internet and the goals of protecting the general public and assisting law enforcement. Defendant failed to present any reasoned or developed argument with respect to his equal protection challenge. Informed by the analysis of the U.S. Supreme Court in Smith v. Doe, the supreme court found defendant failed to meet his burden to clearly show that § 115(b) violated the ex post facto provisions of the United States or Illinois constitutions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

 

246 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Lucien v. Briley


Docket No. 92922


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


213 Ill. 2d 340; 821 N.E.2d 1148; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 2035; 290 Ill. Dec. 574



December 2, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Rehearing denied by Lucien v. Briley, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 11 (Ill., Jan. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Lucien v. Welborn, 1995 U.S. App. LEXIS 1513 (7th Cir. Ill., Jan. 24, 1995)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner sought an order of habeas corpus alleging his extended-term sentence was unconstitutional under Apprendi and he was entitled to immediate release as he had served the maximum nonextended term to which he could have been sentenced. The Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois) held the statute authorizing his extended-term sentence was unconstitutional under Apprendi and issued the habeas corpus order. Defendant warden appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was sentenced to concurrent extended terms of 60 years each for armed robbery and armed violence. On direct appeal, he challenged the extended-term sentences on the ground that the sentencing judge did not find any of the aggravating factors listed in the statute. The appellate court had rejected that argument and noted that the record supported an extended term under the Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-3.2(b)(2) (1979) factor that the offense was accompanied by exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty as the prisoner had repeatedly threatened the victim's life with a knife and severely beat her even though she told him she was pregnant. As to the habeas corpus action, the appellate court held Apprendi did not apply retroactively because it was a procedural rule and it was not among those procedures that were implicit in the concept of ordered liberty. The prisoner's direct appeal concluded some 15 years before Apprendi was decided. Nothing in the extended term statute prohibited compliance with Apprendi. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 1005-3.2(b)(2) was not void ab initio. The trial court erred in granting habeas corpus relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

247 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rosenberg


Docket No. 96834


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


213 Ill. 2d 69; 820 N.E.2d 440; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1671; 289 Ill. Dec. 664



November 18, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at People v. Rosenberg, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 220 (Ill. App. Ct., Mar. 7, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
People v. Rosenberg, 341 Ill. App. 3d 893, 793 N.E.2d 939, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 886, 276 Ill. Dec. 180 (Ill. App. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's motion to quash arrest and suppress evidence was denied. A jury found defendant guilty of controlled substance trafficking. The trial court sentenced defendant to 18 years' imprisonment. The appellate court (Illinois) vacated the trial court's order denying defendant's motion to suppress and remanded for a new hearing on the motion. The supreme court granted the State's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: In vacating the trial court's order denying defendant's motion to suppress, the appellate court held that the prosecution deprived defendant of due process by refusing to grant use immunity to a witness at the suppression hearing. In reversing the appellate court, the supreme court concluded that the witness's testimony at the suppression hearing was not necessary to establish any legitimate expectation of privacy in the search of the boxes and seizure of contraband that defendant may have had. The supreme court noted that defendant could have testified at the suppression hearing on the issue of his expectation of privacy in the contents of the boxes without fear that his testimony would later be used to convict him. Although defendant complained that the testimony could have been used to impeach him if he testified at trial, the supreme court held that such alleged inconvenience did not, itself, provide a sufficient basis upon which to insist that the prosecution should have granted the witness use immunity at the suppression hearing so that he could have established defendant's ability to claim a Fourth Amendment violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

248 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Duncan (In re M.M.D.)


Docket No. 97537


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


213 Ill. 2d 105; 820 N.E.2d 392; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1674; 289 Ill. Dec. 616



November 18, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
Johnson v. Duncan (In re M.M.D.), 344 Ill. App. 3d 345, 800 N.E.2d 831, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1373, 279 Ill. Dec. 543 (Ill. App. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father was granted leave to appeal a decision of an appellate court (Illinois), which affirmed a trial court decision that a preexisting agreement granting grandparent visitation rights had not been rendered invalid based on a subsequent finding that the grandparent visitation statute, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/607(b) (2000) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Respondent grandparents were granted visitation rights under a consent order with the father. The father later sought modification of the order or a finding that it was no longer valid. The appellate court certified the question of whether Illinois courts had jurisdiction to enforce a grandparent visitation order entered prior to the decision in Wickham v. Byrne, or whether as a result of that decision, such a visitation agreement was rendered void. The supreme court noted that its basic ruling in Wickham was that the state could not override the decision of a fit parent regarding a child's visitation with grandparents. However, in the instant case, the state had not made that decision. The parties had entered into what was basically a consent decree, which in general could not be modified without the consent of all of the parties. As the agreement was not clearly contrary to public policy, it could not be rendered void on a public policy basis. Further, as the visitation was by agreement, it was not open to scrutiny under the principles stated in Wickham. However, modification was appropriate if there was a finding that modification would be in the grandchild's best interest.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was affirmed.

 

249 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Robert S. (In re Robert S.)


Docket No. 96773


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


213 Ill. 2d 30; 820 N.E.2d 424; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1669; 289 Ill. Dec. 648



November 18, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Robert S. (In re Robert S.), 341 Ill. App. 3d 238, 792 N.E.2d 421, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 856, 275 Ill. Dec. 190 (Ill. App. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent psychiatric patient was found unfit to stand trial in a criminal matter. Petitioner psychiatrist filed a petition seeking involuntary administration of psychotropic medication pursuant to 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-107.1 (2000). The circuit court granted the petition. The patient appealed. The appellate court (Illinois) affirmed. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient contended that the appellate court erred in holding that the patient was subject to the involuntary administration of psychotropic medication for a period not to exceed 90 days. The appellate court found that, because of his mental illness, the patient had exhibited a deterioration of ability to function, suffering, and threatening behavior. Further, the appellate court found that the suggested benefits of the treatment outweighed the potential for harm, the patient lacked the capacity to make a reasoned decision about the treatment, and other less restrictive services had been explored, but were found inappropriate. The supreme court held that the patient was denied due process because the requirements for an independent examination under 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-804 (2000) were not satisfied. In addition, the supreme court held that 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-107.1 (2000) required that notice of the proceeding be given to the patient's criminal defense attorney. The patient was denied a level playing field and a fundamental requirement of due process: the opportunity to be heard in a meaningful manner.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed in part and reversed in part.

In re Marriage of De Bates


Docket No. 97059


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


212 Ill. 2d 489; 819 N.E.2d 714; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1619; 289 Ill. Dec. 218



October 28, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended January 6, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: De Bates v. Bates, 342 Ill. App. 3d 207, 794 N.E.2d 868, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 879, 276 Ill. Dec. 618 (Ill. App. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the appellate court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a decision of the Illinois Appellate Court which affirmed the trial court's order that terminated the mother's custody of the parties' minor child, awarded custody to appellee father, and restricted the mother's visitation rights. The father cross-appealed the denial of his petition to terminate unallocated maintenance and support based on an alleged conjugal relationship between the mother and another man.


OVERVIEW: Custody was granted to the mother, and after both parties and the child went through psychological evaluations, the court-appointed psychologist recommended that custody be given to the father. The mother contended that § 506 of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/506 (2002), was unconstitutional. The court agreed that § 506(a)(3) was unconstitutional as applied because the child's representative's report was adverse to the mother and she was deprived of her due process to cross-examine the witness. However, the court held that the mother presented no evidence to rebut the report and thus it was harmless error. The court also held that whatever the merits of the parental alienation syndrome (PAS) theory, the trial court's ruling was not dependent on any finding that PAS was present. The balance struck by the trial court by not interviewing the child in camera was not an abuse of discretion. As to the father's calling of a surprise witness, the mother did not demonstrate any prejudice resulting from the testimony. Finally, the court held the mother and the other man were in a dating relationship not akin to a marriage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court.

St. Clair County v. Phillips


Docket No. 97280


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


212 Ill. 2d 407; 818 N.E.2d 1231; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1615; 289 Ill. Dec. 28



October 21, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended December 16, 2004.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review as a matter of right, pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 302(a) because the circuit court of St. Clair County (Illinois) declared 55 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-1121 (West 2000) unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The county filed a petition for demolition pursuant to 55 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-1121 (West 2000). Defendants asserted that the statute was unconstitutional, citing Village of Lake Villa v. Stokovich, 334 Ill. App. 3d 488, 778 N.E.2d 750 (2002), in which the appellate court found 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-31-1 (West 1996) unconstitutional. Defendants argued that the authority that was given to county boards in section 5-1121 of the County Code paralleled that which was given to municipalities in section 11-31-1 of the Municipal Code. Specifically, they argued that, under Stokovich, a statute that allowed demolition upon findings that the structure was dangerous and beyond reasonable repair, without allowing repairs, constituted an unlawful taking. Defendants' motion to dismiss was granted. Subsequently, in Village of Lake Villa v. Stokovich, 211 Ill. 2d 106, 810 N.E.2d 13 (2004), the court held that section 11-31-1 of the Municipal Code was not unconstitutional because the procedure was rationally related to the public interest in health and safety and because the method that was chosen to further that interest was reasonable. Therefore, the circuit court's judgment was vacated.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the circuit court and remanded for further proceedings.

Alternate Fuels, Inc. v. Dir. of the Ill. EPA


Docket No. 96071


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


215 Ill. 2d 219; 830 N.E.2d 444; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1616; 294 Ill. Dec. 32



October 21, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on denial of rehearing June 16, 2005.
Modified and rehearing denied by Alternate Fuels, Inc. v. Dir., Ill. EPA, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 953 (Ill., June 16, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Alternate Fuels, Inc. v. Dir. of the Ill. EPA, 337 Ill. App. 3d 857, 786 N.E.2d 1063, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 296, 272 Ill. Dec. 229 (Ill. App. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Illinois Environmental Protection Agency and its director (Agency), appealed a decision by an appellate court (Illinois) affirming summary judgment in favor of appellee company on its declaratory action that its manufacturing processes were not "wastes" under the Illinois Environmental Protection Act, 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1 et seq. (2002). The company challenged summary judgment rejecting its claim for attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The Agency issued a violation notice under § 31(a)(1) of the Act, 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/31(a)(1) (1998), for the company's failure to secure a permit to burn alternate fuel at one of its plants. When the parties could not agree on whether the alternate fuel was "waste" under the Act, the company sought a declaration that the fuel was not waste and for attorney fees under the Illinois Administrative Procedure Act, 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 100/1-1, based on the Agency's allegedly impermissible rule-making. The parties cross-appealed summary judgment for the company on the declaratory action and for the Agency on attorney fees. The Agency argued that the declaratory action was not justiciable and the fuel was "discarded material" under the Act's definition of waste. The court found that the case was ripe and justiciable since an actual controversy existed and hardship would result if the declaratory action were not resolved. Since the fuel was recycled, it was not "discarded" and was not "waste" that would require a permit. The Agency's interpretation of "discarded material" was not a statement of general applicability, so no rule-making occurred to trigger the right to fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both summary judgment rulings.

Canel v. Topinka


Docket No. 96755


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


212 Ill. 2d 311; 818 N.E.2d 311; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1036; 288 Ill. Dec. 623



October 7, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Motion granted by Canel v. Topinka, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1643 (Ill., Nov. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: AC1-01-2069
Canel v. Topinka, 342 Ill. App. 3d 65, 793 N.E.2d 845, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 844, 276 Ill. Dec. 86 (Ill. App. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the appellate court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, director of the Unclaimed Property Division of the Office of the Treasurer of the State of Illinois and State Treasurer, appealed the judgment from the appellate court (Illinois), which determined that dividends from certain abandoned stock were the private property of plaintiff stockholder and remanded the case to the trial court for a determination of just compensation.


OVERVIEW: In 1999, a bank delivered the stockholder's stock to defendants pursuant to the Uniform Disposition of Unclaimed Property Act (Act), 765 Ill. Comp. Stat. 1025/1 et seq. (1998), now 765 Ill. Comp. Stat. 1025/0.05 et seq. ( 2002), as property presumed abandoned under the Act. The stockholder learned of the remittance of the stock to the State in 1999 and submitted a claim for the return of the stock along with any dividends or other accruals that had been issued during the time the State held the stock. The State Treasurer returned the stock, but refused to return the dividends issued on the stock. The stockholder sued, and the trial court dismissed the suit based on the stockholder's failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The appellate court reversed and remanded. On appeal, the court affirmed, first finding that because defendants never chose to exercise their discretion in favor of a claimant, exhaustion of administrative remedies was unnecessary. It then found that § 15 of the Act was not an escheat law and that the State, as the custodian of stock, could not claim that it was entitled to the dividends, which were an incident of ownership and belonged to the stockholder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the appellate court.

People v. Funches


Docket No. 96784


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


212 Ill. 2d 334; 818 N.E.2d 342; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1037; 288 Ill. Dec. 654



October 7, 2004, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Order of the trial court reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Illinois appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which dismissed one count of an information against defendant, charging him with violating 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/4-103.2(b) (2002). Defendant was charged with theft, attempted first degree murder, and aggravated unlawful failure to obey a peace officer's order to stop.


OVERVIEW: Two police officers testified that defendant opened a cash register drawer in a store while the clerk was elsewhere, and he took a deposit bag containing cash. He was chased out of the store and upon passing an automobile with the engine running, he got in and tried to escape, but he was eventually caught. Prior to trial, defendant sought dismissal of the aggravated failure to obey charge, contending that § 4-103.2(b) was unconstitutional because a stolen vehicle was not a rational basis for a separate anti-flight offense, and because it was disproportionate to other offenses. The trial court held that it was unconstitutional on its face and it granted the motion, and after denying the State's motion for reconsideration, the State appealed. The court found that defendant had failed to demonstrate that the inference of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/4-103(a)(1) (2002), which was incorporated in 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/4-103.2(b), violated due process as applied to him. There was no question that defendant's possession of the vehicle was recent, which was a key factor in permitting the inference and upholding its constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

People v. D.D. (In re D.D.)


Docket No. 96467


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


212 Ill. 2d 410; 819 N.E.2d 300; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1023; 289 Ill. Dec. 143



September 23, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Amended December 16, 2004.
Rehearing denied by D.D. v. D.D., 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1677 (Ill., Nov. 22, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. D.D. (In re D.D.), 337 Ill. App. 3d 998, 788 N.E.2d 10, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 910, 272 Ill. Dec. 706 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Appellate Court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Illinois challenged the decision of an appellate court (Illinois), which held that a juvenile court lacked the statutory authority to order appellee school district to pay for the educational portion of appellee delinquent minor's residential placement pursuant to the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/5-740. The delinquent minor was placed in an out-of-state facility as a condition of his probation.


OVERVIEW: The delinquent minor was a special education student within the school district. He was originally placed in an in-state residential facility but was discharged for numerous violations. The delinquent minor's probation officer recommended the out-of-state therapeutic residential placement in view of the delinquent minor's problems with school attendance, counseling, and probation department appointments. An advocacy supervisor from the county juvenile probation department testified that placement at the out-of-state facility was appropriate. The trial court found that the school district was liable for the educational portion of the delinquent minor's residential placement, since the minor's mother resided in that school district. The school district successfully appealed that decision, and the appellate court held that the trial court had no authority to order the school district to pay for such placement. The court agreed and held that the school district was financially liable only if it was unable to meet a special education student's needs, which was not the case. The placement of the delinquent minor was solely under the Juvenile Court Act, not the school code.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Valdivia v. Izaguirre (In re John M.)


Docket Nos. 97227, 97327 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


212 Ill. 2d 253; 817 N.E.2d 500; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1024; 288 Ill. Dec. 142



September 23, 2004, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment of the trial court reversed; cause remanded to that court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a mother and the attorney general, appealed from an order of the Kane County Circuit Court (Illinois) holding the Illinois Parentage Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 45/1 et seq. (2000), unconstitutional and dismissing with prejudice a petition to determine a father-child relationship brought by plaintiff petitioner.


OVERVIEW: The issue the supreme court faced was whether § 7(a) of the Act, codified at 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 45/7(a) (2002), was facially invalid to the extent that it permits, without a prior best interests hearing, a paternity action to be brought by a man alleging himself to be the biological father of a child who was born during the marriage of the mother to another man. Appellee husband argued that, by not providing for a preliminary best interests hearing, the statute was unconstitutional because it permitted the automatic invasion of an intact family by a stranger and allowed an interloper to involuntarily invade the marital relationship and impugn its integrity. The supreme court held that the husband failed to carry his burden of clearly showing that in all instances the failure to hold a best interests hearing before allowing a paternity action to proceed would be unconstitutional. The situations proposed by the husband made numerous assumptions and suggested various situations wherein the statute might be unconstitutionally applied. In addition, the husband's arguments regarding the social and public policy of the Act were better left for the legislature than to the courts.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Botruff


Docket No. 94334


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


212 Ill. 2d 166; 817 N.E.2d 463; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1019; 288 Ill. Dec. 105



September 23, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 29, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Botruff, 331 Ill. App. 3d 486, 771 N.E.2d 570, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 471, 264 Ill. Dec. 866 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In connection with a mandatory reexamination procedure under the Illinois Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/1 et seq. (2000), respondent requested the appointment of an independent evaluator. The circuit court denied the request. Respondent appealed. The Illinois Court of Appeals reversed the decision. The State petitioned for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Following the completion of his sentence for criminal sexual assault, respondent was committed to the Illinois Department of Human Services. In connection with a mandatory reexamination procedure under the Illinois Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, respondent, who did not attend a probable cause hearing, requested through his attorney the appointment of an independent evaluator. The circuit court denied the request, and, based on the examining expert's report, found that respondent remained a sexually violent person and that no probable cause existed to warrant a hearing on the issue. On appeal, the supreme court found that the appointment of an independent examiner in periodic examination proceedings was controlled by 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/55(a) (2000) of the Act and was left to the discretion of the circuit court. Further, respondent was not denied equal protection by operation of section 55(a). Lastly, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/65(b)(1) (2000) of the Act, which prohibited committed persons from attending limited probable cause hearings, did not violate due process. The appellate court judgment was therefore improper, and the circuit court decision was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed, and the judgment of the circuit court denying the appointment of an independent evaluator was affirmed.

 

258 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


City of Urbana v. Andrew N.B.


Docket Nos 95408, 95803 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


211 Ill. 2d 456; 813 N.E.2d 132; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 990; 286 Ill. Dec. 75



June 24, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
City of Urbana v. Andrew N.B., 335 Ill. App. 3d 180, 780 N.E.2d 765, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1077, 269 Ill. Dec. 293 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgments reversed; circuit court judgments vacated; causes remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In separate actions, defendant juveniles pled guilty to violated municipal ordinances and received dispositions of court supervision. When they violated the terms of their supervision, the cities filed contempt petitions. The trial court found the minors in contempt and sentenced them to detention. The appellate court (Illinois) affirmed. The juveniles' appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/5-125 (2002) violated equal protection because it allowed municipalities to treat similarly situated minors differently by allowing them to choose arbitrarily between referring ordinance violations involving minors to the State for prosecution under the Illinois Juvenile Court Act, which offered procedural protections, or filing their own complaint under the Illinois Municipal Code, which offered no such protections. The supreme court held that § 5-125 did not violate equal protection as the differential in treatment was not arbitrary. Defendants also argued that their uncounseled guilty pleas violated due process. Since defendants did not receive sentences of detention, or even probation, the supreme court concluded that they were not entitled to appointed counsel when they pled guilty. However, the supreme court did hold that in the absence of a statute allowing such a procedure, contempt could not be used as punishment for minors who violated orders of supervision entered on municipal ordinance violations which themselves did not permit imprisonment. The cities improperly attempted to expand the sentencing options available.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's decisions were reversed, the circuit courts' orders finding the juveniles in contempt and sentencing them to detention was reversed, and the causes were remanded to the circuit court to allow the cities to file petitions to revoke supervision or to request that the State file delinquency petitions in these cases.

 

259 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Santos


Docket No. 94620


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


211 Ill. 2d 395; 813 N.E.2d 159; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 992; 286 Ill. Dec. 102



June 24, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Santos v. Ill., 2005 U.S. LEXIS 669 (U.S., Jan. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
People v. Santos, 333 Ill. App. 3d 1, 774 N.E.2d 473, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 714, 266 Ill. Dec. 367 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; judgment of the trial court affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual abuse in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-16(d) (1998). The circuit court sentenced defendant to a four-year prison term. The appellate court (Illinois) reversed defendant's conviction. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the appellate court erred in reversing the trial court's order barring defendant from cross-examining the victim about her inconsistent statements regarding whether she had engaged in sexual activities with anyone else during the 72 hours preceding the assault. The State contended that the trial court properly excluded such evidence. The supreme court held that the rape shield statute, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-7 (1998), did not provide an exception which applied to said testimony. The testimony defendant sought to introduce was not regarding prior sexual activity between himself and the victim, nor was the introduction of the testimony constitutionally required. As none of the exceptions in § 115-7 applied, the trial court properly precluded defendant from introducing said evidence.


OUTCOME: The circuit court ruling prohibiting defendant from introducing evidence of the victim's prior sexual activity was correct. That portion of the appellate court opinion which reversed that ruling was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

260 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Huddleston


Docket No. 96367


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


212 Ill. 2d 107; 816 N.E.2d 322; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 980; 287 Ill. Dec. 560



June 4, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 29, 2004.
Rehearing denied by People v. Huddleston, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1032 (Ill., Oct. 4, 2004)
Related proceeding at Doe v. Huddleston, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 26197 (C.D. Ill., May 4, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois) of three counts of predatory criminal sexual assault pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-14.1(a)(1) (2002). The circuit court determined that § 12-14.1(b)(1.2) was unconstitutional as applied to defendant in that it violated the proportionate penalties clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, and sentenced him to consecutive 10-year sentences. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The convictions were based on allegations that defendant, who was a teacher, sexually assaulted three different students. Reversing the finding that § 12-14.1(b)(1.2) was unconstitutional as applied to defendant, the state supreme court held that § 12-14.1(b)(1.2) did not violate the proportionate penalties clause. The state supreme court found that the mandatory penalty of a natural life sentence was not cruel, degrading, or disproportionate to the offenses committed because (1) defendant committed sexual assaults against three victims, one more than the minimum § 12-14.1(b)(1.2) required; (2) defendant had previously committed a "sex offense;" (3) the commission of the subject offenses appeared to have been the result of planning and well-orchestrated execution, on two separate dates, a month apart; and (4) even if defendant was truly remorseful, that was hardly a determinative factor with respect to the prospect of rehabilitation. Moreover, the court rejected defendant's suggested proportionality comparison to the offense of aggravated battery of a child because the two different offenses did not share a common statutory purpose and involved different kinds of injuries.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the circuit court's decision and remanded the case.

 

261 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Mattis v. State Univs. Ret. Sys.


Docket Nos. 96012, 96114 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


212 Ill. 2d 58; 816 N.E.2d 303; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 676; 287 Ill. Dec. 541



May 20, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Rehearing denied by Mattis v. State Univs. Ret. Sys., 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1031 (Ill., Oct. 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Mattis v. State Univs. Retirement Sys., 296 Ill. App. 3d 675, 695 N.E.2d 566, 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 341, 231 Ill. Dec. 49 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, vacated in part, remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court ruled that state pension law required a one-time early retirement option contribution from the employer to be taken into account when calculating appellee retired professor's retirement annuity. The trial court then ruled his attorneys were entitled to attorney fees and expenses and dismissed four counts of his third-amended complaint. Appellant state university retirement system appealed and he cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The retired professor elected to retire from the state university under the early retirement provisions of 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/15-136.2 (1992). To avoid a reduction in his retirement annuity, that law authorized him to make a one-time contribution to the state university retirement system. The law also stated that if the employee elected to make that early retirement option (ERO) contribution, the employer was obligated to contribute a lump sum to the system. The retired professor did not make an employee ERO contribution. Instead, the state university, made both the employee and employer contributions. The state university retirement system did not take into account the lump sum payment in calculating his retirement annuity. He sued to challenge the annuity calculation. The trial court agreed with the state university retirement system's calculation, but the appellate court disagreed with it. On appeal, the state supreme court found statutory interpretation of the state pension law did not require that the state university retirement system take into account the state university's one-time early retirement option contribution in calculating his retirement annuity.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's ruling that an early retirement option contribution had to be taken into account in calculating retirement benefits under statutory law regarding retirement annuities was reversed. Also, the trial court's judgment awarding attorney fees and expenses to the retired professor's attorneys was reversed, while its dismissal of the retired professor's other claims was affirmed. Also, the cause was remanded with directions.

 

262 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Jorgensen v. Blagojevich


Docket Nos. 97624, 97656 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


211 Ill. 2d 286; 811 N.E.2d 652; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 680; 285 Ill. Dec. 165



May 20, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Amended July 15, 2004.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Illinois Governor and the Comptroller, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which was in favor of plaintiff class of judges and held that 2001 Ill. Laws 607 was invalid for violating Ill. Const. art. VI, § 14, and that Illinois judges were entitled to receive cost-of-living-adjustments (COLAs) as a component of their salaries for 2003 and 2004.


OVERVIEW: The Compensation Review Board determined in 1990 that judge salaries should include COLAs, which were to be annually adjusted. The General Assembly suspended the COLAs implemented by Senate Joint Resolution 192. This was deemed a violation of Ill. Const. art. VI, § 14 and was remedied by new legislation for COLA payments in 2003. The Governor signed a reduction veto to the COLA-authorizing legislation for 2004 in order to prevent the COLA from being implemented, as well as a veto of the bill for 2003 COLAs. The Comptroller was ordered to make the payments upon the court's finding that the veto was unconstitutional, however, he refused. A class action by judges was brought against them. The trial court found that the elimination of the COLAs was unconstitutional, and it ordered payment to the class of judges. On appeal, the court found that the COLAs were fully vested since 1990 and accordingly, efforts to prevent receipt of them violated Ill. Const. art. VI, § 14. Accordingly, 2001 Ill. Laws 607 was invalid, as was the reduction veto. A defense of legislative immunity was inapplicable. The judiciary had authority to compel payment without a specific appropriation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

263 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Townsell


Docket No. 95725


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


209 Ill. 2d 543; 809 N.E.2d 103; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 669; 283 Ill. Dec. 910



April 15, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Townsell v. Illinois, 543 U.S. 1056, 125 S. Ct. 862, 160 L. Ed. 2d 781, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 540 (U.S., Jan. 10, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
People v. Townsell, 336 Ill. App. 3d 340, 783 N.E.2d 164, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 6, 270 Ill. Dec. 589 (Ill. App. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Appellate Court judgment reversed; Circuit Court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to first-degree murder. The Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois) imposed an extended-term sentence of 100 years in prison. The appellate court (Illinois) reduced defendant's sentence to 60 years, finding that the imposition of an extended-term violated Apprendi. The state supreme court allowed the State's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issue was whether an Apprendi claim that was waived pursuant to a guilty plea could nevertheless be considered on appeal under the plain error exception to the waiver rule. The state supreme court concluded that the appellate court erred in using Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(a)'s plain error rule as a means of reaching defendant's Apprendi-based sentencing claims because Apprendi-based sentencing objections could not be heard on appeal from a guilty plea. Moreover, Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(a) did not speak to waivers that resulted from the voluntary relinquishment of known rights, as in the case of a guilty plea. Thus, the appellate court had no authority to forgo the administrative convenience of waiver and reach the merits of defendant's Apprendi claims, as administrative convenience had absolutely nothing to do with the waiver at issue in the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed, and the judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

 

264 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Arvia v. Madigan


Docket No. 95590


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


209 Ill. 2d 520; 809 N.E.2d 88; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 671; 283 Ill. Dec. 895; 34 A.L.R.6th 803



April 15, 2004, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment of the Circuit Court reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Illinois sought review of a decision of an Illinois circuit court, which granted appellee driver's motion for summary judgment, holding that 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-501.8 (2000) was unconstitutional on its face. The circuit court also denied the State's motion to vacate that judgment.


OVERVIEW: The driver, who was under 21 years of age, was stopped for a traffic violation. He was asked to submit to a blood alcohol test under § 11-501.8, commonly referred to as the "zero tolerance law." The driver refused to submit to a test, resulting in the summary suspension of his driving privileges. The suspension was upheld by the Illinois Secretary of State. Rather than seek further review, the driver filed his action seeking a declaration that § 11-501.8 was unconstitutional. The circuit ruled in the driver's favor, leading to the State's appeal. The supreme court reversed. Persons faced with summary suspension of driving privileges under the zero tolerance law were not similarly situated with persons faced with summary suspension for driving while under the influence (DUI) for purposes of equal protection. Thus, equal protection did not require the driver to be afforded the same type of judicial hearing to contest the summary suspension as he would have had for a DUI arrest. Further, the administrative hearing process under the zero tolerance law afforded the driver with substantially the same due process as a DUI judicial hearing and was not constitutionally unsound.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was reversed.

 

265 of 2788 DOCUMENTS



People v. Einoder


Docket Nos. 95942, 95943, 95944 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


209 Ill. 2d 443; 808 N.E.2d 517; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 377; 283 Ill. Dec. 551



April 1, 2004, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged, in three separate indictments, with criminal disposal of waste under 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/44(p)(1)(A) (2000). The Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, granted defendants' motion to dismiss each of the indictments, finding that § 44(p)(1)(A) was unconstitutionally vague. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants allegedly accepted for disposal more than 250 cubic feet of concrete without the permit required by 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/21(d); one defendant was charged with allowing "clean construction or demolition debris" to be deposited above grade without a permit. The trial court held that 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/44(p)(1)(A) was unconstitutionally vague because the term "grade" was not defined and the definition of "waste" was not sufficiently definite to allow ordinary people to understand what conduct was prohibited. The supreme court held that as § 44(p)(1)(A) did not implicate First Amendment rights and defendants did not allege the statute was incapable of any valid application, they had no standing to assert a facial vagueness challenge, and the trial court erred in finding § 44(p)(1)(A) unconstitutionally vague on that basis. The trial court did not find the statute incapable of any valid application, and defendants presented no evidence demonstrating how the disputed statutory sections were vague as applied to their conduct. On remand, the trial court was to reassess the validity of the statutory sections after the parties presented a proper evidentiary basis.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Wexler v. Wirtz Corp.


Docket Nos. 94127, 94128, 94171 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


211 Ill. 2d 18; 809 N.E.2d 1240; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 383; 284 Ill. Dec. 294



April 1, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Rehearing denied by Wexler v. Wirtz Corp., 2004 Ill. LEXIS 995 (Ill., May 24, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; cause remanded with directions to dismiss.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the owners of a retail liquor store, a liquor distributor, and three officials of the State of Illinois, appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held that 1999 Ill. Laws 38, which amended provisions of the Liquor Control Act, the State Finance Act, and the School Construction Law, was unconstitutional. Plaintiffs, a class of taxpayers cross-appealed.

The taxpayer who headed the class challenged the law as a retail purchaser of vodka. The trial court ruled that the statute violated the three readings rule and the single subject clauses of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d) (1970). Without reaching the constitutional question, the Illinois Supreme Court reversed on a finding of lack of standing, holding that (1) the taxpayer paid the increased price voluntarily; (2) the taxpayer could not establish payment of the tax under implied duress because vodka was not an essential good and he went forward with a purchase of vodka with full knowledge of the tax; (3) the distributor was the only entity eligible to protest the tax under the State Officers and Employees Money Disposition Act, 30 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 230/1 et seq. (2000), and it had made it clear it had not desire to do so, and (4) even if the taxpayer could have sought a refund under the Act, he had failed to comply with the procedures set out in the Act for seeking a refund.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with directions that the cause be dismissed.

Fritz v. Johnston


Docket No. 96325


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


209 Ill. 2d 302; 807 N.E.2d 461; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 367; 282 Ill. Dec. 837



March 18, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 12, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Fritz v. Johnston, 205 Ill. 2d 580, 803 N.E.2d 481, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1437, 281 Ill. Dec. 77 (Ill., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state employee sued defendant state employees, alleging they conspired to force him out of his job and that he endured mental anguish and derogation of his name and reputation as a result of their actions. The Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) granted defendants' motion to dismiss. A divided appellate court (Illinois) affirmed the dismissal. The state supreme court granted plaintiff's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Two defendants filed charges with the state police, accusing plaintiff of threatening them with physical violence. Plaintiff claimed these charges were false at the time they were made. Plaintiff claimed that the other two defendants conspired to force him out of his job with a threat of a state police investigation. On appeal, the primary issue was whether the doctrine of sovereign immunity deprived circuit courts of jurisdiction over claims that state employees engaged in civil conspiracy in the furtherance of which unlawful acts were committed. The state supreme court concluded that the doctrine of sovereign immunity was not designed to shield state employees from being held accountable for their criminal actions. Thus, the first two defendants were not immune from plaintiff's suit. Nor was sovereign immunity intended to shield even otherwise lawful actions by state employees, when those actions were committed in the furtherance of a conspiracy. Thus, the second two defendants were not protected by the doctrine. However, plaintiff failed to allege any facts from which the existence of a conspiracy could be inferred with respect to the second two defendants.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed in part the judgment of the appellate court which dismissed the two counts of plaintiff's complaint against the first two defendants, but affirmed in part the judgment of the appellate court which dismissed the two counts against the second two defendants. The cause was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Lyon v. Dep't of Children & Family Servs.


Docket No. 95643


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


209 Ill. 2d 264; 807 N.E.2d 423; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 361; 282 Ill. Dec. 799



March 18, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Lyon v. Dep't of Children & Family Servs., 335 Ill. App. 3d 376, 780 N.E.2d 748, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1071, 269 Ill. Dec. 276 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Appellate Court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee teacher challenged an indicated report of sexual abuse against a student and requested expungement of the report from the Illinois State Central Register. Appellant Illinois Department of Children and Family Services denied the request. On requested administrative review by the teacher, the circuit court set aside the Department's decision. The Illinois Court of Appeals affirmed the circuit court's judgment. The Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The teacher was a choral director at a high school. The Department received a report that he had abused two students. The Department completed its investigation and determined that a report of abuse by the teacher was indicated. The indicated report was entered into the Illinois State Central Register shortly thereafter. The teacher alleged that several actions by the Department violated his due process rights. The appellate court held that the teacher's due process rights were violated by a combination of the Department's use of the credible-evidence standard of proof with the Department's failure to strictly comply with its statutory and regulatory deadlines in processing the administrative appeal. The supreme court found that the Department violated the teacher's due process rights through the combination of the Department's use of the low credible-evidence standard to indicate the report against the teacher and to deny his first-stage appeal and through the delays in the provision of the hearing and of the final administrative decision. Thus, the appellate court properly affirmed the expungement of the indicated reports against the teacher from the Central Register.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court expunging the indicated findings of sexual abuse by the teacher was affirmed.

Vill. of Lake Villa v. Stokovich


Docket No. 95118


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


211 Ill. 2d 106; 810 N.E.2d 13; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 356; 284 Ill. Dec. 360



February 20, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Vill. of Lake Villa v. Stokovich, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 999 (Ill., May 24, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Stokovich v. Lake Villa, 543 U.S. 943, 125 S. Ct. 354, 160 L. Ed. 2d 256, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 6976 (U.S., Oct. 18, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
Vill. of Lake Villa v. Stokovich, 334 Ill. App. 3d 488, 778 N.E.2d 750, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 970, 268 Ill. Dec. 484 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Appellate Court judgment reversed and Circuit Court order vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Village of Lake Villa sought review of a judgment of an Illinois appellate court, which ruled that 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-31-1 (1996) violated due process. That decision was rendered in defendant property owner's appeal of a demolition order entered by a circuit court pursuant to § 11-31-1.


OVERVIEW: The Village provided § 11-31-1 notice to the owners that a building they owned either had to be brought into building code conformance or demolished. The owners failed to act, and the Village sought the demolition order. The circuit court issued the order, finding that the building was unsafe and that it would require substantial renovation. The appellate court then found § 11-31-1 unconstitutional. The Illinois Supreme Court disagreed, holding that (1) the owners' failure to timely comply with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 19 was not fatal to their constitutional attack on 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-31-1 (1996), and the owners had standing to bring their constitutional claim; (2) § 11-31-1 was an exercise of state police power subject to the rational basis level of scrutiny; (3) § 11-31-1 provided the owners with procedural due process; (4) § 11-31-1, as construed by the supreme court in a prior decision, was a constitutional exercise of police power; (5) demolition of property under § 11-31-1 was not an unconstitutional taking; but (6) the circuit court's order had to be vacated because its finding that the building was beyond reasonable repair was not supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was reversed and the circuit court's order was vacated. The case was remanded for further proceedings in the circuit court.

 

270 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Stroud


Docket No. 94823


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


208 Ill. 2d 398; 804 N.E.2d 510; 2004 Ill. LEXIS 4; 281 Ill. Dec. 545



January 23, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
People v. Stroud, 333 Ill. App. 3d 416, 775 N.E.2d 1038, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 729, 266 Ill. Dec. 966 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered a guilty plea to possession of a stolen motor vehicle. He appeared in the courtroom only via closed circuit television. Later, defendant's probation for that conviction was revoked because of a subsequent offense. Eventually, defendant filed a postconviction petition, seeking to vacate his plea. The trial court denied the motion. The Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District, vacated both convictions. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The intermediate appellate court found that nothing barred defendant from collaterally attacking his plea in a postconviction proceeding on constitutional grounds. The intermediate appellate court then found that defendant's guilty plea over closed circuit television violated his constitutional right to be present at a critical stage of the proceeding. The appellate court ruled that a guilty plea did not waive a contention that the plea itself was involuntary because of faulty admonishments. Such claims could be raised for the first time in a postconviction petition. An appearance at a guilty plea proceeding via closed circuit television was constitutionally permissible only if the accused waived the right to physical presence on the record after being advised of his right to be present. Here, defendant did not specifically waive his right to be bodily in the courtroom. Defendant's physical presence would have contributed to the fairness of the proceeding, and thus, his due process right to be present at the proceeding was violated. An admonishment about the right to be physically present should have been given at the beginning of the guilty plea proceeding.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed.

Bd. of Trs. v. Coopers & Lybrand


Docket No. 94676


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


208 Ill. 2d 259; 803 N.E.2d 460; 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2610; 281 Ill. Dec. 56



December 18, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
Bd. of Trs. v. Coopers & Lybrand, L.L.P., 333 Ill. App. 3d 225, 775 N.E.2d 55, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 645, 266 Ill. Dec. 493 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant accounting firm sought review of a decision of an appellate court (Illinois). That decision affirmed a trial court judgment in favor of plaintiff, a community college board of trustees, in an action seeking damages for the firm's failure to discover and report inappropriate investments as part of the audit reports the firm prepared. The board appealed the trial court's application of comparative fault to the verdict.


OVERVIEW: During an audit, the firm failed to inform the board of the improper investments being made by the treasurer of a group of city colleges. The case originally included a second accounting firm, but a settlement was reached with that firm prior to trial. The jury returned a verdict in favor of the board. The damages were reduced based on the board's contributory fault, as limited by the audit interference doctrine. The trial court refused to allow a setoff of the prior settlement amount. The appellate court affirmed. The Illinois Supreme Court reversed in part, holding that (1) the extension of comparative fault concepts in connection with professional services under 225 Ill. Comp. Comp. Stat. Ann. 100/0.01 et seq. (1994).


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the appellate court's affirmance of the denial of a setoff and remanded the case to the trial court with directions to credit the firm with the full amount of the settlement with the joint tortfeasor. The supreme court otherwise affirmed the appellate court's decision.

People v. T.F. (In re Andrea F.)


Docket No. 93595


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


208 Ill. 2d 148; 802 N.E.2d 782; 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2608; 280 Ill. Dec. 531



December 18, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. T.F. (In re Andrea F.), 327 Ill. App. 3d 1072, 764 N.E.2d 1281, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 145, 262 Ill. Dec. 164 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of appellate court reversed; judgment of circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the State and the Department of Children and Family Services (DCFS), appealed from a judgment of the appellate court (Illinois) reversing the circuit court's order terminating the parental rights of appellee father and appointing the DCFS as guardian of the child with the power to consent to adoption.


OVERVIEW: The first issue before the supreme court was whether the father's appeal was moot since he had executed a surrender of his parental rights several days prior to consideration of his appeal. The supreme court concluded that the appeal was not moot because the question of whether circuit courts were required, under former 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/1-5(3), to admonish parents that they risked termination of parental rights if the failed to cooperate with the DCFS was one of public importance, and the circumstances were likely to recur. As for the father's argument that the circuit court denied him due process by failing to admonish him that he risked losing his parental rights if he failed to cooperate with the DCFS, the supreme court concluded that he was not, based on the former law which was applicable in his case. Among other things, the supreme court noted that the risk that the father was erroneously deprived of his parental interest as a result of the failure to give the admonishment in question was minimal because the record amply demonstrated that the father was aware of the need to cooperate with the DCFS and that his parental rights could be terminated.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and that of the circuit court was affirmed.

Vuagniaux v. Dep't of Prof'l Regulation


Docket No. 94073


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


208 Ill. 2d 173; 802 N.E.2d 1156; 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2279; 280 Ill. Dec. 635



November 20, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Vuagniaux v. Dep't of Prof'l Regulation, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1005 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2004)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Illinois Department of Professional Regulation appealed directly from a Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) judgment in plaintiff chiropractor's consolidated actions seeking declaratory and injunctive relief and review of a Department decision reprimanding and imposing penalties on the chiropractor for violating 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 60/26 (1998). The trial court had found several sections of the statute unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The chiropractor's advertisements indicated he was a certified brain stem specialist. Since there was no certification board in medicine or chiropractic for that specialty (it was a program at his training college), the Illinois Medical Disciplinary Board commenced a proceeding against him, based on the Department's argument that the claims were misleading. When the chiropractor objected to the chiropractic representative on the Board, the Board nominated a temporary substitute, although the chiropractor did not approve of him either. The high court held that because the substitution was not made with the approval of the Governor, as required by 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 60/7 (1998), the disciplinary decision was invalid. The proper remedy was remand for reconsideration by a legally constituted Board. For guidance in further proceedings, the high court also considered the chiropractor's constitutional arguments. Most of these required further development on remand, but the high court did uphold the constitutionality of the composition of the Board, with only one chiropractor, as well as the fairness of procedures used in disciplinary proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the determination that the imposition of discipline was invalid, but instead of granting the relief sought by the chiropractor, it reversed the remedial portion of the judgment and remanded the matter to the Department for reconsideration by a properly constituted medical disciplinary board.

Poole v. Clausen (In re Estate of Poole)


Docket No. 93872


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


207 Ill. 2d 393; 799 N.E.2d 250; 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1492; 278 Ill. Dec. 532



October 17, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
Poole v. Clausen (In re Estate of Poole), 328 Ill. App. 3d 964, 767 N.E.2d 855, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 242, 263 Ill. Dec. 129 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Putnam County (Illinois) which denied his petition to revoke letters of administration issued to respondent maternal grandmother. The Illinois Appellate Court reversed the circuit court's order and remanded the cause for a hearing. The Illinois Supreme Court granted the grandmother's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The father had a conjugal relationship with the grandmother's daughter. The daughter, eight months pregnant, was killed in a car wreck. The fetus was stillborn. The grandmother settled a claim with the car's insurer and then sought court approval to execute the settlement and distribute the proceeds. The father thereafter filed a petition to revoke the letters of administration. He asserted he was the baby's natural father and, as such, was entitled to priority in the granting of letters of administration. The supreme court held it was correct for a probate estate to be created. However, 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-2 (1998) had no relevance in determining whether the father was a "parent" within the meaning of 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3 (1998) such that he took precedence over the grandmother for purposes of administering the baby's estate. The supreme court agreed with the appellate court, albeit for different reasons, that a hearing to determine whether the father was the baby's natural father was appropriate. It rejected the contention that, because stillborn fetuses never live, illegitimate fathers of stillborns could not establish themselves as "eligible parents."


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.

 

275 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Van Meter v. Darien Park Dist.


Docket No. 90541


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


207 Ill. 2d 359; 799 N.E.2d 273; 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1499; 278 Ill. Dec. 555



October 17, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
Van Meter v. City of Darien, 316 Ill. App. 3d 1300, 779 N.E.2d 526, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 4676, 268 Ill. Dec. 912 (Ill. App. Ct., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sued defendants, cities, city organizations, and others, alleging that surface water flooded their home upon completion of an adjacent municipal recreation area. The municipal defendants moved to dismiss, alleging that they were entitled to discretionary immunity. The trial court granted the motions, and the Illinois Court of Appeals affirmed. The state supreme court granted leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: In the motions to dismiss pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-619(a)(9) (1998), the municipal defendants argued that they were entitled to discretionary immunity under § 2-201 of the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 10/2-201 (1998). The appellate court held that the trial court erred in granting the motions to dismiss. "Discretionary" actions for purposes of section 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 10/2-201 (1998) immunity were defined as actions unique to a particular public office. There was a distinction between situations involving the making of a policy choice and the exercise of discretion. The municipal defendants were required to establish both of these elements in order to invoke immunity. The appellate court held that the municipal defendants failed to prove either element. It was not apparent on the face of complaint that the municipal defendants' actions and omissions were the result of a policy decision. The municipal defendants failed to show that their actions were discretionary, as it was not apparent on the face of the complaint that the municipal defendants' actions were unique to their particular offices.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

 

276 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Allen v. Woodfield Chevrolet, Inc.


Docket No. 94814


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


208 Ill. 2d 12; 802 N.E.2d 752; 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1493; 280 Ill. Dec. 501



October 17, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
Allen v. Woodfield Chevrolet, Inc., 332 Ill. App. 3d 605, 773 N.E.2d 1145, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 543, 266 Ill. Dec. 75 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant car dealership appealed a decision of an appellate court (Illinois), which reversed a trial court decision that had found no constitutional infirmity in certain amendments to the Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act, 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 505/1 et seq. (1996). Specifically, the trial court held that certain amendments to 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 505/10a (1996) did not violate Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff car buyer sued the dealership in connection with the purchase of a used vehicle but failed to comply with certain presuit notice requirements of the Act. The trial court held against the buyer and the appellate court reversed, holding that Ill. Pub. Act 87-1140 (1993) and Ill. Pub. Act 89-144 (1996), which amended 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 505/10a (1996), violated the constitutional prohibition against special legislation, Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13. On appeal, the court agreed that the amendments were unconstitutional. 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 505/10a (1996), as amended, divided consumer fraud plaintiffs into two groups, those defrauded by vehicle dealers, who were subject to the statutory amendments, and all other defrauded consumers who were not subject to the amendments. At bottom, the amendments placed vehicle dealers on more advantageous footing than all other retailers subject to the Act, thus creating a favored class. The statutory amendments were not simply part of the legislature's ongoing regulation of automobile sales and, rather than protecting consumers from unethical business practices of vehicle dealers, protected vehicle dealers from legitimate claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court, which had invalidated the subject amendments.
