Evans v. Shannon


Docket No. 92238


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


201 Ill. 2d 424; 776 N.E.2d 1184; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 375; 267 Ill. Dec. 533



August 29, 2002, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] On direct appeal, trial court's judgment was reversed and cause was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant car owner sought review of the judgment of the Illinois circuit court finding that the car owner and defendants, driver and the driver's employer, were jointly liable in plaintiff parents' wrongful death and survivor actions.


OVERVIEW: The parents' son died when his vehicle collided with a car negligently driven by the driver. The driver was an employee of the employer, who had a vehicle detailing and cleaning business. The driver, acting in his capacity as an employee of the employer, had driven the car owner's car to the employer's place of business. The car was locked up for the night. After regular business hours, the driver returned to the shop and, without authority, took the car for his own use. The driver was intoxicated when he struck the son's vehicle. The parents alleged negligent entrustment against the car owner. The parents failed to establish the elements of negligent entrustment. There was no reason that the car owner knew or should have known that the driver was unlicensed or incompetent. Evidence that the car owner knew of six or seven detours that workers for the employer had taken over several years fell short of establishing the evidence necessary under this element. The car owner did not give express or implied permission to the driver to drive the vehicle at the time of the accident. The driver was only given permission to drive the vehicle to the employer's place of business.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

317 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ballard


Docket No. 88885


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


206 Ill. 2d 151; 794 N.E.2d 788; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 376; 276 Ill. Dec. 538



August 29, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified Upon Denial of Rehearing December 2, 2002.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ballard v. Illinois, 540 U.S. 833, 124 S. Ct. 81, 157 L. Ed. 2d 61, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 6205 (2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Ballard v. Pierce, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 39431 (N.D. Ill., May 30, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) for first degree murder, robbery, concealment of a homicidal death, unlawful possession of a stolen motor vehicle, and armed robbery. After hearing aggravation and mitigation testimony, the trial judge sentenced defendant to death for the first-degree murder conviction. The trial judge imposed additional sentences, to be served concurrently.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered an acquaintance in order to get money to buy drugs. The primary evidence used by the State against defendant came from his own admissions to his family, friends, and to police. The appellate court held that prior to or at the time of defendant's videotaped crime scene statement, there was not such a constitutionally significant degree of prosecutorial involvement as to trigger defendant's U.S. Const. amend. Defendant's statements to the police were voluntary. There were no sufficient mitigating factors to preclude the imposition of the death penalty. The trial court considered and weighed all the evidence presented before it. In addition, the evidence presented in aggravation and mitigation was not closely balanced. A detailed account regarding defendant's attack on another victim was irrelevant victim impact testimony. However, it did not so prejudice defendant. The Illinois death penalty statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Munson


Docket No. 88799


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


206 Ill. 2d 104; 794 N.E.2d 155; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 334; 276 Ill. Dec. 260



June 20, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Munson, 171 Ill. 2d 158, 662 N.E.2d 1265, 1996 Ill. LEXIS 16, 215 Ill. Dec. 125 (1996)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Post-conviction court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, armed robbery, aggravated kidnapping, and arson. Defendant waived a jury for sentencing and was sentenced to death on the murder conviction and to concurrent prison terms on the other convictions. The trial court denied defendant's post-trial motions. The State's motion to dismiss defendant's post-conviction petition was granted. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In response to defendant's assignments of error on appeal from his conviction and death sentence, the supreme court held (1) that trial counsel's failure to raise a Batson claim was not an error since it had no merit based on the prosecutor's indication that when she used her peremptory challenge she believed the subject venireperson was Caucasian; (2) that probable cause existed for defendant's warrantless arrest based on informant's information and, thus, trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to file a motion to quash the arrest; (3) that trial counsel was not professionally deficient for failing to present additional mitigation evidence where the proffered evidence was cumulative and defendant failed to establish that a reasonable probability existed that the trial court would not have imposed the death penalty had this evidence been presented at sentencing; and (4) that post-conviction counsel was not ineffective under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c), since there was no evidence showing or even suggesting that a witness was rewarded for testimony or that counsel should have requested further discovery.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and death sentence were affirmed.

People v. Lindsey


Docket No. 89138


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


201 Ill. 2d 45; 772 N.E.2d 1268; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 336; 265 Ill. Dec. 616



June 20, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
 People v. Lindsey, 309 Ill. App. 3d 1031, 243 Ill. Dec. 538, 723 N.E.2d 841, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 27 (3d Dist. 2000).



DISPOSITION: Court of appeals' judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court rejected defendant's argument, in a case where he was convicted on two drug possession charges, that his appearances in the trial court through closed circuit television at the time of arraignment and jury waiver violated his constitutional and statutory rights to be present. It then affirmed his convictions and sentences. The state supreme court allowed defendant's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Police officers executed a search warrant, and recovered drugs and drug paraphernalia. Defendant was arrested. He was then arraigned. Defendant was represented by counsel, who was present in the courtroom. Defendant, however, appeared via closed circuit television from a jail. Defense counsel acknowledged receipt of the indictment and requested a jury trial. Defendant then "appeared" at eight pretrial hearings via the closed circuit television. He decided to waive his right to a jury trial. The trial court, speaking to defendant across the closed circuit system, admonished defendant regarding his right to a jury trial. Finding that defendant understood his right to trial by jury and was voluntarily giving it up, the trial court accepted his jury waiver. When defendant wanted to speak to his attorney privately, his counsel left the courtroom and contacted defendant by telephone. Defendant was convicted. The appellate court affirmed his conviction and sentence. After it entered its decision, the state supreme court found the record did not show his courtroom absence denied him any constitutional or statutory right, or contributed to make the proceedings against him unfair.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Harris


Docket No. 89796


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


206 Ill. 2d 293; 794 N.E.2d 181; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 343; 276 Ill. Dec. 286



June 20, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Harris, 182 Ill. 2d 114, 695 N.E.2d 447, 1998 Ill. LEXIS 367, 230 Ill. Dec. 957 (1998)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] On direct appeal, post-conviction court's judgment was affirmed, in part, reversed, in part, and cause was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the dismissal of his post-conviction petitions by the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) after his convictions for murder and attempted armed robbery and sentence to death were affirmed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's post-conviction petition raised eight grounds for relief. The appellate court held, inter alia, that defendant did not show that there was a bona fide doubt concerning his fitness to stand trial. Information as to the polysubstance abuse of a State witness, and his statement about gang foes was not material under Brady. Aggravation testimony of a corrections officer, which defendant failed to show was perjured, did not result in a Brady violation. The appellate court ordered an evidentiary hearing as to defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel at sentencing where counsel signed an affidavit stating that he failed to investigate and present evidence in mitigation because he did not believe defendant would be sentenced to death. Defendant's request for a new sentencing hearing was denied. The failure of defendant's appellate counsel to raise an argument based on the amendment of the armed robbery statute did not constitute ineffective assistance since defendant was indicted prior to the amendment. Defendant's argument that Illinois' death penalty statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1 (West 1998), was unconstitutional based on Apprendi was rejected.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of trial counsel based upon trial counsel's failure to investigate and present evidence in mitigation was reversed, and the trial court was ordered to conduct an evidentiary hearing on the issue on remand. In other respects, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Schweigert v. Schweigert

The state supreme court upheld the trial court's order but on different grounds. The statute had been held facially unconstitutional in its entirety by a prior court decision.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was affirmed.

People v. Hopkins


Docket No. 91938


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


201 Ill. 2d 26; 773 N.E.2d 633; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 330; 265 Ill. Dec. 869



June 6, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY:  People v. Hopkins, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 1180 (Ill. App. Ct. June 5, 2001).



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of De Kalb County (Illinois), the trial court sentenced defendant to 75 years' imprisonment for first degree murder involving the death of a 70-year old victim and a concurrent 20-year sentence for armed robbery and home invasion. The Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District, vacated the sentence for first degree murder and the state supreme court granted the State's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, armed robbery, aggravated battery, and home invasion after a 70-year old man died from stab wounds to the chest and neck. The trial court found that the victim was 60 years old or older at the time of the offense, was handicapped, and that the offense was accompanied by exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty, and it sentenced defendant to 75 years in prison for the murder, pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-2(a)(1) (1994). The intermediate appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction but reversed his extended-term sentence for murder. The state supreme court held that (1) the trial court could impose an extended-term sentence if only one of the factors listed in 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-3.2(b) (1994) was proved beyond a reasonable doubt and because the victim's age was proved beyond a reasonable doubt, the trial court did not have to find that the victim was handicapped or that the offense was exceptionally brutal or heinous beyond a reasonable doubt before it imposed an extended-term sentence; and (2) the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed that part of the intermediate appellate court's judgment that affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for armed robbery and home invasion, but reversed that of the intermediate appellate court's judgment that reversed the defendant's sentence for first degree murder, and affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

323 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hill


Docket No. 91329


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


199 Ill. 2d 440; 771 N.E.2d 374; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 325; 264 Ill. Dec. 670



May 22, 2002, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Trial court's judgment was reversed and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with home invasion while armed with a firearm in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-11(a)(3) (Supp. 1999), as amended. He moved to dismiss on grounds that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-11 violated the state constitution's separation of powers clause (Ill. Const. art. II, § 1), and the proportionate penalties clause (Ill. Const. art. I, § 11). The Illinois circuit court agreed, and dismissed the charges. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The home invasion statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-11(a)(3) ( Supp. 1999), as amended by 2000 Ill. Laws 91-404, § 5, carried a mandatory add-on sentence where a defendant armed with a firearm used or threatened the use of force upon anyone in the invaded home, whether or not injury occurred. The circuit court held that § 12-11(a)(3), by imposing mandatory add-on sentences, violated the separation of powers clause. The supreme court disagreed. First, trial courts retained the ability under § 12-11(a)(3) to consider aggravating and mitigating factors. Second, aggravating and mitigating factors did not have to be a part of the sentencing equation if the legislature deemed such factors inappropriate. The 15/20/25-life enhancement penalty applied when the offender possessed a firearm, discharged a firearm and/or injured an occupant of the dwelling. The supreme court held that the sentencing range was not so severe as to render the statute unconstitutional as violative of the proportionality clause. A 21-to-45-year sentence for violating § 12-11(a)(3) (Supp. 1999) was not cruel or degrading, nor did it shock the moral conscience.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

324 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Flynn v. Ryan


Docket No. 90263


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


199 Ill. 2d 430; 771 N.E.2d 414; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 327; 264 Ill. Dec. 710



May 22, 2002, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] On direct appeal, trial court's judgment was reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, former trustee and state senator, filed a declaratory judgment suit against defendants, governor and attorney general, challenging the constitutionality of the Illinois State Gift Ban Act (Act), 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. 425/1 et seq. (2000). Defendants asserted that plaintiffs lacked standing. The parties cross-moved for summary judgment. The Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois) entered judgment for plaintiffs. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that the trial court erred by invalidating portions of the Act on its face on vagueness grounds where plaintiffs did not allege a first amendment interest at stake in the Act, and plaintiffs lacked standing to raise arguments regarding alleged encroachments upon the powers of the executive and judicial branches of government because neither plaintiff was an official of the executive or judicial branch of government. The supreme court held that plaintiffs lacked standing to advance any of the claims they raised in the circuit court. The supreme court noted that plaintiffs failed to demonstrate that there was a concrete dispute. Thus, plaintiffs' challenge requested the court to issue an advisory opinion, which the court could not do. Thus, the supreme court held that the trial court erred by declaring the Act unconstitutional, and the complaint should have been dismissed in its entirety.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

Hill v. Cowan


Docket No. 90229


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


202 Ill. 2d 151; 781 N.E.2d 1065; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 308; 269 Ill. Dec. 875



April 18, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Modified Upon Denial of Rehearing December 2, 2002.
Rehearing denied by, 12/02/2002
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hill v. Cowan, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 3116 (U.S., Apr. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Hill, 101 Ill. 2d 591, 1985 Ill. LEXIS 344 (1985)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee warden sought direct review of a judgment of the St. Clair County Circuit Court (Illinois) granting appellee habeas corpus petitioner immediate release from confinement on the grounds that the extended term portions of the sentences imposed after his conviction on guilty plea violated the Apprendi rule.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner pled guilty to attempted murder, rape, and armed robbery, and received extended-term sentences upon the trial court's finding of exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty, as permitted by the sentencing statute in effect at the time. Two decades later he sought habeas corpus relief, arguing that without a jury finding on the issue of special circumstances, his extended-term sentences violated the rule of Apprendi. The high court held that the trial court erred in granting relief. The statutes in question, codified at the time of the petition at 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-3.2, 5-8-2, had already been held not unconstitutional on their faces. If petitioner had not pled guilty, he might have succeeded on a challenge to the constitutionality of the statute as applied to him under Apprendi, but by pleading guilty, he waived his right to a jury trial and to a jury's finding of all elements contributing to his sentence beyond a reasonable doubt. Furthermore, his guilty plea had been upheld on direct appeal and on an earlier petition for post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting the petition.

 

326 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Blanco


Docket No. 91085


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


199 Ill. 2d 410; 770 N.E.2d 214; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 311; 264 Ill. Dec. 320



April 18, 2002, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with offenses including armed robbery while in possession of a firearm. Prior to trial, defendant filed a motion arguing that the 15-year sentencing enhancement in 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-2(b) violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970). The Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) invalidated the 15-year enhancement. The State immediately appealed.


OVERVIEW: A statute was presumed constitutional, and the party challenging the statute bore the burden of demonstrating its invalidity. The court had a duty to construe a statute in a manner that upheld its validity and constitutionality if it reasonably could be done. Whether a statute was constitutional was a question of law that was reviewed de novo. The appellate court held the appeal was controlled by the decision in People v. Walden, which concluded that the 15-year sentencing enhancement for armed robbery while in possession of a firearm in 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-2(b) violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution and therefore was unenforceable. Given the identity of issue between this appeal and Walden, the appellate court held that the trial court's order invalidating the 15-year enhancement was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed, and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.

Wickham v. Byrne


Docket Nos. 92048, 92135 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


199 Ill. 2d 309; 769 N.E.2d 1; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 313; 263 Ill. Dec. 799



April 18, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Case No. 92135: Langman v. Langman, 325 Ill. App. 3d 101, 258 Ill. Dec. 816, 757 N.E.2d 505, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 553 (3d Dist. 2001).



DISPOSITION: Court of appeals' judgment in case No. 92048 was reversed and court of appeals' judgment in case No. 92135 was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois) and an Illinois appellate court, in separate cases, ruled respectively that 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/607(b)(1) (2000) and 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/607(b)(3) (2000), allowing grandparent visitation, were and were not unconstitutional as applied. Appellant father appealed the trial court ruling, appellant paternal grandparents appealed the appellate court ruling, and the cases were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The father and mother had a child. The mother died. The father permitted the child to see the child's maternal grandmother. However, the father declined to leave the child with her unsupervised and overnight. In a separate case, the mother and father had two children. The father then died. The paternal grandparents wanted visitation, but the mother would only allow supervised visitation. The trial court ruled in the father's case that he had not shown the state lacked a compelling interest in ordering grandparent visitation; thus, it found the applicable statute, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/607(b)(1) (2000), constitutional as applied. The appellate court ruled in the case of the paternal grandparents that 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/607(b)(1) (2000) was unconstitutional because the mother had a due process right to raise her children the way she saw fit. After the cases were consolidated, the state supreme court found 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/607(b)(1) (2000) and 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/607(b)(3) (2000), allowing for grandparent visitation, were facially unconstitutional since they violated the substantive due process rights of the parents to raise their children as they saw fit.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order in the father's case finding the statutory provisions were not unconstitutional as applied was reversed. Also, the appellate court's decision finding in the case of the paternal grandparents that the statutory provisions as applied were unconstitutional was affirmed.

People v. Walden


Docket No. 90976


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


199 Ill. 2d 392; 769 N.E.2d 928; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 315; 264 Ill. Dec. 91



April 18, 2002, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] On direct appeal, trial court's judgment was affirmed and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with one count of armed robbery while in possession of a firearm, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-2(a)(2) (2000). Defendant moved to dismiss the information because the statute under which he was charged and would have been sentenced was unconstitutional and contained an unlawful double sentence enhancement. The Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) granted the motion. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented on appeal was whether the 15-year sentencing enhancement for armed robbery while in possession of a firearm, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-2(a)(2), (b) (2000), was valid and enforceable. The supreme court held that the 15-year enhancement for armed robbery while in possession of a firearm violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution and was unenforceable. The supreme court found that the enhancement created a more severe punishment for the less serious offense of armed robbery while in possession of a firearm than existed for armed violence predicated upon aggravated robbery. Thus, the supreme court determined that the matter was subject to remand to address this issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The case was remanded for resentencing.

Prior to trial, he argued the 15-year sentencing enhancement for committing an armed robbery while in possession of a firearm, 720 Ill. Comp. I, § 11. However, it found defendant's speedy-trial rights were not violated because, pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(a)(4), the time during which the State took an appeal was not counted against the State.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, defendant's argument that his speedy-trial rights were violated by the delay caused by the State's appeal was rejected, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Jackson

SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


199 Ill. 2d 286; 769 N.E.2d 21; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 317; 263 Ill. Dec. 819



April 18, 2002, Opinion Filed

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the intermediate appellate court judgment.

People v. Johnson

SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


205 Ill. 2d 381; 793 N.E.2d 591; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 301; 275 Ill. Dec. 820

After the petition was denied, the state supreme court found the trial court erred in not allowing DNA testing, a hearing should have been ordered on the alleged ineffectiveness, and trial counsel should have been ordered to give an evidence deposition.

People v. Belcher


Docket No. 91417


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


199 Ill. 2d 378; 769 N.E.2d 920; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 298; 264 Ill. Dec. 83



April 4, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] People v. Belcher, 319 Ill. App. 3d 906, 254 Ill. Dec. 169, 746 N.E.2d 1217, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 222 (4th Dist. 2001).



DISPOSITION: Court of appeals' judgment was reversed and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to murder and received a sentence of 60 years' imprisonment. The Court of Appeals (Illinois) declined to vacate the guilty plea and sentence or allow defendant leave to file a motion to withdraw his plea. On remand, defendant's motion to reconsider sentence was denied. The appellate court affirmed. Defendant's petition for leave to appeal was granted, pursuant to 177 Ill. 2d R. 315(a).


OVERVIEW: The state's highest court held that defendant should have been given an opportunity to file the motion to vacate his guilty plea under the unusual circumstances of the case. The court-appointed psychiatrist opined, prior to trial, that defendant was sane at the time of the murder, under the insanity definition in Ill. Pub. Act 89-404 (1989). Based upon that representation, defendant pled guilty to the murder. However, the insanity provisions used at trial were enacted in contravention of the single subject rule, and were thus, unconstitutional. Had the fact been known to defendant at that time, his decision to forgo the affirmative defense and to enter a guilty plea might have been different. In fact, the psychiatrist testified that under the former version of the insanity statute, he would have concluded that defendant was insane at the time of the murder, as defendant was unable to conform his conduct to the requirements of law. The trial court relied upon that representation in accepting defendant's guilty plea. Thus, all parties involved may have been operating under a misapprehension of law.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded.

 

333 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Southwestern Ill. Dev. Auth. v. Nat'l City Envtl., L.L.C.


Docket No. 87809


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


199 Ill. 2d 225; 768 N.E.2d 1; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 299; 263 Ill. Dec. 241



April 4, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Southwestern Ill. Dev. Auth. v. Nat'l City Envtl., L.L.C., 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6453 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Southwestern Ill. Dev. Auth. v. National City Envtl., 304 Ill. App. 3d 542, 238 Ill. Dec. 99, 710 N.E.2d 896, 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 300 (5th Dist. 1999).



DISPOSITION: Court of appeals' judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois appellate court reversed a trial court's judgment that found appellant government agency properly exercised its power of eminent domain in taking property owned by appellee property owners and conveying it to a third party. The government agency filed a petition for leave to appeal, which the state supreme court granted. After reversing the appellate court's decision, the state supreme court granted a petition for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: The Illinois General Assembly created the government agency to promote recreational activities and facilities to reduce unemployment and enhance the state's general welfare. To achieve those purposes, the legislature empowered the government agency to issue bonds to develop or improve projects. The government agency then issued the bonds. It lent the proceeds to a third party to develop a multipurpose automotive sports and training facility. Since that project was very successful, the third party found it needed to expand, and needed additional parking. The third party persuaded the government agency to have the property owners' property condemned so the third party could obtain it to increase its parking, even though the third party could have built a parking facility on its existing land. After the trial court ordered that title to the property be vested in the government agency and the appellate court affirmed, the state supreme court found that the government agency's taking of the property was unconstitutional as the taking was to benefit a private party in helping it to solve its parking problems and was not primarily for a public use or public purpose.


OUTCOME: Upon the property owners' petition for rehearing, the appellate court's initial decision to reverse the trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

334 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Daniels v. Indus. Comm'n (archibald Candy Co.)


Docket No. 90318


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


201 Ill. 2d 160; 775 N.E.2d 936; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 293; 266 Ill. Dec. 864



March 21, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended September 27, 2002. As Modified on Denial of Rehearing August 29, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Daniels v. Industrial Comm'n, 315 Ill. App. 3d 580, 247 Ill. Dec. 350, 732 N.E.2d 66, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 486 (1st Dist. 2000) 



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An arbitrator awarded appellant claimant temporary total disability (TTD), medical expenses, and other compensation for a work-related injury. Appellee employer appealed. Appellee industrial commission (IC) decreased the weeks of TTD and vacated the rest of the award. A circuit court confirmed the IC's decision. The Appellate Court, Industrial Commission Division, Illinois, affirmed. The claimant was granted leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Before the IC heard the matter, one of the three commissioners on the panel assigned to review the case was elevated to commission chairman and a second commissioner resigned. The new commission chairman appointed a succession of arbitrators to temporarily fill the two vacant posts. The claimant argued to the appellate court and later to the state supreme court that the IC's decision was void because the deciding panel was illegally constituted. The appellate court rejected that argument, but the state supreme court agreed with the claimant. Pursuant to § 13 of the Illinois Workers' Compensation Act, 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 305/13, the governor had authority to appoint commissioners to the IC with the senate's consent and authority to temporarily appoint replacement commissioners to fill vacancies while the senate was in recess. One exception allowed the commission chairman to make appointments, but it did not apply. Since the commission chairman lacked statutory authority to appoint the commissioners who finally decided the case, the appointments had no legal effect and the IC's decision was void. The case had to be remanded to the IC for a decision by a legally constituted panel.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court vacated the IC's decision, reversed the judgments of the appellate court and the circuit court, and remanded the cause to the IC for a decision by a legally constituted panel.

 

335 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Porter v. Jolliff (in Re Jolliff)


Docket No. 91563


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


199 Ill. 2d 510; 771 N.E.2d 346; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 321; 264 Ill. Dec. 642



March 13, 2002, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the decedent's sister and his former guardian, filed a statutory custodial claim under 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-1.1 (2000). Appellee, the decedent's daughter and the administrator of his estate, opposed the claim on grounds that § 18-1.1 was unconstitutional. The Cook County, Illinois, Circuit Court, agreed with the daughter, and dismissed the sister's custodial claim. The sister appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sister lived with and cared for the decedent from 1987 to his death in 1999. Under § 18-1.1, a spouse, parent, sibling, or child was entitled to a fixed compensation for living with and caring for a disabled decedent for at least three years. The trial court held that § 18-1.1 violated the special legislation, equal protection, due process, and separation of powers provisions of the Illinois Constitution. The supreme court disagreed. The classification of close family members who alone were eligible for compensation bore a rational relationship to the purpose of the statute, and was not arbitrary. Thus, neither the special legislation nor the equal protection clauses, Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13, and art. I, §2, respectively, were violated. There was no due process violation: the minimum claim amounts were not arbitrary, and the statute remedied the inequity of allowing heirs who never cared for a decedent to recover more from his estate than one who dedicated years of her life to him. The statute was not too vague to be applied. Finally, by setting minimum claim amounts, the legislature did not violate the separation of powers provision of Ill. Const. art. II, § 1.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the cause was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

336 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Davis


Docket No. 89704


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


205 Ill. 2d 349; 793 N.E.2d 552; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 286; 275 Ill. Dec. 781



February 22, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Davis v. Illinois, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6694 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002).



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The circuit court sentenced defendant to death for a woman's murder. On direct appeal, the Supreme Court of Illinois remanded for resentencing as the circuit court failed to fully consider the mitigating factor of defendant's good prison behavior. Defendant again waived his right to a jury for the second phase of the sentencing hearing and a Circuit Court of Henry County (Illinois) judgment imposed the death penalty. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court held a new sentencing hearing upon remand. The supreme court summarized evidence in that hearing and decided that the circuit court adequately expressed its reasoning for weighing aggravators and mitigators and finding defendant eligible for and imposing the death sentence. The circuit court admitted and analyzed the testimony of four admitted prostitutes, rendered credible because they corresponded to each other; an officer's testimony; and physical evidence of defendant's brutal sexual attacks on the prostitutes in his car in secluded areas. They lived to testify; the victim did not. The fact that defendant was not charged for the conduct against the women did not mean their testimony could not be used to minimize the weight of defendant's 72 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(c) mitigator: that he had no significant history of prior criminal activity (and not as an "other reasons" aggravator). Counsel's trial strategy to allow admission of the officer's testimony to show the women's testimony inconsistencies was not ineffective assistance. Several Apprendi arguments were analyzed and rejected. The death penalty statute's constitutionality was reaffirmed.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment and directed the clerk of the supreme court to enter an order setting the date on which the sentence of death entered by the circuit court was to be carried out.

Petersen v. Wallach


Docket No. 89947


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


198 Ill. 2d 439; 764 N.E.2d 19; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 6; 261 Ill. Dec. 728



January 25, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Peterson v. Wallach, 314 Ill. App. 3d 823, 248 Ill. Dec. 38, 733 N.E.2d 713, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 507 (1st Dist. 2000) 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff daughter brought an action against defendant attorney alleging the attorney negligently rendered estate planning advice to her mother. The attorney moved to dismiss the complaint at time-barred. The circuit court dismissed the complaint. The daughter appealed. The appellate court (Illinois) reversed. The attorney appealed.


OVERVIEW: The daughter argued that the plain language of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-214.3(d) indicated that the exception to the six year statute of repose for attorney malpractice actions applied to her claim because the section did not draw a distinction between probate and nonprobate distributions. The supreme court held that the language of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-214.3(d) unambiguously supported its application to all cases when the alleged injury caused by the attorney's act or omission did not occur until the death of the person for whom the professional services were rendered. The court noted that there was no language limiting such actions to those that involve assets distributed through probate proceedings or excluding actions that involve nonprobate distributions of assets. Thus, the manner of distributing the decedent's assets was of no consequence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.

 

338 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


In re K.L.P. v. R.P.


Docket No. 90407


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


198 Ill. 2d 448; 763 N.E.2d 741; 2002 Ill. LEXIS 8; 261 Ill. Dec. 492



January 25, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 15, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: R.R.E. v. R.P. (In re K.L.P.)*1, 316 Ill. App. 3d 110, 249 Ill. Dec. 246, 735 N.E.2d 1071, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 734 (2d Dist. 2000) 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Appellate Court appointed appellate counsel to represent appellee indigent mother after the trial court denied her request for court-appointed counsel during an ultimately successful effort to terminate her parental rights under the Adoption Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 50/1 (1998). The attorney soon sought interim payment. The appellate court directed appellant county to pay reasonable attorney fees. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: In a custody action under the Juvenile Court Act, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/1 et seq. (1998) (Juvenile Court Act), the trial court appointed an attorney to represent the indigent mother. It then entered orders allowing the State to petition to terminate her parental rights. The State petitioned with respect to her son, but not two daughters. Thereafter, appellee natural father and stepmother petitioned for adoption pursuant to the Adoption Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 50/5(C)(1998) (Adoption Act), and sought to terminate her parental rights. The trial court denied a request for appointed counsel. She represented herself. The trial court granted the petitions. The indigent mother appealed. The appellate court appointed counsel for her. That counsel soon requested payment. The appellate court ordered the county to pay the attorney. After the county appealed, the state supreme court held equal protection grounds dictated the indigent mother was entitled to the same procedural safeguards under the Adoption Act, including counsel, as a similarly situated parent had in a Juvenile Court Act proceeding as the adoption involved state action. Thus, counsel had a right to the payment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

339 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Beaubien v. Ryan


Docket Nos. 92701, 92702, 92703, 92704, 92705, 92706, 92707, 92708 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


198 Ill. 2d 294; 762 N.E.2d 501; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1787; 260 Ill. Dec. 842



December 27, 2001, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Plaintiffs' requests were denied and judgment was entered for the defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff voters requested a declaratory judgment to invalidate defendant Illinois Legislative Redistricting Commission's (commission) redistricting plan, claiming the challenged districts did not comport with the compactness requirement of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 3.


OVERVIEW: After the federal census, the commission held a series of meeting and public hearings to create a redistricting plan. The state supreme court held that the voters had the burden of proving that the plan was unconstitutional. However, no procedural irregularities were cited and no assertion was made that the commission failed to consider relevant evidence or took into account evidence it should not have considered. Overall, the level of compactness had changed little from the prior plan. The commission rigorously adhered to the equality of population requirement. Its plan provided adequate representation to minorities and other special interests and conformed to legal requirements regarding political fairness. The plan actually resulted in far fewer splits of counties, townships, and municipalities than the other plans considered by the commission.


OUTCOME: The voters' requests for a declaratory judgment invalidating the redistricting plan were denied.

People v. Rivera


Docket No. 89884


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


198 Ill. 2d 364; 763 N.E.2d 306; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1445; 261 Ill. Dec. 336



December 6, 2001, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Rivera, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 43 (Ill., Feb. 4, 2002)
Appeal after remand at People v. River, 333 Ill. App. 3d 1228, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 4978 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] People v. Rivera, 315 Ill. App. 3d 454, 248 Ill. Dec. 318, 734 N.E.2d 26, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 475 (3d Dist. 2000) 
People v. Rivera, 315 Ill. App. 3d 454, 734 N.E.2d 26, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 475, 248 Ill. Dec. 318 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: The appellate court was affirmed in part, vacated in part, and the cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court of Illinois granted leave to appeal in order to decide whether a circuit court may, during the summary stage of a post-conviction proceeding, partially dismiss some claims raised in a post-conviction petition while advancing other claims raised in the same petition to the second stage of the proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Summary partial dismissals made during the first stage of a post-conviction proceeding were not permitted under the Illinois Post-Conviction Hearing Act (the Act), 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 et seq. (1998). The language, amendments, and legislative history of the Act supported this position. The appellate court erred in finding that the error in permitting a partial dismissal was so fundamental that the entire process needed to be started anew and not reaching any of the remaining issues of defendant's post-conviction appeal. It was difficult to perceive how further proceedings could benefit anyone, as defendant was given the opportunity to consult with appointed counsel, to discuss the claims that had been improperly dismissed, and to re-allege them if he so desired. The proceedings ordered by the appellate court were unwarranted.


OUTCOME: The appellate court holding concerning partial summary dismissals was affirmed. The appellate court decision remanding this matter for further proceedings was vacated and the matter was remanded.

 

342 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Ryan v. World Church of the Creator


Docket No. 89780


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


198 Ill. 2d 115; 760 N.E.2d 953; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1441; 260 Ill. Dec. 180



November 21, 2001, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attorney general (AG) filed a complaint against defendants, church and individual, seeking a declaratory judgment, a finding that they violated the Solicitation Act, 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. 460/0.01-23 (1998), and an injunction. The AG also sought to impose a fine and to freeze their assets. They moved to dismiss. The Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, granted their motion and denied the AG's motion for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that because the act regulated speech, it had to meet a heightened standard of precision. The supreme court found that the act's registration provisions applied to all entities that solicited funds for purposes defined in the act, and did not in any way control the content of speech. Therefore, the registration and reporting requirements were content neutral, and the law was subject to an intermediate level of scrutiny. The supreme court concluded that the registration and reporting requirements of the act served a substantial governmental interest. As to whether the challenged provisions of the act were narrowly tailored to serve this interest, the supreme court held that although the terms at issue were broad in scope, the court failed to see how they could be more precisely defined. The terms defendants challenged had well-settled definitions in Illinois. The supreme court concluded that the act's registration and reporting requirements were narrowly tailored to serve the state's substantial governmental interest in protecting its citizens from fraud and did not unnecessarily burden First Amendment speech.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

Burger v. Lutheran Gen. Hosp.


Docket Nos. 89643, 89644 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


198 Ill. 2d 21; 759 N.E.2d 533; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1423; 259 Ill. Dec. 753



October 18, 2001, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Trial court's judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff patient's medical malpractice suit against defendants, hospital, corporations, and physicians, the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, declared that parts of 210 Ill. Comp. Stat. 85/6.17 of the Hospital Licensing Act (HLA), 210 Ill. Comp. Stat. 85/1 et seq., were unconstitutional. The hospital and corporations appealed to the state supreme court. The appeal was consolidated with another.


OVERVIEW: The challenged parts of the HLA allowed ex parte communications regarding patient records between certain non-party health care providers with counsel and hospital staff who were parties and gave immunity for HLA violations under some circumstances. The circuit court found that (1) parts of 210 Ill. Comp. Stat. 85/6.17(d), (e), and all of 210 Ill. Comp. Stat. 85/6.17(h) violated the separation of powers doctrine; (2) 210 Ill. Comp. Stat. 85/6.17(d), (e) unreasonably invaded patients' constitutional privacy interests; (3) § 6.17(d), (e) was not impermissible special legislation in violation of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13; and (4) the invalid parts of the HLA were severable. The appealing defendants and amici argued that the circuit court's decision ignored the compelling health-care policy concerns that supported the challenged provisions. The state supreme court held that 210 Ill. Comp. Stat. 85/6.17(d), (e), (h) did not violate separation of powers because they did not interfere with a court's power to regulate discovery or the activity of litigants and their counsel; § 6.17(d), (e) did not violate patient privacy; and § 6.17(e) was not impermissible special legislation.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the part of the circuit court's decision that found that the special legislation clause of the state constitution was not violated; reversed the parts of the decision that found that parts of the act violated the separation of powers clause of the state constitution and violated patient privacy rights under the state constitution; and remanded the matter to the circuit court for further proceedings.

People v. Ford


Docket No. 90083


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


198 Ill. 2d 68; 761 N.E.2d 735; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1430; 260 Ill. Dec. 552



October 18, 2001, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing December 3, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Ford, 192 Ill. 2d 697, 742 N.E.2d 331, 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1725 (Ill. 2000).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(1), and the trial court imposed an extended-term sentence of 100 years. Defendant appealed, and the Appellate Court (Illinois) affirmed. Defendant filed a petition for rehearing, which the appellate court denied. Defendant filed a motion for leave to file a late petition for leave to appeal, and the state supreme court granted the motion and the petition.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to the murder. The victim was tortured prior to the murder because it was believed that the victim was involved in the murder of a friend of defendant. The State sought the death penalty, and the trial court found defendant was eligible for the death penalty. The trial court declined to impose the death penalty based on defendant's youth and cooperation. Defendant argued that his 100 year extended-term sentence violated the Apprendi doctrine. Under Apprendi, any fact that increased the penalty for a crime beyond the prescribed statutory maximum was required to be submitted to a jury, and proven beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court held that the sentence imposed did not violate Apprendi. Based exclusively upon facts that were proved beyond a reasonable doubt, defendant faced a prescribed statutory maximum sentence of death. The sentence actually imposed did not exceed this maximum. The appellate court held that when a defendant was found eligible for the death penalty by proof beyond a reasonable doubt, the imposition of an extended-term prison sentence under 730 Ill. Comp. Stats.5/5-5-3.2(b)(2), 5/5-8-2(a)(1), complied with Apprendi.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

347 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Varner (in Re Varner)


Docket No. 90151


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


198 Ill. 2d 78; 759 N.E.2d 560; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1433; 259 Ill. Dec. 780



October 18, 2001, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Varner (In re Det. of Varner), 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1454 (Ill., Dec. 3, 2001)
Vacated by, Remanded by Varner v. Illinois, 537 U.S. 802, 154 L. Ed. 2d 3, 123 S. Ct. 69, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 5399 (2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] People v. Varner (In re Varner), 315 Ill. App. 3d 626, 734 N.E.2d 226, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 668 (2000).
People v. Varner (In re Varner), 315 Ill. App. 3d 626, 734 N.E.2d 226, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 668, 248 Ill. Dec. 518 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant to be a sexually violent person under the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 207/1 et seq. Defendant was committed for control, custody and treatment. The Appellate Court (Illinois) affirmed. Defendant's petition for leave to appeal was granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to criminal sexual assault and was sentenced. As his prison term was ending the State filed proceedings to have him committed indefinitely pursuant to the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act (Act), 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 207/1 et seq. In the appeal, defendant argued that his commitment under the Act could not be squared with the principles of substantive due process because it occurred without a specific finding by the jury that he lacked volitional control over his sexually violent criminal behavior. The appellate court held that the Act required that the future danger posed by an individual be linked to the existence of a mental condition and the mental condition was required to have been one which affected an individual's ability to control his conduct. In defining "sexually violent person," the Act did not refer to persons suffering from personality disorders, only to persons suffering from "mental disorders." The term "mental disorder" was, in turn, specifically defined by the Act, and the precommitment requirement of a mental disorder, as defined by the Act, was sufficient to pass constitutional muster.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Simpson


Docket Nos. 85084, 86926 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


204 Ill. 2d 536; 792 N.E.2d 265; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1081; 275 Ill. Dec. 34



September 27, 2001, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Simpson v. Illinois, 535 U.S. 991, 152 L. Ed. 2d 472, 122 S. Ct. 1547, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 2428 (2002)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Dismissed by, in part United States ex rel. Simpson v. Briley, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 1504 (N.D. Ill., Feb. 5, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court. COUNTY: Cook. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. John A. Wasilewski. CASE NUMBERS: TR92CR13071.
People v. Simpson, 172 Ill. 2d 117, 665 N.E.2d 1228, 1996 Ill. LEXIS 28, 216 Ill. Dec. 671 (1996)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, sentenced to death, appealed the orders of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissing his amended post-conviction petition and his petition for post-judgment relief under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1401 (1998). The matters were consolidated for appeal.


OVERVIEW: Court dismissed defendant's amended post-conviction petition and petition for post-judgment relief under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1401 (1998). The trial court did not err in denying defendant's discovery request, as it was a fishing expedition. The trial court did not improperly make fact-findings by restating an affidavit or finding that defendant's lack of credibility assertions were legally insufficient without affidavit support. Defendant was competent to proceed with the post-conviction process because his mental condition had not deteriorated since the last court date and post-conviction counsel used some of defendant's pro se arguments. There was no evidence that a police officer committed perjury. The alleged prosecutorial misconduct did not undermine confidence in the outcome of the trial. The appellate court refused to hear claims that defendant waived by not bringing them on direct appeal. The appellate court refused to hear claims barred by res judicata. Standby counsel, not under a duty to actively participate in preparing defendant's legal defense, was not ineffective.


OUTCOME: The dismissals of defendant's motions were affirmed.

 

350 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


In re H.G.


Docket Nos. 89115, 89783, 90053 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


197 Ill. 2d 317; 757 N.E.2d 864; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1068; 259 Ill. Dec. 1



September 20, 2001, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] No. 89115-Affirmed. Nos. 89783, 90053-Appeals dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) and the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) held 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 50/1(D)(m-1) to be unconstitutional. Appellant State took a direct appeal to the state's highest appellate court, and the cases were consolidated for review.


OVERVIEW: The state's highest appellate court held that the Adoption Act, specifically 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 50/1(D)(m-1), was an unconstitutional violation of a parent's substantive due process rights under the Fourteenth Amendment and the Illinois Constitution. The provision impinged upon a parent's fundamental liberty interest in raising her child. Thus, it had to meet the strict scrutiny test and be narrowly tailored to serve a compelling governmental interest. The presumption of unfitness set forth in § 50/1(D)(m-1) was not narrowly tailored to the compelling goal of identifying unfit parents, because in many cases the length of a child's stay in foster care had nothing to do with the parent's ability or inability to safely care for the child, but instead was due to circumstances beyond the parent's control. Because there would be many cases in which children remained in foster care for the statutory period even when their parents could properly care for them, the presumption was not a narrowly tailored means of identifying parents who posed a danger to their children's health or safety. The decisions of the Cook County court had become final and were therefore moot.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County was affirmed. The appeals from the Circuit Court of Cook County were dismissed.

People v. Sypien


Docket No. 89265


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


198 Ill. 2d 334; 763 N.E.2d 264; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1077; 261 Ill. Dec. 294

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the dismissal of defendant's disorderly conduct charge by the Circuit Court of De Kalb County (Illinois), since 1998 Ill. Laws 90-456 (act) amending the Criminal Code of 1961, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-1 et seq., violated the single subject rule of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d) (1970).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with disorderly conduct for allegedly making a false report of a stolen vehicle to the police. He maintained that the act violated the single subject rule by combining amendments to juvenile proceedings with amendments to the criminal code. The trial court agreed. The state supreme court determined that the act was permissible on its face because it dealt with criminal and correctional matters. The state supreme court reviewed each individual amendment in the act to determine if they all related to criminal and correctional matters. It held that the connection between juvenile abuse, neglect, and dependency hearings under the act and the criminal law was neither natural nor logical.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of defendant's charges was affirmed.

 

352 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Langendorf v. City of Urbana


Docket No. 90635


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


197 Ill. 2d 100; 754 N.E.2d 320; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1036; 257 Ill. Dec. 662



July 26, 2001, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, Appellate Court, Fourth District. COUNTY: Champaign. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. John R. DeLaMar. CASE NUMBERS: AC4-99-0449, TR98L247.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen filed a declaratory judgment action against defendant city, challenging the zoning of two parcels of property that were rezoned by the city pursuant to annexation agreements. The trial court granted the city's motion to dismiss, finding that his cause of action was barred because it was filed beyond the limitations period. The Court of Appeals (Illinois) reversed the decision, and the city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that annexation and zoning were, in the abstract, distinct concepts, and that the one year statute of limitations in 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-1-46 did not apply to the instant action. The state supreme court held that the zoning of the parcels could not be separated from the annexation. The provisions of the annexation agreements made it clear that the rezoning of the properties was an integral part of and was in fact the essential condition of and consideration for the agreements. The agreements provided that upon annexation, the tracts would be converted from county zoning to city zoning, that the zoning would remain in effect for a 20-year term, and that the corporate authorities would not rezone the properties for the life of the agreements. The citizen did not argue that there were procedural defects in the city's passage of the annexation and zoning ordinances in question, or that they did not receive notice or an opportunity to be heard. The supreme court held that the limitations period set forth in 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-1-46 precluded the kind of belated indirect attack on the annexation that the citizen made at the instant stage.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed, and the trial court's judgment was affirmed.

D.S. v. R.S. (in Re D.S.)


Docket No. 88460


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


198 Ill. 2d 309; 763 N.E.2d 251; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 773; 261 Ill. Dec. 281



June 21, 2001, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Rehearing February 4, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal, Appellate Court, Second District. COUNTY: Kane. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Thomas E. Mueller. CASE NUMBERS: AC2-98-1022, TR93J405.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) directing it to prosecute a pending petition to terminate parental rights under the Illinois Juvenile Court Act (Act). The Supreme Court of Illinois allowed the State's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: After minor was adjudicated as neglected and abused, her guardian ad litem petitioned for termination of parental rights. The State claimed it was the only party who could bring the action. After various actions and appeals, the lower court ordered the State to prosecute the action, and it appealed. The Illinois Supreme Court granted leave to appeal and held that the guardian ad litem, but not the minor, was authorized to file but not prosecute the petition. The lower court could order the State to prosecute the petition since it had authority under the Act to determine the best interests of the minor. The separation of powers doctrine was not violated because both the State and the lower court had concurrent obligations to protect the minor's best interests. The minor's rights and interests were fully represented by the guardian and the lower court.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

People v. Carney


Docket No. 90549


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


196 Ill. 2d 518; 752 N.E.2d 1137; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 779; 256 Ill. Dec. 895



June 21, 2001, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 29, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 10184.
Appeal after remand at People v. Carney, 327 Ill. App. 3d 998, 765 N.E.2d 1028, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 70, 262 Ill. Dec. 420 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Appellate Court, First District. COUNTY: Cook. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Colleen McSweeney Moore. CASE NUMBERS: AC1-98-4677, TR97CR29458.
People v. Carney, 317 Ill. App. 3d 806, 740 N.E.2d 435, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 877, 251 Ill. Dec. 354 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed, circuit court affirmed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed Illinois Appellate Court order vacating defendant's consecutive sentences imposed pursuant to Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4(a), and ordering his sentences to run concurrently, on grounds that the sentencing statute operated unconstitutionally to increase defendant's punishment without separate jury findings.


OVERVIEW:  730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4(a) authorized imposition of consecutive sentences on defendants convicted of very serious felonies where bodily injury was involved. Defendant's consecutive sentences for first-degree murder and armed robbery had been vacated by an intermediate appellate court, on grounds that they violated the constitutional rule of Apprendi, which precluded imposition of additional punishments based on findings, at sentencing, not made by the finder of fact on the issue of guilt or innocence. The high court held that the statute did not violate the Apprendi rule, because under Illinois law, each sentence imposed was a separate punishment for a separate offense. Whether they were served consecutively or concurrently was constitutionally irrelevant, so long as no sentence exceeded the statutory maximum. The statute simply directed a sentencing court in the exercise of its discretion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court, affirming the circuit court on the issue of sentencing, and remanded to the appellate court for consideration of other issues raised in defendant's appeal, on which that court had not yet ruled.

People v. Bolden


Docket No. 87117


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


197 Ill. 2d 166; 756 N.E.2d 812; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 770; 258 Ill. Dec. 538



June 21, 2001, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 18, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 1675.
Rehearing denied by People v. Bolden, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1086 (Ill., Oct. 1, 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Bolden v. Illinois, 535 U.S. 936, 122 S. Ct. 1316, 152 L. Ed. 2d 225, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 1675 (2002)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by United States ex rel. Bolden v. Walls, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 42692 (N.D. Ill., Apr. 30, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal, Appellate Court, First District. COUNTY: Cook. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Stuart E. Palmer. CASE NUMBERS: AC1-96-4221, TR94CR8397.
People v. Bolden, 301 Ill. App. 3d 1082, 746 N.E.2d 335, 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 1061, 253 Ill. Dec. 887 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An Appellate Court judgment affirmed the defendant's convictions for first degree murders of two persons and for attempted first degree murder and aggravated battery of a third person. Defendant was sentenced to natural life imprisonment for the two murder convictions and to a consecutive term of 30 years' imprisonment for attempted murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant retained counsel, appeared, and was identified in the lineup by a witness, and then was arrested. Defendant and his counsel claimed he agreed to appear in the lineup only if his counsel could be present in the viewing room. The police refused to permit counsel to be in the viewing room. The supreme court affirmed that defendant's rights were not violated by the police refusal, because prior to the initiation of adversary proceeding, by formal charge, preliminary hearing, indictment, information, or arraignment, defendant did not have a right to counsel under U.S. Const. amends. V, VI, even where he had retained counsel or where counsel was told he could attend the lineup. Defendant could have been counseled to, and was free to, leave and not participate in the lineup. The refusal to allow his counsel to observe the witness did not transform a voluntary appearance to an involuntary search and seizure violation under U.S. Const. amend. IV or Ill. Const. art. I, § 6 (1970). The scope of protection under § 6 was not greater than under U.S. Const. amend. IV. Circuit court nonpattern instructions on refusal to permit counsel to view were not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Wagener

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for murder and concealment of a homicidal death and the imposition of consecutive sentences by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), claiming violation of the attorney-client privilege and unconstitutionality of the sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of murdering his wife and secreting her body. He was found guilty, but mentally ill of both offenses. He was sentenced to consecutive sentences. People v. Kuntu


Docket No. 83279


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


196 Ill. 2d 105; 752 N.E.2d 380; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 482; 256 Ill. Dec. 500



May 24, 2001, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court. COUNTY: Cook. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Joseph J. Urso. CASE NUMBERS: TR94CR9948.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed in part and vacated in part; death sentence reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his jury convictions before the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on seven counts of first degree murder and one count of aggravated arson. Defendant also appealed his subsequent sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of setting his apartment building on fire which resulted in seven people dying and numerous others being injured. Defendant confessed to the crime and there was additional incriminating evidence including witnesses. There was a question as to defendant's mental status. There was also a later hearing on the issue of whether a juror's relationship to the prosecutor compromised the juror's impartiality. The appellate court held that the trial court was in a better position to determine whether the juror was impartial and its determination that the relationship was remote did not contradict the manifest weight of the evidence. The appellate court did vacate defendant's convictions for felony murder on each count where he was already convicted of murder. However, the appellate court held a new death sentence hearing would be required due to improper remarks by the prosecution. The prosecution was not allowed to confuse the jury by arguing a statutory mitigating factor was actually an aggravating factor. Nor was the prosecution allowed to misstate the law by arguing defendant would "get five freebies" if he was not given the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed as to defendant's convictions except that his convictions for felony murder were vacated. The jury's conclusion that defendant was eligible for the death penalty remained standing. However, his death sentence was reversed and the matter was remanded.

People v. Dameron

SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS

DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; death sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his murder conviction in Kane County Circuit Court (Illinois) and imposition of the death penalty by the trial court, claiming that errors occurred in both the guilt determination and sentencing phases. He also challenged the constitutionality of the Illinois death penalty statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the heinous murder of his infant daughter. After his conviction, and after being mistakenly told that he could not have the jury instructed that the death penalty and a natural life sentence were the only available sentences under Illinois law, he waived a sentencing jury, and the trial court sentenced him to death. However, defendant's waiver of a sentencing jury was rendered involuntary by his reliance on the understanding of the trial court, as well as all counsel, that he was not entitled to an instruction regarding sentencing options. Finally, the sentencing record showed that defendant's due process rights were violated by reliance on resources outside the record; the court directed that a different judge take over on remand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, but vacated for new sentencing proceeding, despite upholding death penalty's constitutionality. Defendant's waiver of sentencing jury was tainted by reliance on incorrect information received from trial court. Because trial court considered matters outside the record, new sentencing proceeding was to be conducted by another judge.

Miller v. Rosenberg


Docket No. 89009


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


196 Ill. 2d 50; 749 N.E.2d 946; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 473; 255 Ill. Dec. 464



April 19, 2001, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied June 4, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Ill. LEXIS 499.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. Trial Judge: Honorable Charles F. Scott. Case Number: TR95L1803.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dentist filed suit for malicious prosecution against appellee patient in the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) after a jury found appellant not liable in a medical malpractice lawsuit brought by appellee. The circuit court declared that 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-109 (1996) violated the Illinois Constitution. Appellant challenged the ruling directly to the Supreme Court of Illinois.


OVERVIEW: Appellee contended that 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-109 (1996) was unconstitutional because it arbitrarily and irrationally eliminated the common law special injury requirement for the select group of plaintiffs who were health care professionals, thereby making it far easier for these plaintiffs to file and proceed with a malicious prosecution claim than it was for other malicious prosecution plaintiffs who still had to establish a special injury. The supreme court found that § 2-109 did not violate the prohibition against special legislation found in Ill. Const. 1970, art. IV, § 13 and the guarantee of equal protection contained in Ill. Const. 1970, art. I, § 2. There were discernible, rational reasons why the Illinois General Assembly distinguished between health care professionals who filed malicious prosecution suits against unsuccessful medical malpractice plaintiffs and all other individuals who might bring a malicious prosecution action. The classification was based upon a rational difference of situation or condition and the classification bore a reasonable relationship to the purposes of the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded as appellee failed to establish that the statute constituted impermissible special legislation.

People v. Jamison


Docket No. 80967


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


197 Ill. 2d 135; 756 N.E.2d 788; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 475; 258 Ill. Dec. 514



April 19, 2001, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Jamison v. Illinois, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 3630 (U.S. May 20, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County. Trial Judge: Honorable John P. Freese. Case Number: TR95CF609.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to first degree murder and armed robbery, and was sentenced to death by the Circuit Court of McLean County, Illinois. He appealed. The appellate court remanded so that defendant could be properly admonished, and he was granted leave to file a motion to withdraw his plea, which he did. He then sought review of the trial court's denial of this motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant fatally shot a woman, pulled her from her car, and drove away in it. He was charged with first degree murder and aggravated vehicular hijacking; the latter charge was amended to armed robbery, as this charge, but not hijacking, made defendant eligible for the death penalty. He pled guilty, and after a bench trial was sentenced to death. The trial court denied his motion to withdraw his plea, and he appealed. The appellate court affirmed. As defendant was taking psychotropic medication for depression, testimony was taken concerning his competency, and the evidence showed that this medication improved rather than impaired his cognitive functioning. As there was no bona fide doubt of his fitness, lack of a formal fitness hearing did not require reversal. His counsel was not ineffective in not seeking such a hearing, or in stipulating to psychiatric testimony. There was a factual basis for the plea to armed robbery, and the prosecutor had discretion to charge him with this offense. Defendant was not entitled to withdraw his plea due to his alleged ignorance of the consequences of the armed robbery amendment. Finally, the death penalty statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant development authority sought review of the judgment of the Illinois appellate court which reversed the decision of the trial court. The appellate court held appellant had not properly exercised its right of eminent domain because it sought to condemn property in order to convey it for a private use.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought to purchase appellee's property for the purpose of providing parking for a race track which had been expanding its operations. The appellate court reversed. The supreme court held the property could be condemned with the intent of transferring it to a private entity if the taking was for a public purpose. The supreme court found the taking was for a public purpose because there were issues of public safety and economic development.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and the cause was remanded.

Primeco Pers. Communs., L.P. v. State Commerce Comm'n


Docket Nos. 89075, 89084 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


196 Ill. 2d 70; 750 N.E.2d 202; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 246; 255 Ill. Dec. 621



March 29, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Ill. LEXIS 493.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Trial Judge: Honorable Robert V. Boharic. Case Number: TR98CH05500.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wireless telecommunications retailers and intervening plaintiff consumers sued defendant Illinois Commerce Commission, joined by intervening defendant city, claiming, inter alia, that the municipal infrastructure maintenance fee (municipal IMF) of 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 635/20, violated the Illinois Constitution. The trial court agreed with one of the plaintiffs' three constitutional claims. Each side appealed.


OVERVIEW: Cities were allowed to impose municipal IMF's on telecommunications retailers as a percentage of the retailers' charges to customers. The retailers in the case asserted that the municipal IMF violated the Uniformity Clause of Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2, because, as wireless providers, they could not be included in the class of retailers subject to the fee because they did not physically occupy the public rights-of-way. The state supreme court held (1) the municipal IMF was intended to establish a uniform system for allowing telecommunications providers to access the public rights-of-way in exchange for a fee; (2) because wireless providers did not own, operate, or maintain their infrastructure within the public rights-of-way, the trial court correctly found that subjecting them to the municipal IMF was unreasonable and violated Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2; (3) the trial court erred in finding the municipal IMF statute invalid on its face because the fact it was unconstitutional as applied to wireless providers was insufficient to render it wholly invalid with respect to all entities subject to it; and (4) it was unnecessary to address the other counts of the complaint.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's order of summary judgment that found the municipal infrastructure maintenance fee statute in violation of the Illinois Constitution's Uniformity Clause, as applied to retailers who did not own, operate, or maintain any part of their infrastructure within the public rights-of-way, but not insofar as the trial court held the statute invalid on its face.

In re R.C.

SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS

March 2, 2001, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] (89018). Appeal, Circuit Court, Cook County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Stephen R. Yates. CASE NUMBERS: TR95COA539. (88891). CASE NUMBERS: TR95COA539.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On direct appeal in an adoption matter, petitioners, the proposed adoptive parents, guardian ad litem, and state attorney general, sought review of a circuit court's order that a section of the Adoption Act, specifically 750 Ill.
