OVERVIEW: Appellee in adoption case gave her child up at birth for adoption. Two days later, she was transferred to the psychiatric ward. The child was placed with petitioner-appellants. The alleged birth father surrendered his parental rights. Appellants filed for adoption, contending appellee's consent was not required because she was an unfit parent as defined in 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 50/1(D)(p) (1998) of the Adoption Act. It reversed the circuit court and remanded the case.

Its determination that statute was unconstitutionally vague was premature. Prior appellate decisions imposing rational relation scrutiny were overruled, as state's interest in protecting minors was sufficiently compelling to satisfy strict due process scrutiny.

People v. Crespo


Docket No. 86556


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


203 Ill. 2d 335; 788 N.E.2d 1117; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 189; 273 Ill. Dec. 241



February 16, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified March 31, 2003. As Corrected February 22, 2001.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Crespo v. Ill., 2003 U.S. LEXIS 6402 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Crespo, 182 Ill. 2d 555, 707 N.E.2d 1241, 1999 Ill. LEXIS 158 (1999)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) criminal convictions in connection with multiple stabbings of his girlfriend and her daughter, arguing his aggravated battery conviction should be vacated because it stemmed from the same physical act as the armed violence charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, armed violence, and two counts of aggravated battery for intentionally or knowingly causing great bodily harm and for using a deadly weapon, in connection with stabbing his girlfriend and her daughter, killing his girlfriend. His sentences were to run concurrently. The appellate court affirmed, but ordered the mittimus be amended to reflect only one aggravated battery conviction. Defendant argued this conviction should be vacated because it stemmed from the same physical act as the armed violence charge. The State claimed the daughter's three stab wounds were three separate acts sustaining three convictions. The supreme court found that each wound could have supported a separate offense but that was not how the State charged defendant, or presented and argued the case. The indictment did not differentiate among the daughter's separate stab wounds but charged the same conduct, stabbing, under four different theories of criminal culpability; in other words, a single act charged four different ways. As the State made no attempt to apportion the crimes among the stab wounds, the court would not do so on appeal.


OUTCOME: Judgments of both appellate and circuit courts were affirmed in part and reversed in part. Appellate court ordered circuit court to amend mittimus to reflect only one aggravated battery conviction, affirming first degree murder and armed violence convictions. Supreme court held defendant's remaining aggravated battery conviction should also have been reversed, as all crimes stemmed from one act.

People v. Izzo


Docket No. 88887


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


195 Ill. 2d 109; 745 N.E.2d 548; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 190; 253 Ill. Dec. 425



February 16, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 22, 2001.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charge against him of unauthorized possession or storage of weapons on public property in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/21-6 on the grounds that § 21-6 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was carrying a S.W.A.T. knife at a public school and was charged with violating § 21-6. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. Any person of ordinary intelligence would have understood that the chief security officer was the person who had the responsibility for overseeing security issues at the school. There was no merit to defendant's argument that the statute violated the separation of powers under Ill. Const. art. II, § 1. The statute did not give the chief security officers the authority to determine if or when a defendant would be prosecuted for failing to obtain written permission to possess or store weapons on public property.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded because the statute was not unconstitutional.

 

367 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Sundance Homes v. County of Du Page


Docket Nos. 88763, 88764 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


195 Ill. 2d 257; 746 N.E.2d 254; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 192; 253 Ill. Dec. 806



February 16, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 22, 2001.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant builders won review of Illinois court of appeals' reversal of trial court judgment in class action against appellee county for refund of impact fees collected by county under statutes and ordinances later invalidated as unconstitutional. Appellate court held suit was barred by statute of limitation of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-205 (1996) and laches, as appellants waited over five years after paying the fees to seek a refund.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were homebuilders in appellee county. A 1987 enabling act allowed appellee to establish and collect road impact fees from builders. Appellee passed implementing ordinances. In 1995, in another case, the enabling act and implementing ordinances were held unconstitutional and fees were ordered returned. Appellants, not parties to that suit, later requested return of their fees. Appellee refused. Appellants filed a class action to force return of the fees and sought summary judgment, which was granted. The circuit court certified a class, created a common fund for its benefit, ordered appellee to transfer a certain sum into the fund, and awarded attorneys fees. The appellate court reversed, holding the suit was barred by the statute of limitation in 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-205 (1996), or laches. The supreme court granted leave to appeal and affirmed, holding the five-year statute of limitations applied and the cause of action had accrued when the fees were paid, not after the statute was invalidated, analogizing impact fee refunds to tax refunds.


OUTCOME: Appellate court judgment was affirmed, as appellants' action was barred by the five-year statute of limitation, because their cause of action accrued on the date they paid the challenged impact fees and not on the date the statute authorizing the fees was held unconstitutional.

 

368 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Ill. Press Ass'n v. Ryan


Docket No. 88597


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


195 Ill. 2d 63; 743 N.E.2d 568; 2001 Ill. LEXIS 2; 252 Ill. Dec. 700



January 19, 2001, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court, Sangamon County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Thomas R. Appleton. CASE NUMBERS: TR99MR172.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Vacated and Appeal Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the declaratory judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), granted to appellees.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought declaratory judgment regarding a provision of the Illinois Constitution that required ethics commissions created under the State Gift Ban Act (Act), 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. 425/1 et seq. (West 1998), to conduct their proceedings in public. Defendant moved for dismissal. The trial court held that proceedings of the commission that served the legislative branch must be public. The trial court believed that plaintiffs could seek declaratory relief in advance of commission proceedings. The trial court also concluded that defendant was a proper party. He appealed. Declaratory relief was obtainable only when there was an actual controversy between adverse parties. The trial court should have refused to enter a declaratory judgment, as it appeared the judgment would not terminate the controversy. 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-701(a) (West 1998). An adjudication of the merits of this appeal would have constituted merely an advisory opinion. Defendant had no role in the allegedly improper application of the statutes; he possessed no control over the legislative branch ethics commission's compliance with the constitutional provision that formed the basis of plaintiffs' suit.


OUTCOME: Judgment vacated and the appeal was dismissed. An adjudication of the merits of this appeal would have constituted merely an advisory opinion.

People v. Smith


Docket No. 86775


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


195 Ill. 2d 179; 745 N.E.2d 1194; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1714; 253 Ill. Dec. 660



December 1, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 12, 2001.
Certiorari Denied October 1, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 6519.
Rehearing denied by People v. Smith, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 248 (Ill., Apr. 2, 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Smith v. Illinois, 534 U.S. 886, 151 L. Ed. 2d 139, 122 S. Ct. 197, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 6519 (2001)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Smith, 176 Ill. 2d 217, 680 N.E.2d 291, 1997 Ill. LEXIS 28, 223 Ill. Dec. 558 (1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), dismissing his petition for post-conviction relief without an evidentiary hearing, following his convictions for first degree murder, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and home invasion, and his sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in trial court for first degree murder, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and home invasion, and sentenced to death. Defendant filed a post-conviction petition, which was denied by the trial court without an evidentiary hearing. Defendant appealed, claiming that the trial court erred in denying his post-conviction petition because his trial counsel and his appellate counsel rendered ineffective assistance, and the prosecution's closing remarks were inflammatory. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court properly denied defendant's petition because he failed to prove that his trial counsel was ineffective the pre-trial hearing and at trial, that the prosecution's remarks were not inflammatory, and that defendant failed to prove that his appellate counsel was ineffective.


OUTCOME: Convictions and sentence affirmed because defendant failed to prove that his trial counsel was ineffective, the prosecution's remarks were not inflammatory, and defendant failed to prove that his appellate counsel was ineffective.

 

370 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hall


Docket No. 86168


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


195 Ill. 2d 1; 743 N.E.2d 126; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1716; 252 Ill. Dec. 552



December 1, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 1, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5779.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), convicting him for murder and, following remand for a new sentencing hearing, sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in trial court for murder and sentenced to death. Following unsuccessful appeals, defendant was granted the habeas relief of a remand for a new sentencing hearing. The trial court again sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed, claiming that he was denied a fair capital sentencing hearing because plaintiff state introduced victim impact evidence from the victim of a prior crime, the trial court erroneously excluded several items of mitigation evidence, plaintiff's cross-examination of defense witnesses was improper, plaintiff's closing argument was inflammatory, the trial court's improperly injected a mercy explanation, the trial court refused to allow defendant to address the jury in allocution, and that the state death penalty statute was unconstitutional. The court affirmed, holding that defendant was not denied a fair capital sentencing hearing because the trial court's evidentiary rulings were proper, plaintiff's closing argument was not inflammatory, and the state death penalty statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Death sentence affirmed because defendant was not denied a fair capital sentencing hearing as the trial court's evidentiary rulings were proper, plaintiff state's closing argument was not inflammatory, and the state death penalty statute was not unconstitutional.

People v. Kirchner


Docket No. 86049


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


194 Ill. 2d 502; 743 N.E.2d 94; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1717; 252 Ill. Dec. 520



December 1, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied June 29, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5053.
Rehearing denied by People v. Kirchner, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 221 (Ill., Jan. 29, 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Kirchner v. Illinois, 533 U.S. 955, 121 S. Ct. 2603, 150 L. Ed. 2d 760, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5053 (2001)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by People v. Kirchner, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1414, 2012 IL App (4th) 100823-U (2012)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), convicting him for three counts of first degree murder and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in the trial court for three counts of first degree murder and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed, claiming that the trial court erred in failing to excuse certain jurors in voir dire, that the trial court erred in certain of its evidentiary rulings, and that the trial court's allowance of certain prosecutorial remarks and refusal of his requested jury instructions during his sentencing proceeding required vacation of his sentence and remand for a new hearing. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in failing to excuse certain jurors in voir dire, that the trial court's evidentiary rulings were not in error, and that the trial court's refusal to allow certain prosecutorial remarks and refusal of his requested jury instructions at defendant's sentencing hearing was not in error and did not require remand for a new hearing.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentence were affirmed because the trial court did not abuse its discretion in failing to excuse certain jurors in voir dire, the trial court's evidentiary rulings were not in error, and the trial court's allowance of certain prosecutorial remarks and refusal of defendant's requested jury instructions during his sentencing proceeding was not in error.

People v. Chapman


Docket No. 85332


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


194 Ill. 2d 186; 743 N.E.2d 48; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1719; 252 Ill. Dec. 474



December 1, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied June 29, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5071.
Rehearing denied by People v. Chapman, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 218 (Ill., Jan. 29, 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Chapman v. Illinois, 533 U.S. 956, 121 S. Ct. 2606, 150 L. Ed. 2d 762, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5071 (2001)
Post-conviction proceeding at People v. Chapman, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 5247 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 22, 2008)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Motion granted by People v. Chapman, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 270 (Ill., Mar. 9, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Chapman, 949 N.E.2d 660, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 635, 350 Ill. Dec. 868 (Ill., 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Chapman v. Hardy, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 77199 (N.D. Ill., June 1, 2012)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him based on a jury verdict of the first-degree murder of his ex-girlfriend and son and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of the first-degree murder of his ex-girlfriend and their five-month-old son after the bodies of the victims were found strangled and decomposed in a water channel. He was sentenced to death and appealed. The court affirmed, finding that it was not error to deny defendant's motion to suppress his confession. The confession was voluntary, and there was no deceitful conduct which prevented defendant from consulting with his attorney. Defendant was not entitled to the appointment of new counsel to represent him on his claim of ineffective assistance of trial counsel. The sentencing jury was sufficiently instructed on the mental state necessary for finding defendant eligible for the death penalty. It was not an abuse of discretion to deny defendant's request for a continuance of the second stage of the capital sentencing hearing. The introduction of a victim impact statement during that stage was not reversible error. The death penalty was an appropriate sentence for defendant. The court adhered to prior decisions finding the death penalty statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1 (West 1998), constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because it was not error to deny defendant's motion to suppress statements made to authorities and the death penalty was an appropriate sentence. The death penalty statute was not unconstitutional.

People v. Wiley


Docket No. 86557


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


2000 Ill. LEXIS 1697



November 16, 2000, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal, Circuit Court. COUNTY: Cook. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Lon William Shultz. CASE NUMBERS: TR85C14839.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), dismissing his post-conviction petition without an evidentiary hearing, following unsuccessful appeals from his convictions for first degree murder and armed robbery, and his sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in trial court for first degree murder and armed robbery, and sentenced to death. Following unsuccessful appeals, defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief. The trial court dismissed defendant's post-conviction petition without a hearing, stating both that the petition was untimely and that the petition was patently without merit. Defendant appealed, claiming that the petition was timely and that his appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to argue that the death eligibility finding was constitutionally deficient, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel at the death eligibility hearing, and that he was denied effective assistance of counsel at the aggravation and mitigation stage of his death penalty sentencing hearing. The court affirmed, holding that defendant failed to show that his appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to dispute his death penalty eligibility as constitutionally deficient or ineffective at the death eligibility hearing, and that defendant failed to identify any evidence that might have changed the trial court's ruling at the aggravation and mitigation stage of his death penalty sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: Convictions and death sentence affirmed because defendant failed to show that his appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to dispute his death penalty eligibility as constitutionally deficient or ineffective at the death eligibility hearing, and defendant failed to identify any evidence that might have changed the trial court's ruling at the aggravation and mitigation stage of his death penalty sentencing hearing.

 

374 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Casillas


Docket No. 83911


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


195 Ill. 2d 461; 749 N.E.2d 864; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1702; 255 Ill. Dec. 382



November 16, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied June 4, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Ill. LEXIS 495. Certiorari Denied November 26, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 10674.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal, Circuit Court. COUNTY: Cook. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Loretta H. Morgan. CASE NUMBERS: TR95CR23925, TR95CR32125.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction, by jury, of two counts of first degree murder, and death sentence for having committed two or more murders, by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), for the shooting deaths of jewelry store owners whose store was robbed.


OVERVIEW: Six years after a jewelry store was robbed and its two owners found shot to death, defendant, after being interviewed, admitted involvement and blamed his codefendant for the shootings. At his simultaneous severed trial, defendant testified differently: that his codefendant was responsible for the robbery and that defendant was involved out of fear. The jury did not receive Ill. Pattern Jury Instructions, Crim. No. 2.02 and 2.03 (3rd ed. 1992), on the presumption of innocence. Defendant was convicted of the murders and death-sentenced for having committed two. The court affirmed. The jury had been adequately instructed at length regarding the innocence presumption and need not have been questioned individually on their understanding. Counsel was not ineffective in that defendant was not prejudiced by the instructions' absence. Evidence was overwhelming concerning defendant's assistance in the crimes. Evidence of defendant's gang affiliation was used to rebut his implication that a state witness was not truthful. The trial court took steps to ensure defendant was not unduly prejudiced by mention of a prior conviction, and took two weeks to deliberate over his sentence.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Jury received adequate innocence-presumption instruction despite not getting statutory instructions and gang affiliation and prior conviction evidence was not unduly prejudicial to defendant. Trial court took all defendant's evidence into consideration in two-week deliberation over death sentence. Sentence was based on double murder and was constitutional.

Morris B. Chapman & Assocs. v. Kitzman


Docket No. 88393


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


193 Ill. 2d 560; 739 N.E.2d 1263; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1703; 251 Ill. Dec. 141



November 16, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Appellate Court, Fifth District. COUNTY: Madison. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Ann Callis. CASE NUMBERS: AC5-97-1005, TR93MR375.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant law firm appealed from the judgment of the appellate court (Illinois), denying appellant's motion to dismiss appellee law firm's action for attorney fees regarding an underlying wrongful death action.


OVERVIEW: Following a settlement in an underlying wrongful death action, appellee law firm brought an action for reasonable attorney fees against appellant law firm. The circuit court dismissed the action, but on appeal, the appellate court denied appellant's motion to dismiss, holding that appellee sufficiently stated a cause of action pursuant to the common fund doctrine. Appellant filed an appeal, claiming that full faith and credit and res judicata barred appellee's action, and that appellee's common fund doctrine claim could not have been used to obtain attorney fees in a wrongful death action. The court affirmed, holding that full faith and credit and res judicata did not bar appellee's action, and that appellee's complaint sufficiently stated a cause of action for reasonable attorney fees pursuant to the common fund doctrine.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because full faith and credit and res judicata did not bar appellee law firm's action, and appellee's complaint sufficiently stated a cause of action against appellant law firm for reasonable attorney fees pursuant to the common fund doctrine.

People v. Hall


Docket No. 86194


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


194 Ill. 2d 305; 743 N.E.2d 521; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1692; 252 Ill. Dec. 653



October 26, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 15, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 9779.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal, Circuit Court, Madison County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Charles V. Romani Jr. CASE NUMBERS: TR94CF1703.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's conviction and death penalty for two counts of first-degree murder went from the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) to the state supreme court on direct review under Ill. Const. art. VI, § 4(b) (1970), and Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 603, 609(a), 134 Ill. 2d. R. 603, 609(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of killing two young women with shotgun and semiautomatic weapons and leaving their bodies in a field. The State put on a strong circumstantial case which the defense rebutted aggressively but unsuccessfully. The evidence showed the victims were in a car defendant claimed the driver kept stealing from him, he threatened the driver with a shotgun within hours of the murders, he had a violent history, and one of the murder weapons was purchased by his wife and shipped to him. It also showed he wiped down the van rented the night of the murders and threw away a pair of boots to eliminate evidence. Premeditated double murder was sufficiently aggravating to warrant the death penalty. On direct review, defendant claimed violation of his speedy trial rights, insufficient evidence and erroneous evidentiary rulings, ineffective assistance of counsel, marital privilege, and cumulative error. He also challenged the death penalty statute. The court affirmed, finding there was no plain error and other errors were harmless. Counsel was not ineffective. Defendant was not prejudiced or denied a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The few errors committed in the trial and sentencing were harmless, because the result would have been the same. Defendant's speedy-trial motion did not present an issue of fact outside the record material to disposition of the motion. The evidence was sufficient. A rational trier of fact could have found defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The State presented a strong circumstantial case.

 

377 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Lulay v. Lulay


Docket Nos. 87874, 87896 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


193 Ill. 2d 455; 739 N.E.2d 521; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1694; 250 Ill. Dec. 758



October 26, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Appellate Court, Second District, DuPage County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Rodney W. Equi. CASE NUMBERS: AC2-99-0495, TR96D102.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents challenged the trial court's denial of their motion to dismiss, entered by the Circuit Court of DuPage County (Illinois), in a case where appellee grandmother filed a petition for visitation and appellants, who had divorced and had three minor children, opposed such visitation.


OVERVIEW: Appellee grandmother petitioned for visitation pursuant to 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/607(b)(1) (West 1998) with her grandchildren, the three children of appellant parents. Appellants who were divorced, shared joint custody and neither had been deemed unfit. They moved to dismiss the petition and argued the statute should not have been interpreted to allow a grandparent to sue for visitation. They also contended the statute as applied was an unconstitutional infringement on a fundamental liberty interest. The trial court denied the motion. Appellants' request for an interlocutory appeal was denied. The court granted permission to appeal. The court held the statute's plain language permitted a grandparent to seek such visitation. Even so, the court reversed the trial court's denial of appellants' motion to dismiss. It held under strict scrutiny analysis, applied because the fundamental right to raise children was involved, the statute was unconstitutional as the state had no compelling interest in forcing appellants, who had not been found to be unfit, to allow visitation they had decided they did not want for their minor children.


OUTCOME: Trial court's decision reversed and cause remanded with directions to it to dismiss appellee's petition because even though Illinois statutory law permitted a grandparent to file a visitation petition where the grandparent's own child objected to grandparent visitation, the statute as applied was an unconstitutional infringement on appellants' fundamental liberty interest in raising their children.

People v. Williams


Docket No. 85453


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


193 Ill. 2d 306; 739 N.E.2d 455; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1392; 250 Ill. Dec. 692



October 13, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied June 29, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5026.
Rehearing denied by, 11/27/2000
Writ of certiorari denied Williams v. Illinois, 533 U.S. 953, 121 S. Ct. 2599, 150 L. Ed. 2d 756, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5026 (2001)
Related proceeding at People v. Caffey, 205 Ill. 2d 52, 792 N.E.2d 1163, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1426, 275 Ill. Dec. 390 (2001)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court, DuPage County. CASE NUMBERS: TRCF2372.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant directly appealed her murder convictions for abetting in killings under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-2(c) (1994) and death sentence, following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), for the deaths of a mother and two of her children, involving also the kidnapping of two children.


OVERVIEW: For a few months defendant lied to others, including her probation officer, that she was pregnant, then she was arrested while holding the baby from a mother who had been killed and whose womb had been cut open a day earlier. Also slain were two of the mother's other children. Defendant, her boyfriend, and cousin were separately tried for murder and she was convicted and sentenced to death. The court affirmed. Evidence was overwhelming. Defendant admitted she had wanted a baby and that she was present at the killings. Defendant aided the principals under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-2(c) (1994) by conferring with them, getting a gun, and visiting the crime scene shortly before the murders. Testimony of a kidnapped later-murdered child's statements was admissible under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-10 (1994), and as spontaneous declarations because though a night had passed, he was still traumatized. As defendant was independently eligible for the death penalty for murdering a kidnapped child, jury consideration of allegedly invalid aggravators was harmless. Despite defendant's psychological vulnerability to predatory males, no evidence supported a compulsion mitigator.


OUTCOME: Conviction and death sentence were affirmed. Testimony of statements of kidnapped later-murdered child incriminating defendant was admissible under statute pertaining to physical acts against children, and as spontaneous declarations due to his trauma, although a night had passed. As defendant was independently eligible for death penalty for kidnap-murder aggravator, jury consideration of allegedly invalid aggravators was harmless.

People v. Wright


Docket No. 87116


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


194 Ill. 2d 1; 740 N.E.2d 755; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1234; 251 Ill. Dec. 469



October 2, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended on Denial of Rehearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of February 17, 2000, Previously Reported at: 2000 Ill. LEXIS 311.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the appellate court (Illinois) which vacated his convictions for possession of title without complete assignment and failure to keep records, but remanded the case for a limited non-evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: The State charged defendant salvage yard owner with two counts of possession of a stolen motor vehicle, in violation 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-103(a)(1) (West 1996); 27 counts of failure to keep records, in violation 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-401.2(a), (i) (West 1996); and 25 counts of possession of title without complete assignment 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/4-104(a)(2) (West 1996). The trial court found defendant not guilty of possession of stolen motor vehicles and not guilty of two counts of failure to keep records, but guilty on all remaining charges of failure to keep records and possession of title without complete assignment. The appellate court reversed and ordered the cause remanded for a limited non-evidentiary hearing. The court reversed and ordered the convictions vacated because there was insufficient evidence to support defendant's convictions for possession of title without complete assignment. Additionally, defendant's convictions for failure to keep records were unsupported because Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-401.2 was unconstitutional where it failed to provide reasonable means of preventing the trafficking of stolen vehicles and auto parts.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed. Defendant salvage yard owner's convictions were vacated. There was insufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction for possession of title without complete assignment and the statute imposing a penalty on defendant for failure to keep records was unconstitutional.

People v. Fair


Docket No. 84731


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


193 Ill. 2d 256; 738 N.E.2d 500; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1232; 250 Ill. Dec. 284



September 28, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended October 3, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal, Circuit Court, Cook County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Paul J. Nealis. CASE NUMBERS: TR87CR16691.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from a Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) order dismissing without evidentiary hearing his post-conviction petition based on the corruption of his trial and sentencing judge, alleging violations of his due process right to a fair trial.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of a double murder and sentenced to death. His conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. His petition for writ of certiorari was denied. Following his conviction, it was discovered that his trial and sentencing judge had engaged in extensive criminal conduct on the bench, including taking bribes for sentences. Petitioner filed a post-conviction petition, alleging the judge's massive corruption violated his right to a fair trial guaranteed by the due process clauses of the United States and Illinois Constitutions. The State's motion to dismiss the petition was granted without evidentiary hearing, because petitioner did not establish a nexus between the judge's criminal conduct and petitioner's murder trial. The court affirmed the constitutionality of the death penalty statute and held his ineffective assistance claims barred by res judicata, but reversed the denial of his discovery request for the judge's confession and related investigatory interviews, ordering production of the discovery and subsequent reconsideration of whether the judge's criminal conduct violated petitioner's due process right to a fair trial.


OUTCOME: Judgment dismissing post-conviction petition without evidentiary hearing was affirmed in part, but circuit court's denial of petitioner's discovery request for judge's confession and related witness interviews was reversed, with directions to order production of those materials and enter new ruling on due process issue.

People v. Malchow


Docket No. 88228


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


193 Ill. 2d 413; 739 N.E.2d 433; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1226; 250 Ill. Dec. 670



September 21, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Appellate Court, Second District, Lake County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. George Bridges. CASE NUMBERS: AC2-98-0576, TR97CF3372.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged Appellate Court (Illinois) affirmance of conviction for noncompliance with Illinois Sex Offender Registration Act, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/1 et seq. (West 1998), arguing unconstitutionality of that law and Illinois Sex Offender and Child Murderer Community Notification Law, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 152/101 et seq. (West 1998).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of failing to register in compliance with the Illinois Sex Offender Registration Act, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/1 et seq. (West 1998). Although that statute had already survived constitutional challenge, the court considered defendant's challenge to a related statute dealing with consequences of registration, the Illinois Sex Offender and Child Murderer Community Notification Law, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 152/101 et seq. The burden was on defendant to show unconstitutionality and he failed to carry it. His primary argument was that the statute violated the U.S. Const. art. I, §§ 9, 10 and Ill. Const. art. I, § 16 prohibitions against ex post facto laws. While the statute was clearly retroactive, the court found that its intent and effect were not primarily punitive, but protective of the public, as it was clearly tailored to provide only limited dissemination of information.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, because he failed to meet his burden to show the statutes' unconstitutionality. The registration statute had already been found constitutional, and once the court determined that the notification statute was not unduly punitive in intent or effect, all constitutional arguments collapsed.

 

382 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Parks v. Kownacki


Docket Nos. 87834, 87839 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


193 Ill. 2d 164; 737 N.E.2d 287; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1212; 249 Ill. Dec. 897



August 10, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Fifth District Appellate Court of St. Clair County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Lloyd A. Cueto. CASE NUMBERS: AC5-97-0900, TR95L308.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged a judgment of the Illinois Court of Appeals, which reversed a decision of the trial court and held that equitable estoppel precluded appellants from asserting a statute of limitations defense to appellee victim's claims of childhood sexual abuse by appellant priest and that appellee was under a legal disability.


OVERVIEW: Appellee victim sued appellant priest, appellant parish, and appellant diocese, alleging appellant priest had sexually abused her when she was a teenager and had intentionally inflicted upon her emotional distress. Appellee did not file her claims until over 20 years after the alleged physical abuse occurred. However, evidence revealed appellant priest had threatened appellee that the Roman Catholic Church would excommunicate her and her family if she revealed he had sexually assaulted her. The trial court granted appellants' motions to dismiss, finding appellee's claims were barred by the statute of repose for childhood sexual abuse claims. The lower appellate court reversed. Judgment was reversed. Appellee was aware as a teenager that appellant priest had done something wrong to her after the latter performed a forced abortion on appellee. Appellee's failure to understand the connection between the sexual abuse and other psychological injuries did not toll the statute of limitations. Appellee was not legally disabled for purposes of tolling the limitations period even though appellants' conduct may have rendered her "psychiatrically unable" to take legal action.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; appellee neither demonstrated that a legal disability tolled the two-year limitations period nor showed that equitable estoppel prevented appellants from raising the statute of limitations as a defense. As a result, appellee's claims based on her allegations of sexual abuse were time-barred.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Hancock County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Stephen G. Evans. CASE NUMBER: TR96CF46.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Hancock County (Illinois), rejecting defendant's insanity defense and rejecting defendant's argument that the insanity statute was unconstitutional, and the judgment finding defendant guilty of first degree murder, attempted first degree murder, aggravated criminal sexual assault, home invasion, and residential burglary.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed defendant's conviction because the insanity statute in effect when the crime occurred was unconstitutional. Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, attempted first degree murder, aggravated criminal sexual assault, home invasion, and residential burglary. Defendant pled insanity and appealed after a jury found him guilty. Defendant argued that the insanity statute was unconstitutional because it violated the one-subject rule. After the trial court denied defendant's constitutional argument, the state supreme court ruled the statute unconstitutional. Therefore, the court reversed defendant's conviction and ordered a new trial. The court held that the trial court could not have applied the new statute because such application would have violated the ex post facto clause of the U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, and Ill. Const. art. I, § 16. Therefore, defendant's conviction was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: Judgment rejecting defendant's insanity defense and rejecting defendant's argument that the insanity statute was unconstitutional was reversed because the statute was found unconstitutional in separate case. Therefore, the judgment finding defendant guilty of first degree murder, attempted first degree murder, aggravated criminal sexual assault, home invasion, and residential burglary was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of DuPage County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Ronald B. Mehling. CASE NUMBER: TR85CF707.

Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 et seq. (1994). Defendant also challenged constitutionality of the death penalty, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(g) (1985).


OVERVIEW: In 1985, defendant was convicted numerous crimes including murder, and at a separate hearing defendant was sentenced to death under Ill. Rev. Stat., ch. 38, para. 9-1(b)(6) (1985). Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by People v. Alvine, 409 Ill. App. 3d 1168, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1149, 377 Ill. Dec. 753, 2 N.E.3d 669 (2011)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at, Request granted People v. Alvine, 2015 IL App (2d) 130627-U, 2015 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 513 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of DuPage County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Ronald B. Mehling. CASE NUMBER: TR92CF937.

DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the trial court (Illinois), which sentenced defendant to death for felony murder without a sentencing hearing, following vacation and remand of defendant's conviction and death sentence for knowing murder, following defendant's convictions after striking and killing a police officer while attempting to steal a car.


OVERVIEW: Defendant struck and killed a police officer while attempting to steal a car, and was convicted of both knowing murder and felony murder and sentenced to death for knowing murder, but not sentenced on the felony-murder count. The court reversed defendant's knowing murder conviction, vacated defendant's death sentence, and remanded the cause to the trial court, and also held that defendant could have been sentenced on the felony murder count. On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, that he was entitled to a new sentencing hearing on remand. The court vacated defendant's death sentence. The trial court's sentencing of defendant without a hearing was contrary to the court's previous order. The court had vacated defendant's death sentence and instructed the trial court that defendant could have been sentenced on the felony-murder conviction for which he had not yet received a sentence. When the court remanded the case at that time, it clearly contemplated that defendant would have received the sentencing hearing to which he was entitled under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(d).


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's death sentence. The trial court's sentencing of defendant without a hearing was contrary to the court's previous order, which vacated defendant's previous death sentence, and contemplated that defendant would have received the sentencing hearing to which he was entitled under statute.

People v. Jung


Docket No. 86634


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


192 Ill. 2d 1; 733 N.E.2d 1256; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 982; 248 Ill. Dec. 258



July 6, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court. LaSalle County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. William Balestri. CASE NUMBERS: TR97DT135, TR97TR3687.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State sought interlocutory review of Circuit Court, LaSalle County's (Illinois) grant of drunk driving defendant's motion in limine to exclude blood alcohol results obtained while he was receiving emergency treatment, on grounds that 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501.4-1 (West 1996) violated defendant's Ill. Const. art. I, § 12 privacy rights.


OVERVIEW: Drunk driving defendant's blood alcohol test results, obtained while he was in the emergency room following an automobile accident, were turned over to law enforcement authorities pursuant to 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501.4-1 (West 1996). He sought exclusion, arguing that the statute violated his right of privacy guaranteed by Ill. Const. art. I, § 12. The court held the statute constitutional. Driving was not a right, but a privilege. In exchange for that privilege, defendant waived constitutional rights where reasonable to promote public safety. Defendant also challenged the statute for violating privacy rights when applied to pedestrians; the court held that he lacked standing because he was not a pedestrian. Finally, he challenged the statute as violating separation of powers, because the judiciary had exclusive control over discovery. The court held that permitting disclosure to law enforcement had nothing to do with control of discovery or separation of powers.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for further proceedings. The statutory waiver of privacy rights in exchange for driving privileges was reasonable and therefore constitutional. Defendant lacked standing to challenge law on behalf of non-drivers. Finally, permitting reporting of results to law enforcement did not violate separation of powers.

People v. McCallister

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed, on direct review, from circuit court of St. Clair County (Illinois) jury conviction and death sentence for three counts of first degree murder during drug transaction, with aggravating factors of murder during another felony and murder of two or more persons.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder for the shooting deaths of three people during a drug transaction in the victims' home. Pucinski v. County of Cook


Docket No. 88441


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


192 Ill. 2d 540; 737 N.E.2d 225; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 992; 249 Ill. Dec. 835



July 6, 2000, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner court clerk sought writ of mandamus to compel respondent county and treasurer to pay for computer and software purchased for her office. Respondents argued purchase's noncompliance with Illinois Counties Code, 55 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-1001 et seq. (West 1998) and Cook County, Ill. Ordinances ch. 10, §§ 17, 18.


OVERVIEW: After respondent county and official refused to approve purchase of a mainframe computer and software using monies of the Illinois Court Document Storage Fund, petitioner circuit court clerk arranged for the purchase herself and instituted a mandamus proceeding to compel respondents to pay for it. The court held that respondents were not required to pay for the purchase, because petitioner failed to comply with approval requirements of the Illinois Counties Code, 55 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-1001 et seq. (West 1998), and applicable county ordinances. The Illinois Clerks of Court Act did not empower clerks to authorize fund expenditures on their own, but only to approve purchases that were authorized under normal county procedures. This arrangement did not violate separation of powers principles, because in Illinois counties had many responsibilities for running and financial administration of courts. Because this provision did not infringe courts' inherent authority, it was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ, because the statute expressly denied petitioner authority to dictate how the disputed funds should have been spent, and subjected expenditures to approval by respondents. This provision did not violate separation of powers, because the activities in question derived not from courts' inherent authority, but from statutes.

People v. Nieves


Docket No. 84564


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


192 Ill. 2d 487; 737 N.E.2d 150; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 994; 249 Ill. Dec. 760



July 6, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court. Cook County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Themis N. Karnezis. CASE NUMBERS: TR96CR2726.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment, entered in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of first degree murder, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(1) (1992), and sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, defendant argued that he received ineffective assistance of counsel when his attorney presented a mercy killing defense, the trial court erred in allowing the State to introduce hearsay evidence at defendant's sentencing hearing, and the trial court improperly denied defendant's request to make a statement in allocution. The court affirmed the judgment, noting that it could not have found defendant received ineffective assistance of counsel. Defendant had shown neither that his attorney's performance fell below an objective standard of reasonableness nor that a reasonable probability existed that, had his attorney pursued another line of defense, the result of the proceeding would have been different. Additionally, the court determined the issue of hearsay evidence was waived because defendant failed to object when the evidence was introduced. Finally, the court rejected defendant's allocution argument because defendant had neither a statutory nor a constitutional right to make a statement in allocution in capital sentencing hearings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment because defendant had shown neither that his attorney's performance fell below an objective standard of reasonableness nor that a reasonable probability existed that, had his attorney pursued another line of defense, the result of the proceeding would have been different. Further, defendant did not object to the introduction of the challenged hearsay evidence; thus, the issue was waived on appeal.

People v. Williams


Docket No. 82807


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


193 Ill. 2d 1; 737 N.E.2d 230; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 984; 249 Ill. Dec. 840



July 6, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 23, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 3263.
Rehearing denied by People v. Williams, 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1246 (Ill., Oct. 2, 2000)
Writ of certiorari denied Williams v. Illinois, 532 U.S. 996, 121 S. Ct. 1657, 149 L. Ed. 2d 640, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 3263 (2001)
Subsequent appeal at People v. Williams, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 373 (2011)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Williams, 2014 IL App (5th) 120385-U, 2014 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2044 (2014)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Williams v. Butler, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 64702 (S.D. Ill., May 18, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court. St. Clair County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Richard A. Aguirre. CASE NUMBERS: TR96CF100.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; death sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the circuit court of St. Clair County (Illinois) which convicted him of first degree murder and sentenced him to because the jury found, under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(b)(11), 5/9-1(b)(6) (West 1994), that there were no factors sufficient to preclude imposition of the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. Defendant robbed a store and shot the clerk. The court affirmed the conviction, finding sufficient evidence for a jury to convict. The trial court properly excluded testimony of a witness as not against his penal interest. The court reversed the death penalty and remanded for new sentencing. On the record, no reasonable trier of fact could have found murder was committed by the death sentence statutory requirement of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(b)(11) (1994) "in a cold, calculated, and premeditated manner pursuant to a preconceived plan, scheme, or design." The murder and robbery took place in less than a minute. Time for reflection was a requirement of that statute. Jury verdict did not contain requisite mens rea finding for felony-murder statutory aggravating factor under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(b)(6) (1994). The court could not usurp the jury's sentencing function since defendant had elected for jury to sentence. Death penalty could only be reconsidered under felony-murder, since error based upon flawed verdict form, and not under the premeditated factor, because that would violate double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed, but the sentence was vacated and remanded for new sentencing. No reasonable trier of fact could have found the murder was committed within the statutory requirements for premeditation. Because the jury verdict did not contain requisite mens rea finding for felony-murder aggravating factor, the court ordered reconsideration of that factor.

Mich. Ave. Nat'l Bank v. County of Cook


Docket No. 88286


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


191 Ill. 2d 493; 732 N.E.2d 528; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 825; 247 Ill. Dec. 473



June 15, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Appellate Court, First District. Cook County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Sophia H. Hall. CASE NUMBERS: AC1-98-1974, TR93L15751.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a wrongful death and medical negligence action, plaintiff appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court, First District, Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed the judgment of the trial court entering summary judgment for defendants.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a medical malpractice action against defendants alleging that decedent died as a proximate cause of defendants' negligence. Defendants filed a motion for summary judgment, contending they were immune from liability under the Local Government and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/1-101 et seq. (1992). The trial court granted summary judgment. The court affirmed, noting that because the gravamen of plaintiff's action against defendants was that defendants' failure either to perform examinations or to adequately perform examinations led to defendants' failure to diagnose decedent's breast cancer, which, in turn, proximately caused her death, the immunity provided to local public entities and their public employees in 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/6-105, -106, applied. Specifically, the court determined that § 6-105 immunity applied to defendants' alleged failure to conduct physical examinations. In addition, § 6-106 immunity applied because of defendants' failure to diagnose breast cancer when defendants rendered no medical treatment to decedent in relation to her breast condition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment because defendants were immunized from liability pursuant to the Local Government and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act. Therefore, summary judgment was appropriately granted.

People v. Jones


Docket No. 83756


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


191 Ill. 2d 354; 732 N.E.2d 573; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 826; 247 Ill. Dec. 518



June 15, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied January 8, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 283.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court. St. Clair County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Richard A. Aguirre. CASE NUMBERS: TR79CF285.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, previously sentenced to death after conviction upon guilty plea of three counts of first-degree murder, appealed an order of the Circuit Court, St. Clair County (Illinois), dismissing without hearing his third petition for post-conviction relief, in which he claimed ineffective assistance of trial counsel.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, on death row in Illinois, had twice petitioned unsuccessfully for post-conviction relief and also unsuccessfully petitioned for writ of habeas corpus. The court held that under the Illinois Post-Conviction Hearing Act, a criminal defendant faced severe procedural bars to any petition after the first. Petitioner had to show good cause, an objective factor external to the defense that impeded earlier efforts, for failure to raise claims in prior proceedings and actual prejudice, meaning an error that so infected the trial that conviction violated due process, resulting from claimed errors. This petitioner failed to show actual prejudice. Petitioner claimed that counsel was ineffective based on counsel's failure to request a hearing on fitness for trial due to ingestion of psychotropic drugs. Since by Illinois law psychotropic drugs were not a basis for claiming unfitness for trial, petitioner was not prejudiced by failure to hold a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed denial, because petitioner failed to establish the prejudice prong of the cause and prejudice test required to be met before a court could consider a post-conviction petition after denial of the first one.

People v. Sims


Docket No. 84686


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


192 Ill. 2d 592; 736 N.E.2d 1048; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 827; 249 Ill. Dec. 610



June 15, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied February 26, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 1784.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court. St. Clair County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Robert P. LeChien. CASE NUMBERS: TR94CF899.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and death sentence by the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) for first-degree murder, attempted first degree murder, and armed robbery. The appeal was based upon denial of motions to suppress his statements made after his alleged arrest without probable cause, to not have indictment read to jury, and to limit cross examination of a State witness, wrongful dismissal of a juror, and ineffective counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, attempted first degree murder, and armed robbery, based upon his 1994 actions in a robbery causing the death of a young woman and the injury of her husband. Upon appeal the court affirmed the circuit court's convictions and death sentence. The court found probable cause at time of the warrantless arrest based upon the totality of the circumstances which included an informant's lead based on more than casual rumor. Defendant also had given a false name to officers. Therefore his post-Miranda statements were admissible. Indictment reading to jury at fitness hearing was not prejudicial as it did not relate details of the attack and instructions limiting issues to fitness were given to the jury. State lab witness properly not cross-examined on theft of a microscope as the relevance of that issue to his fabrication of evidence was remote and uncertain. Not error to dismiss juror for cause for religious beliefs against death penalty. Judge's and prosecutor's comments to jury were not reversible error. Under Strickland counsel not ineffective for withholding a witness for strategic reasons. Death penalty was reaffirmed as constitutional.


OUTCOME: Conviction and death sentence judgment affirmed. There was probable cause to make a warrantless arrest based upon totality of circumstances, which included an informant's lead based upon more than casual rumor. Indictment reading to fitness jury was not prejudicial. Lab expert cross-examination properly limited. Juror properly dismissed for death penalty religious beliefs. Counsel not ineffective for withholding witness for strategic reasons.

People v. Montgomery


Docket No. 82527


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


192 Ill. 2d 642; 736 N.E.2d 1025; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 828; 249 Ill. Dec. 587



June 15, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied June 4, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 4195.
Rehearing denied by People v. Montgomery, 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1240 (Ill., Oct. 2, 2000)
Writ of certiorari denied Montgomery v. Illinois, 532 U.S. 1068, 150 L. Ed. 2d 213, 121 S. Ct. 2221, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 4195 (2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied United States ex rel. Montgomery v. McAdory, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 16049 (N.D. Ill., Sept. 8, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court. Cook County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Michael R. Weber. CASE NUMBERS: TRPC5019.
People v. Montgomery, 162 Ill. 2d 109, 642 N.E.2d 1260, 1994 Ill. LEXIS 148 (1994)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denying him post-conviction relief following his conviction and sentence to death for the rape and murder of two women.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced to death for the rape and murder of two women. The court affirmed the order of the circuit court which denied him post-conviction relief. The circuit's court's determinations following its evidentiary hearing were not to be disturbed unless manifestly erroneous. Evidence supported that court's finding that the trial judge did not indicate in ex parte discussions that he would not impose the death sentence if defendant pled guilty. The trial had proceeded as a stipulated bench trial. Evidence had also supported that court's finding that there had not been ineffective trial, post-conviction relief, or appellate counsel, in the waiver of jury trial for guilt or sentencing, and in the presentation of mitigating evidence in the sentencing phase, and for strategic choices. The court stated that the additional evidence of defendant's troubled family and youth was not inherently mitigating, could be construed as aggravating, and was corroborative of other evidence. Lack of evidence at sentencing was not prejudicial where the outcome would probably have been the same, so the court concluded counsel was not ineffective for not presenting it.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed. Circuit court decisions following its evidentiary hearing were not manifestly erroneous. The decisions included that the trial judge did not agree in ex parte discussions with defense counsel to not impose the death penalty if defendant pled guilty and waived a jury trial, that not presenting more evidence of defendant's troubled youth was not prejudicial, and that counsel was not ineffective for strategic decisions.

 

397 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Maness


Docket No. 86463


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


191 Ill. 2d 478; 732 N.E.2d 545; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 831; 247 Ill. Dec. 490



June 15, 2000, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal, Circuit Court. Randolph County. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. John M. Goodwin, Jr. CASE NUMBERS: TR997CF207.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Randolph County (Illinois), which granted appellee's motion to dismiss the charge of permitting the sexual abuse of a child, a violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/5.1 (West 1992), because the statute was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: After appellee was charged with the offense of permitting the sexual abuse of a child, she filed a motion to dismiss, arguing that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/5.1 (West 1992), was unconstitutionally vague as to what constituted "reasonable steps" to prevent the commission of future acts of sexual abuse. The motion was granted and appellant state appealed. The supreme court affirmed the circuit court's order dismissing the charge against appellee, holding that the statute was unconstitutionally vague because it was not clear what the "reasonable steps" were that a parent must take in order to avoid criminal prosecution under the statute. Specifically, the court found that the statute left a parent to speculate as to what the statute commanded and that it was unclear what a parent must do to take "reasonable steps" under the statute, and that authorities remained without standards to guide their enforcement of the statute.


OUTCOME: Dismissal affirmed; the statute was unconstitutionally vague because it was not clear what the "reasonable steps" were that a parent was required to take in order to avoid criminal prosecution under the statute.

 

398 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Williams


Docket No. 85625


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


192 Ill. 2d 548; 736 N.E.2d 1001; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 666; 249 Ill. Dec. 563



May 25, 2000, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of first degree murder, aggravated kidnapping, and armed robbery, and received the death penalty, the jury finding no sufficient mitigating factors. Defendant's death sentence was stayed pending direct review by the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of first degree murder, aggravated kidnapping, and armed robbery, and sentenced him to death, after considering aggravation and mitigation testimony. On direct review, the supreme court affirmed. Defendant killed a 19-year-old girl after instigating a savage beating and rape when she stole $ 50 cocaine. Four eyewitnesses testified against defendant. Defendant put the victim in the trunk of her own car with a pillowcase over her head and drove off with a shotgun. The victim was found dead in an empty lot from a shotgun wound to the head, still wearing the pillowcase. The court found defendant's ineffective assistance of trial counsel and improper evidentiary rulings and closing arguments had been waived and were not subject to plain error, and his disparate sentence was not inappropriate as codefendant was not similarly situated.


OUTCOME: Conviction and death penalty were affirmed, as court found no plain error excusing any of defendant's procedural defaults, and would not address issues waived by defendant. Sentence disparity with co-defendant's sentence was not improper as co-defendant was not similarly situated or culpable.

 

399 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Easley


Docket No. 84418


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


192 Ill. 2d 307; 736 N.E.2d 975; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 667; 249 Ill. Dec. 537



May 25, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Easley, 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1241 (Ill., Oct. 2, 2000)
Writ of habeas corpus denied United States ex rel. Easley v. Hinsley, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 2896 (N.D. Ill., Feb. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Easley, 148 Ill. 2d 281, 592 N.E.2d 1036, 1992 Ill. LEXIS 72, 170 Ill. Dec. 356 (1992)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the dismissal of his petition for post-conviction relief by the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois) after his conviction and death sentence by the same court for the gang-related conspiracy to murder and the actual murder of a superintendent of the prison where defendant was serving a sentence for another murder.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was in prison for murder, he and another inmate murdered a prison superintendent, following prison gang instructions. Defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed the dismissal of his motion for postconviction relief under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act. 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1. The court affirmed the dismissal. The death sentence was not unreasonably disparate. The other murderer was sentenced to death, and the gang members who ordered the murder were sentenced to life. The sentence was not arbitrary or capricious. Under the Strickland analysis defendant received effective assistance of trial and appellate counsel. Constitutional ineffective assistance claims were not to be another way of rearguing issues previously addressed. Defendant was not unfit for trial because he was mentally unsound, unwilling to cooperate with counsel, or suicidal. The State had race neutral reasons for excluding venireman after Batson challenge including that he lived in a gang area. Defendant's prior murder conviction and prison conduct were relevant aggravators as was the cold-blooded and calculated assassination of a prison official.


OUTCOME: The dismissal was affirmed. Strickland test applied to determine defendant did not receive ineffective assistance of trial or appellate counsel. Defendant could not raise indirectly through ineffective assistance claim those objections that should have been made at trial or on direct appeal. Sentence was not unreasonably disparate.

 

400 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Segers v. Indus. Comm'n


Docket No. 87816


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


191 Ill. 2d 421; 732 N.E.2d 488; 2000 Ill. LEXIS 650; 247 Ill. Dec. 433



May 18, 2000, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed from the order of the appellate court (Illinois), which reversed the order of the trial court granting defendant employer's motion for summary judgment in plaintiff's action for declaratory relief seeking a declaration that the Workers' Occupational Diseases Act, 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 310/9 (West 1998), did not bar her claim for death benefits, or that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff's husband settled a disability claim against defendant employer under the Workers' Compensation Act and the Worker's Occupational Diseases Act. After plaintiff's husband died, plaintiff filed an action for declaratory relief, which sought a declaration that the Workers' Occupational Diseases Act, 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 310/9 (West 1998), did not bar her claim for death benefits, or that the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment, and plaintiff appealed. The intermediate appellate court reversed, and defendant appealed. Judgment was reversed because the settlement agreement was the compromise of a dispute on questions in addition to the extent of disability and the statute barred plaintiff's claim for death benefits; plaintiff failed to meet the burden of establishing that the statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Denial of defendant employer's motion for summary judgment was reversed because the settlement agreement was the compromise of a dispute on questions in addition to the extent of disability, therefore the statute barred plaintiff's claim for death benefits, and plaintiff failed to meet the burden of establishing that the statute was unconstitutional.
